Dalalat al-Nass: Definition and Application
Defines dalalat al-nass and illustrates with Quranic verse and kaffarah rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dalalat al-nass, identify its operation in Quranic texts, and apply it to derive rulings in new cases.

Core Idea
Dalalat al-nass derives rulings from the implied cause, not explicit words, and is stronger than qiyas.

In Hanafi legal theory, not all rulings come from the explicit wording of the text. Some are derived through the implied meaning known as dalalat al-nass. This lesson defines this concept and demonstrates its application through three key examples: the prohibition of harming parents, the obligation of kaffarah for women, and the extension of kaffarah to eating and drinking in Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Define dalalat al-nass
Understand that it is the ruling derived from the cause ('illah) understood from the text, not the explicit wording. It is also called mafhum al-khitab.
The term appears in the text as 'محوسیٰ خطاب' which likely means 'مفهوم خطاب'.
2
Analyze the first example: prohibition of 'uff'
The text 'Do not say uff' explicitly prohibits a minor harm. The cause is causing harm to parents. Since hitting is a greater harm, it is prohibited by dalalat al-nass (priority reasoning).
Note the cause is directly understood from the prohibition.
3
Analyze the second example: woman's kaffarah
The explicit text obliges kaffarah on a man who has intercourse during Ramadan fast. The cause is transgression against the fast. Since the woman also transgresses, she is obliged by dalalat al-nass.
The commentator stresses this is dalalat, not qiyas.
4
Analyze the third example: eating and drinking
The cause of transgression also applies to eating and drinking, and more intensely, so kaffarah is wajib by priority (awlā) via dalalat al-nass.
This illustrates awlawiyya (priority) within dalalat al-nass.

واما دلالة النص ولالۃ النص منطوق کلام نہیں ہوتا اور اس کا نام محوسیٰ خطاب رکھا گیا ہے جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فلا تقل لهما اف یہ حرمہ ضرب پر دال ہے لیکن یہ مراد منطوق کلام نہیں ہے بلکہ اس نہی سے جو علہ مفہوم ہوتی ہے وہ در حقیقت ازلی ہے یعنی والدین کے ساتھ ایسا سلوک کرنا حرام ہے جوان کے لئے باعث تکلیف و ایزا ہو اور تافیف اسی وجہ سے حرام ہے اور یہ ایزا نسبت تالیف کے ضرب میں زیادہ ہے لہذا وہ بطریق اولی حرام ہوگی یہ ہے دلالۃ النص جو نحوی کلام سے اخذ ہوتی ہے ۔ وکالكفارة بالوقاع وجبت عليه نصا بحاله صوم جماع کرنے کے ساتھ مرد پر کفارہ خود نص سے واجب ہے لیکن عورت پر دلالتہ کیونکہ جو معنی یعنی جو سبب موجب کفارہ ہے وہ ہے جنایتہ علی الصوم اور یہ مشترک ہے عورت اور مرد کے درمیان اگرچہ عورت کے حق میں نص صریح تو نہیں ہے لیکن دلالہ واجب ہو جائیگا۔ وکوجوب الكفارة عندنا في الاكل والشرب اگر صائم في رمضان اپنا روزہ محمد ا کھانے پینے کے ساتھ فاسد کر دے تو عند الاحناف کفارہ واجب ہو جاتا ہے یہ وجوب بھی دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہے نص تو وارد ہوئی ہے جماع میں لیکن جو معنی اور علتہ موجب کفارہ وقاع میں مفہوم ہوتا ہے وہ ہے کونه جناية على الصوم فانه چونکہ صوم امساک عن المفطرات الثلث [صوم امساک عن المفطرات الثلث: اکل شرب جماع] کو کہتے ہیں اجماع - اکل - شرب سے رکنے اور بند رہنے کا نام صوم ہے۔ جب اس شخص نے جماع کیا تو منظر صوم سے امساک اس نے ترک کر دیا ہے یہ ہے جنایتہ افساد علی الصوم في رمضان جو موجب كفارة ہے صورۃ جماع میں اور یہی جنایتہ اکل اور شرب میں بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ اس میں افساد صوم رمضان فی رمضان کی جنایتہ موجود لہذا اکل و شرب میں بھی کفارہ لازم بلکہ بطریق اولی لازم ہے ۔ لات الصبر عندھا کیونکہ شدہ جوع میں صبر عن الطعام اور شدہ عطش میں صبر عن الماء اشد اور اصعب ہے۔ نسبت صبر عن الجماع عند الشهوة سے کیونکہ اکل و شرب سے صبر کرنا قلیل الوقوع ہے اور کھانے پینے میں رغبتہ کثیرۃ اور شوق قومی موجود ہوتا ہے علی الخصوص نہار میں کیونکہ نفس کو کھانے پینے کے ساتھ الفت ہے اور ان کی طرف فرط حاجتہ ہے اور جماع میں یہ وجوہات موجود نہیں ہیں لہذا جب بنسبت جماع کے صبر عن الاكل والشرب کچھ مشکل ہے تو لائق ہے کہ اس کے اندر زاجر ضرور ہونا چاہئے تاکہ رکاوٹ قومی ہو جائے اگر اس میں زراجہ نہ ہو تو پھر بھوک و پیاس کے وقت وہ صوم بلا خطر فاسد کر دے گا سوچیگا کہ صرف یوم بیوم ہوگا یہ کوئی کیڑی بات نہیں لہذا فی الحال تو شدہ جوع اور شدۃ عطش رفع کرلوں تو جب اس کے اندر کفارہ والی زجر موجود ہوگی تو ڈر کے مارے بھوک اور پیاس کی شدۃ برداشت کرے گا۔ افساد صوم کا خیال تک بھی نہیں کرے گا لہذا اکل و شرب میں کفارہ بطریق اولی دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ واجب ہے قیاس کے ساتھ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اعتراض نہیں ہوگا کہ قیاس کے ساتھ حدود و کفارات ثابت نہیں ہو سکتے.
As for dalalat al-nass: it is not the explicit wording (mantuq) of the speech, and it is named mafhum al-khitab. Like Allah's saying: 'Do not say to them 'uff'' (17:23), this indicates the prohibition of hitting, but it is not the intended explicit wording; rather, from this prohibition, the understood cause is essentially that it is forbidden to treat parents in a way that causes them hardship and harm. 'Uff' is forbidden for this reason, and this harm is less than hitting, so hitting is forbidden by even stronger priority. This is dalalat al-nass, derived from the conceptual implication of the speech. And like the expiation for intercourse: it is wajib upon the man by explicit text (nass) in his case. For the woman, it is wajib by dalalat, because the meaning – the cause that necessitates expiation – is transgressing against the fast, and this is shared between man and woman. Even though there is no explicit text for the woman, it becomes wajib by dalalat. And like the obligation of expiation according to us (Hanafis) for eating and drinking: if a fasting person in Ramadan invalidates his fast by eating and drinking, then according to the Hanafis expiation becomes wajib. This obligation is also established by dalalat al-nass. The text (nass) is reported about intercourse, but the meaning and cause understood in intercourse is that it is a transgression against the fast. Since fasting means abstaining from the three nullifiers (eating, drinking, intercourse). When the person had intercourse, he abandoned the abstinence that is the essence of fasting. This is the transgression of corrupting the fast in Ramadan, which is the cause of expiation in the case of intercourse. And this same transgression exists in eating and drinking, because the transgression of corrupting the fast of Ramadan in Ramadan exists. Therefore, expiation becomes necessary in eating and drinking as well – indeed, by even stronger priority. Because the difficulty of abstinence from food and drink is greater: patience with food in extreme hunger and patience with water in extreme thirst is more severe and harder compared to patience with intercourse when desire is present. This is because abstaining from eating and drinking is rare, and desire and strong inclination for them abound, especially during daytime, since the soul is accustomed to eating and drinking and has extreme need for them. These factors are not present in intercourse. Therefore, since abstaining from eating and drinking is harder than abstaining from intercourse, it is fitting that a deterrent (zajir) should exist in it to provide a strong obstacle. If there were no deterrent, then at the time of hunger and thirst he would break the fast without fear, thinking it is only a temporary matter. So if he raises severe hunger and thirst immediately, then when the deterrent of expiation exists, he will bear the severity of hunger and thirst out of fear and will not even think of corrupting the fast. Hence, in eating and drinking, expiation is wajib by dalalat al-nass by way of priority (awlā), not by qiyas. Therefore, the objection that hadd and kaffarah cannot be established by qiyas does not arise.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed exposition of dalalat al-nass (indication of the text), a Hanafi usul concept distinct from the explicit wording (mantuq). The commentator defines it as the ruling derived from the cause or reason (‘illah) understood from the text, even though the text does not explicitly mention the case. Three examples are given: (1) The Quranic verse 'Do not say uff' to parents – the cause is causing harm, so hitting is prohibited by stronger priority. (2) Kaffarah for intercourse – the text explicitly requires it for the man; the woman is included by dalalat because the cause (transgression against the fast) is shared. (3) Kaffarah for eating and drinking – though the text only mentions intercourse, the same cause exists more intensely, so expiation is wajib by dalalat bi al-awlā (priority reasoning). This demonstrates that dalalat al-nass is a valid source of law in the Hanafi school, even for punishments (kaffarat), which cannot be established by qiyas.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): The indication of the text derived from the cause ('illah) or implied meaning, not the explicit wording.
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit wording of the text that directly yields a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does the woman also become liable for kaffarah for intercourse during the fast, even though the text only mentions the man?
A) By qiyas because the act is similar
B) By dalalat al-nass because the cause (transgression against the fast) is shared
C) By consensus of the companions
D) By necessity of the situation

Key Takeaway
Dalalat al-nass derives rulings from the text's implied cause, providing a stronger basis than qiyas and applicable even in areas like kaffarah.

Dalaalat al-Nass in Qisas: Defining the 'Illah
Explaining the Hanafi critique of dalaalat al-nass in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of dalaalat al-nass by distinguishing between the 'illah definitions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn for qisas.

Core Idea
Dalaalat al-nass extends a ruling only when the effective cause is exactly the same as in the original text.

This lesson unpacks how the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use dalaalat al-nass to extend qisas from a sword to a blunt object, and why Abu Hanifa rejects that extension by refining the 'illah. You will learn that the same textual indication can lead to different rulings depending on how precisely the 'illah is defined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its 'illah
Find the original case (striking with a sword) and the ruling (qisas wajib). Then extract the 'illah as understood by each party.
The text states that the Sahibayn identify the 'illah as 'striking with something the body cannot bear'. Abu Hanifa identifies it as 'a crime that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly'.
2
Apply dalaalat al-nass to the new case
Check whether the 'illah of the original case is equally present in the new case (blunt object). For the Sahibayn it is; for Abu Hanifa it is not (blunt object demolishes only inwardly).
This step shows that even with the same text, the scope of extension changes with the definition of the 'illah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's 'illah: it requires demolishing both outwardly and inwardly. Blunt objects demolish only inwardly, so the 'illah is not met and qisas does not apply.
The distinction between outward and inward demolition is key to Hanafi precision in causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے مقتول کو تلوار کے ساتھ قتل کیا ہو ۔ صاحبین اسی ثانی معنی کے لحاظ سے استدلال بدلالۃ النص کرتے ہیں حاصل استدلال یہ ہے کہ خان المعنى الذى منصوص ہیں جو معنی علت حکم ہے اس کو جاری کرنے کی کوشش ہے تاکہ یہ دلالتہ النص میں درج ہو جائے یعنی وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے کہ وہ موجب ہے جزا کامل کا اس بارہ میں کہ جب حرمہ نفس تباہ کی جائے تو وہ معنی ضرب ہے ایسی شئی کے ساتھ کہ جسم و بدن اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ يفهم موجبا لفظ موجبا ترکیب میں ضمیر نیفہیم سے حال ہے مفہوم یہ ہوگا کہ وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ موجب ہے للجزاء جزاء كامل كا عن انتهاك حرمة النفس يه جار مجرور لفظ الجزاء کے ساتھ متعلق ہے یعنی حرمتہ نفس کی انتہاک پر جزاء کا موجب جو معنی سمجھ آتا ہے اور الانتهاك افتعال کا باب ہے ان تھک لفظ نون اس کا فاکلمہ ہے دھو القطع اس کا معنی ہے قطع کرنا اور کاٹ دینا بولتے ہیں سیف نھیک ای قاطع انتھاک کا معنی فارسی میں حرمت کسی شکستن یعنی کسی نفس کی حرمہ کو توڑنا اور کاٹنا ایسے طریق پر کہ وہ حلال نہیں۔ الضرب یہ خبر ہے ان کی جو مذکو رہے فی قولہ فان المعنی یعنی وہ معنی جو موجب ہے جزاء کا وہ ہے الضرب بما لا يطيقه البدن اور یہ معنی جیسے ضرب بالسیف میں موجود ہے اسی طرح ضرب بالمثقل میں بھی موجود ہے تو دلالہ یہ ضرب بالمثقل موجب قصاص ہوگی۔
وقال البوحنیفہ المعنی امام فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ معنی جو منصوص میں موجب قصاص ہے وہ ہے جرم ينقض البنية ظاهر و باطنا یعنی ایسا خم جو نبیہ انسانی کی ظاہر و باطنا نقض کرے اور توڑ دے ظاہرا یوں کہ جسم میں زخم ہو جاتے اور جستہ کی تخریب ہو اور باطنا یوں کہ از باق اور اخراج نفس حیوانیہ کا ہو جاتے جس کے ساتھ حس و حرکۃ وابستہ ہے نانه حينئدة تقع الجناية قصداً على النفس الحيوانية قصدا کے ساتھ قتل خطا کا اخراج کیا کہ وہ قصداً نہیں اور نقض بنیہ ظاہر و باطنا کے ساتھ اس جرح سے احتراز کیا جو سرایتہ نہ کرے اور موت تک نہ پہونچاتے کیونکہ یہ نقص بنیہ صرف فاصل کرتا ہے باطنا نہیں کرتا اور ضرب بالمثقل سے بھی احتراز کیا کیونکہ وہ نقض بنسیہ صرف باطنا کرتا ہے کہ از ہاق روح تو ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ظاہر وہ نقض نہیں کرتا۔ لہذا جرح جو نقص بنیہ ظاہر او باطنا کرے اور ہو بالعمد یہ اکمل الجنایتہ ہے لہذا جزاء اکمل یعنی قصاص اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہونا چاہیے۔ وکوجوب الكفارة عند الشافعی امام شافعی کے نزدیک قتل عمد میں کفارہ قتل اور سیمین غموس میں کفارہ ہمین واجب ہے اور اس کا وجوب بدلالة النص وہ ثابت کرتے ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ جب قتل خطا میں نص وارد ہے ومن قتل مؤمناً أخطاء فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة تو اس نص کی دلالہ سے محتل محمد میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور سیمین منعقدہ میں کفارہ نص کے ساتھ ثابت ہے ولكن يواخذكم بما عقد تم الايمان فكفارته الایتہ تو اس نص کی دلالت سے یمین غموس میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ لانه لما وجب یہ دلیل ہے اثبات كفارة بدلالۃ النص کی حاصل یہ کہ جب قتل خطامہ میں کفارہ واجب ہے باوجود یکہ یہ قائل معنو ہے اس نے رمی الی الصید کی ہے یار می الی کا فر حربی کی ہے غلطی سے مسلم کو لگ گئی تو اس عذر - با وجود جب کفارہ واجب ہے تو قتل عمد میں بطریق اولی واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ یہ قتل بدون العز اور اسی طرح کفارہ یمین معقودہ میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جب ۔ اس یمین میں حنت و کذب ثابت ہوگا تو یمین غموس جونی الاصل وفی الحال کا ذب ہے تو اس میں بطریق اولیٰ کفارہ واجب ہونا چاہیئے۔ یہ ہے امام شافعی کا طریق استدلال لکھنا نقول سے اس کا جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ کفارہ ایک قسم کی عبادۃ ہے اس کا ثواب جبراً لما ارتكب یعنی جس جرم کا ارتکاب ہوا ہے یہ ثواب اس کا جبر نقصان کر دیتا ہے اور وہ جرم مٹ جاتا ہے فلهذا چونکہ اس کے اندر معنی عبادہ ہے تو اسی لحاظ سے اس کی ادائیگی بالصوم ہو جاتی ہے فیھا معنی العقویۃ اور کفارہ میں معنی عقوقیہ وسزا بھی موجود ہے ۔ فانها جزاء یہ ایک ایسی جزاء ہے جو ارتکاب جرم سے زجر و منع کرتی ہے تو گویا کفارہ ذی جہتیں ہوا من جهة عبادة من جهة عقوبته يجب ان يكون سببها دائرا بين المحظر والاباحة تو واجب ہے کہ کفارہ کا سبب ایسا فعل ہو جو دائر بین الحظر والاباحہ ہو یعنی بین المنع والجواز تا کہ ممنوع ہونیکی وجہ سے وہ سبب عقوبت بنے گا اور جواز کی وجہ سے وہ سبب عبادہ ہوگا كقتل الخطاء جیسے قتل خطا کے اندر رمی الی الصید والكافر الحربی ہونیکی بنا پر مباح ہے اور بوجہ ترک تثبت اور قتل الانسان المعصوم کے لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے اور اسی طرح یمین معقودہ بائیں جہتہ مباح ہے یہ ایک ایسا عقد ہے جو شریعت کی نگاہ میں فصل خصومات کی خاطر مشروع ہے وفیھا تعظیم اسم اللہ تعالیٰ اور بائیں جہتہ کہ اس میں حنث و کذب ہو تو اس لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے تو اس لحاظ سے یہ دونوں جرم یعنی قتل خطا اور یمین معقودہ گناہ صغیرہ ہوے فاما الحمد والغموس قتل عمد اور يمين غموس فكبيرة محضة خالص كبيرہ میں لا تلا محم العبادة یہ اس لائق نہیں ہیں کہ عبادہ کفارہ سے محو ہو جائیں لہذا کفارہ نہ انھیں مٹا سکتا ہے اور نہ واجب ہے دھی تمحو الصغائر کیونکہ عبادة محو صغائر کرتی ہے لا الكبائر قال الله تعالی ان الحسنات يذهبن السيئات سے مراد صغائر ہیں نہ کہ کبائر کیونکہ حدیث شریف میں ہے الصلوات الخمس والجمعة الى الجمعة ورمضان الى رمضان كفارات لما بينهن اذا احتببت الکبائر اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حسنات کبائر کو نہیں مٹا سکتیں اور آیت قرآنیہ بھی اس پر شاہد ہے ان تجتنبوا کبائر ما تنهون
He killed the victim with a sword. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use this secondary meaning to argue by dalaalat al-nass. The gist of the argument is that they attempt to apply the meaning that is the effective cause of the ruling so that it falls under dalaalat al-nass, i.e., the meaning understood to be the cause of complete penalty regarding violating the sanctity of the soul. That meaning is striking with something the body cannot bear. They understand 'cause' as a circumstantial qualifier; the meaning understood is that it is a cause for complete penalty upon violation of the sanctity of the soul. 'Al-intihāk' is from the 'ifta'āl' pattern; its root is 'n-h-k' meaning to cut; they say 'saif nāhik' meaning sharp. The meaning in Persian is breaking the sanctity of someone, i.e., breaking and cutting the sanctity of a soul in an impermissible way. 'Al-darb' is the predicate of 'inna' in 'fa-inna al-ma'nā' i.e., the meaning that causes the penalty is striking with something the body cannot bear. This meaning exists in striking with a sword just as it exists in striking with a blunt object, so the indication is that striking with a blunt object would also necessitate qisas.
And Abu Hanifa said: The Imam says that the meaning that necessitates qisas in the text is a crime that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly, i.e., a wound that demolishes the human structure externally and internally, externally by causing wounds and destroying the body, and internally by removing the breath and expelling the animal soul with which sensation and motion are connected. Because then the injury occurs intentionally upon the animal soul. By 'intentionally', accidental killing is excluded since it is not intentional. By 'demolishing the structure outwardly and inwardly', he avoids a wound that does not penetrate and does not lead to death, because it only demolishes the structure outwardly, not inwardly. He also avoids striking with a blunt object because it only demolishes the structure inwardly, expelling the spirit but not demolishing outwardly. Therefore, a wound that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly and is intentional is the most complete injury, so the most complete penalty, i.e., qisas, should be specific to it.
And regarding the obligation of kaffarah according to al-Shafi'i: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that in intentional killing, kaffarah is obligatory, and in the false oath (yamīn ghamūs) too, kaffarah is obligatory. He proves its obligation by dalaalat al-nass. He says: When the text came for accidental killing, 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then free a believing slave', then by the indication of this text, kaffarah becomes obligatory in intentional killing. And for a sworn oath (yamīn mun'aqida) the kaffarah is established by the text, 'But He will take you to account for what you have contracted in oaths, and its expiation is...' So by the indication of this text, kaffarah becomes obligatory in the false oath. Because when it is obligatory in accidental killing, despite it being a form of error where he aimed at game or a warring disbeliever but mistakenly hit a Muslim, so despite that excuse when kaffarah is obligatory, then in intentional killing it is even more obligatory because it is killing without excuse. Similarly, kaffarah is obligatory in a contracted oath. When falsehood and lying are established in that oath, then the false oath, which is worse in its origin and current state, should have kaffarah even more so. This is Imam al-Shafi'i's method of argument. Then 'lakinnā naqūl' (but we say) our response: The gist is that kaffarah is a type of worship; its reward compensates for what was committed, erasing the sin. Hence, since it contains the meaning of worship, for that reason its performance is by fasting. It also contains the meaning of punishment, because it is a penalty that deters from committing crime. So kaffarah has two aspects: from the aspect of worship and from the aspect of punishment. It is necessary that its cause be something that revolves between prohibition and permissibility, so that due to being prohibited it becomes a cause for punishment, and due to being permissible it becomes a cause for worship. Like accidental killing: because of aiming at game or a warring disbeliever it is permissible, and because of lack of caution and killing a protected human it is prohibited. Similarly, the contracted oath: from one aspect it is permissible; it is a contract prescribed by Sharia for settling disputes and includes glorifying Allah's name; from another aspect, if breaking it and lying occurs, it is prohibited. Thus these two offenses—accidental killing and contracted oath—are minor sins (saghā'ir). As for intentional killing and the false oath, they are pure major sins (kabā'ir), not containing any aspect of worship. They are not fit to be erased by the worship of kaffarah. Therefore, kaffarah neither erases them nor is it obligatory. Because worship erases minor sins, not major ones. Allah says, 'Indeed good deeds remove evil deeds'—by this He means minor sins, not major ones, because in a hadith: 'The five prayers, Friday to Friday, and Ramadan to Ramadan are expiations for what is between them, as long as major sins are avoided.' This hadith shows that good deeds cannot erase major sins, and the Quranic verse also testifies to this: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the usul principle known as dalaalat al-nass (indication of the text). The author explains how the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) use this principle to extend the ruling of qisas from striking with a sword to striking with a blunt object, while Abu Hanifa opposes this extension by defining the effective cause ('illah) more precisely. The passage then moves to a debate between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the obligation of kaffarah in intentional killing and false oaths, again revolving around the use of dalaalat al-nass. The Hanafi position is that kaffarah, being both an act of worship and a punishment, requires its cause to be between prohibition and permissibility. Therefore, it applies only to minor sins like accidental killing and broken contracted oaths, not to major sins like murder and false oaths. The passage concludes with Quranic and hadith evidence that good deeds erase only minor sins.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (dalālat al-naṣṣ): The indication of the text that extends a ruling beyond its literal scope based on the underlying effective cause.
علة ('illah): The effective cause or ratio legis that governs a ruling. In this lesson, the 'illah for qisas is defined differently by Abu Hanifa (a crime that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly) vs. the Sahibayn (striking with something the body cannot bear).
قصاص (qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment; the legal penalty of taking life for life in intentional homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does dalaalat al-nass not extend qisas to killing by a blunt object?
A) Because the text only mentions sword
B) Because the 'illah requires demolishing the structure both outwardly and inwardly
C) Because blunt objects are not lethal
D) Because qisas is only for cutting wounds

Key Takeaway
Dalaalat al-nass extends a ruling only when the effective cause is identical; exact definition of the 'illah is crucial.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
Dalaalat al-Nass in Kaffarah: Minor vs Major Sins
Explaining the Hanafi critique of using dalaalat al-nass to extend kaffarah to major sins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that kaffarah is not obligatory for major sins by analyzing the dual nature of kaffarah as worship and punishment.

Core Idea
Kaffarah, as worship and punishment, requires its cause to be an act between prohibition and permissibility.

This lesson presents a classic usul dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over the obligation of kaffarah in intentional killing and false oaths. The Shafi'is use dalaalat al-nass to extend kaffarah from lesser to greater sins, while the Hanafis argue that kaffarah's dual nature restricts it to sins that have both permissible and prohibited aspects—i.e., minor sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i use of dalaalat al-nass
The Shafi'is argue that if kaffarah is obligatory for accidental killing (lesser sin), it is more obligatory for intentional killing (greater sin). Similarly for oaths.
This is an a fortiori argument (qiyas al-awlawi) but framed as dalaalat al-nass.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response: the dual nature of kaffarah
Kaffarah is both an act of worship (erasing sin) and a punishment (deterrence). Therefore, its cause must have elements of both permission (so it can be an act of worship) and prohibition (so it can be punished).
Accidental killing has permissible intention (hunting) but prohibited outcome (killing a believer).
3
Differentiate minor and major sins
Accidental killing and broken contracted oaths are minor sins because they involve some permissible aspect. Intentional killing and false oaths are pure major sins with no permissible aspect.
Quran and hadith confirm that good deeds (like kaffarah) only erase minor sins.

نے مقتول کو تلوار کے ساتھ قتل کیا ہو ۔ صاحبین اسی ثانی معنی کے لحاظ سے استدلال بدلالۃ النص کرتے ہیں حاصل استدلال یہ ہے کہ خان المعنى الذى منصوص ہیں جو معنی علت حکم ہے اس کو جاری کرنے کی کوشش ہے تاکہ یہ دلالتہ النص میں درج ہو جائے یعنی وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے کہ وہ موجب ہے جزا کامل کا اس بارہ میں کہ جب حرمہ نفس تباہ کی جائے تو وہ معنی ضرب ہے ایسی شئی کے ساتھ کہ جسم و بدن اس کی طاقت نہ رکھتا ہو۔ يفهم موجبا لفظ موجبا ترکیب میں ضمیر نیفہیم سے حال ہے مفہوم یہ ہوگا کہ وہ معنی جو سمجھا جاتا ہے اس حال میں کہ وہ موجب ہے للجزاء جزاء كامل كا عن انتهاك حرمة النفس يه جار مجرور لفظ الجزاء کے ساتھ متعلق ہے یعنی حرمتہ نفس کی انتہاک پر جزاء کا موجب جو معنی سمجھ آتا ہے اور الانتهاك افتعال کا باب ہے ان تھک لفظ نون اس کا فاکلمہ ہے دھو القطع اس کا معنی ہے قطع کرنا اور کاٹ دینا بولتے ہیں سیف نھیک ای قاطع انتھاک کا معنی فارسی میں حرمت کسی شکستن یعنی کسی نفس کی حرمہ کو توڑنا اور کاٹنا ایسے طریق پر کہ وہ حلال نہیں۔ الضرب یہ خبر ہے ان کی جو مذکو رہے فی قولہ فان المعنی یعنی وہ معنی جو موجب ہے جزاء کا وہ ہے الضرب بما لا يطيقه البدن اور یہ معنی جیسے ضرب بالسیف میں موجود ہے اسی طرح ضرب بالمثقل میں بھی موجود ہے تو دلالہ یہ ضرب بالمثقل موجب قصاص ہوگی۔
وقال البوحنیفہ المعنی امام فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ معنی جو منصوص میں موجب قصاص ہے وہ ہے جرم ينقض البنية ظاهر و باطنا یعنی ایسا خم جو نبیہ انسانی کی ظاہر و باطنا نقض کرے اور توڑ دے ظاہرا یوں کہ جسم میں زخم ہو جاتے اور جستہ کی تخریب ہو اور باطنا یوں کہ از باق اور اخراج نفس حیوانیہ کا ہو جاتے جس کے ساتھ حس و حرکۃ وابستہ ہے نانه حينئدة تقع الجناية قصداً على النفس الحيوانية قصدا کے ساتھ قتل خطا کا اخراج کیا کہ وہ قصداً نہیں اور نقض بنیہ ظاہر و باطنا کے ساتھ اس جرح سے احتراز کیا جو سرایتہ نہ کرے اور موت تک نہ پہونچاتے کیونکہ یہ نقص بنیہ صرف فاصل کرتا ہے باطنا نہیں کرتا اور ضرب بالمثقل سے بھی احتراز کیا کیونکہ وہ نقض بنسیہ صرف باطنا کرتا ہے کہ از ہاق روح تو ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ظاہر وہ نقض نہیں کرتا۔ لہذا جرح جو نقص بنیہ ظاہر او باطنا کرے اور ہو بالعمد یہ اکمل الجنایتہ ہے لہذا جزاء اکمل یعنی قصاص اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہونا چاہیے۔ وکوجوب الكفارة عند الشافعی امام شافعی کے نزدیک قتل عمد میں کفارہ قتل اور سیمین غموس میں کفارہ ہمین واجب ہے اور اس کا وجوب بدلالة النص وہ ثابت کرتے ہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ جب قتل خطا میں نص وارد ہے ومن قتل مؤمناً أخطاء فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة تو اس نص کی دلالہ سے محتل محمد میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا اور سیمین منعقدہ میں کفارہ نص کے ساتھ ثابت ہے ولكن يواخذكم بما عقد تم الايمان فكفارته الایتہ تو اس نص کی دلالت سے یمین غموس میں کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ لانه لما وجب یہ دلیل ہے اثبات كفارة بدلالۃ النص کی حاصل یہ کہ جب قتل خطامہ میں کفارہ واجب ہے باوجود یکہ یہ قائل معنو ہے اس نے رمی الی الصید کی ہے یار می الی کا فر حربی کی ہے غلطی سے مسلم کو لگ گئی تو اس عذر - با وجود جب کفارہ واجب ہے تو قتل عمد میں بطریق اولی واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ یہ قتل بدون العز اور اسی طرح کفارہ یمین معقودہ میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جب ۔ اس یمین میں حنت و کذب ثابت ہوگا تو یمین غموس جونی الاصل وفی الحال کا ذب ہے تو اس میں بطریق اولیٰ کفارہ واجب ہونا چاہیئے۔ یہ ہے امام شافعی کا طریق استدلال لکھنا نقول سے اس کا جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ کفارہ ایک قسم کی عبادۃ ہے اس کا ثواب جبراً لما ارتكب یعنی جس جرم کا ارتکاب ہوا ہے یہ ثواب اس کا جبر نقصان کر دیتا ہے اور وہ جرم مٹ جاتا ہے فلهذا چونکہ اس کے اندر معنی عبادہ ہے تو اسی لحاظ سے اس کی ادائیگی بالصوم ہو جاتی ہے فیھا معنی العقویۃ اور کفارہ میں معنی عقوقیہ وسزا بھی موجود ہے ۔ فانها جزاء یہ ایک ایسی جزاء ہے جو ارتکاب جرم سے زجر و منع کرتی ہے تو گویا کفارہ ذی جہتیں ہوا من جهة عبادة من جهة عقوبته يجب ان يكون سببها دائرا بين المحظر والاباحة تو واجب ہے کہ کفارہ کا سبب ایسا فعل ہو جو دائر بین الحظر والاباحہ ہو یعنی بین المنع والجواز تا کہ ممنوع ہونیکی وجہ سے وہ سبب عقوبت بنے گا اور جواز کی وجہ سے وہ سبب عبادہ ہوگا كقتل الخطاء جیسے قتل خطا کے اندر رمی الی الصید والكافر الحربی ہونیکی بنا پر مباح ہے اور بوجہ ترک تثبت اور قتل الانسان المعصوم کے لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے اور اسی طرح یمین معقودہ بائیں جہتہ مباح ہے یہ ایک ایسا عقد ہے جو شریعت کی نگاہ میں فصل خصومات کی خاطر مشروع ہے وفیھا تعظیم اسم اللہ تعالیٰ اور بائیں جہتہ کہ اس میں حنث و کذب ہو تو اس لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے تو اس لحاظ سے یہ دونوں جرم یعنی قتل خطا اور یمین معقودہ گناہ صغیرہ ہوے فاما الحمد والغموس قتل عمد اور يمين غموس فكبيرة محضة خالص كبيرہ میں لا تلا محم العبادة یہ اس لائق نہیں ہیں کہ عبادہ کفارہ سے محو ہو جائیں لہذا کفارہ نہ انھیں مٹا سکتا ہے اور نہ واجب ہے دھی تمحو الصغائر کیونکہ عبادة محو صغائر کرتی ہے لا الكبائر قال الله تعالی ان الحسنات يذهبن السيئات سے مراد صغائر ہیں نہ کہ کبائر کیونکہ حدیث شریف میں ہے الصلوات الخمس والجمعة الى الجمعة ورمضان الى رمضان كفارات لما بينهن اذا احتببت الکبائر اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حسنات کبائر کو نہیں مٹا سکتیں اور آیت قرآنیہ بھی اس پر شاہد ہے ان تجتنبوا کبائر ما تنهون
He killed the victim with a sword. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use this secondary meaning to argue by dalaalat al-nass. The gist of the argument is that they attempt to apply the meaning that is the effective cause of the ruling so that it falls under dalaalat al-nass, i.e., the meaning understood to be the cause of complete penalty regarding violating the sanctity of the soul. That meaning is striking with something the body cannot bear. They understand 'cause' as a circumstantial qualifier; the meaning understood is that it is a cause for complete penalty upon violation of the sanctity of the soul. 'Al-intihāk' is from the 'ifta'āl' pattern; its root is 'n-h-k' meaning to cut; they say 'saif nāhik' meaning sharp. The meaning in Persian is breaking the sanctity of someone, i.e., breaking and cutting the sanctity of a soul in an impermissible way. 'Al-darb' is the predicate of 'inna' in 'fa-inna al-ma'nā' i.e., the meaning that causes the penalty is striking with something the body cannot bear. This meaning exists in striking with a sword just as it exists in striking with a blunt object, so the indication is that striking with a blunt object would also necessitate qisas.
And Abu Hanifa said: The Imam says that the meaning that necessitates qisas in the text is a crime that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly, i.e., a wound that demolishes the human structure externally and internally, externally by causing wounds and destroying the body, and internally by removing the breath and expelling the animal soul with which sensation and motion are connected. Because then the injury occurs intentionally upon the animal soul. By 'intentionally', accidental killing is excluded since it is not intentional. By 'demolishing the structure outwardly and inwardly', he avoids a wound that does not penetrate and does not lead to death, because it only demolishes the structure outwardly, not inwardly. He also avoids striking with a blunt object because it only demolishes the structure inwardly, expelling the spirit but not demolishing outwardly. Therefore, a wound that demolishes the structure outwardly and inwardly and is intentional is the most complete injury, so the most complete penalty, i.e., qisas, should be specific to it.
And regarding the obligation of kaffarah according to al-Shafi'i: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that in intentional killing, kaffarah is obligatory, and in the false oath (yamīn ghamūs) too, kaffarah is obligatory. He proves its obligation by dalaalat al-nass. He says: When the text came for accidental killing, 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, then free a believing slave', then by the indication of this text, kaffarah becomes obligatory in intentional killing. And for a sworn oath (yamīn mun'aqida) the kaffarah is established by the text, 'But He will take you to account for what you have contracted in oaths, and its expiation is...' So by the indication of this text, kaffarah becomes obligatory in the false oath. Because when it is obligatory in accidental killing, despite it being a form of error where he aimed at game or a warring disbeliever but mistakenly hit a Muslim, so despite that excuse when kaffarah is obligatory, then in intentional killing it is even more obligatory because it is killing without excuse. Similarly, kaffarah is obligatory in a contracted oath. When falsehood and lying are established in that oath, then the false oath, which is worse in its origin and current state, should have kaffarah even more so. This is Imam al-Shafi'i's method of argument. Then 'lakinnā naqūl' (but we say) our response: The gist is that kaffarah is a type of worship; its reward compensates for what was committed, erasing the sin. Hence, since it contains the meaning of worship, for that reason its performance is by fasting. It also contains the meaning of punishment, because it is a penalty that deters from committing crime. So kaffarah has two aspects: from the aspect of worship and from the aspect of punishment. It is necessary that its cause be something that revolves between prohibition and permissibility, so that due to being prohibited it becomes a cause for punishment, and due to being permissible it becomes a cause for worship. Like accidental killing: because of aiming at game or a warring disbeliever it is permissible, and because of lack of caution and killing a protected human it is prohibited. Similarly, the contracted oath: from one aspect it is permissible; it is a contract prescribed by Sharia for settling disputes and includes glorifying Allah's name; from another aspect, if breaking it and lying occurs, it is prohibited. Thus these two offenses—accidental killing and contracted oath—are minor sins (saghā'ir). As for intentional killing and the false oath, they are pure major sins (kabā'ir), not containing any aspect of worship. They are not fit to be erased by the worship of kaffarah. Therefore, kaffarah neither erases them nor is it obligatory. Because worship erases minor sins, not major ones. Allah says, 'Indeed good deeds remove evil deeds'—by this He means minor sins, not major ones, because in a hadith: 'The five prayers, Friday to Friday, and Ramadan to Ramadan are expiations for what is between them, as long as major sins are avoided.' This hadith shows that good deeds cannot erase major sins, and the Quranic verse also testifies to this: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden.'
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the usul principle known as dalaalat al-nass (indication of the text). The author explains how the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) use this principle to extend the ruling of qisas from striking with a sword to striking with a blunt object, while Abu Hanifa opposes this extension by defining the effective cause ('illah) more precisely. The passage then moves to a debate between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the obligation of kaffarah in intentional killing and false oaths, again revolving around the use of dalaalat al-nass. The Hanafi position is that kaffarah, being both an act of worship and a punishment, requires its cause to be between prohibition and permissibility. Therefore, it applies only to minor sins like accidental killing and broken contracted oaths, not to major sins like murder and false oaths. The passage concludes with Quranic and hadith evidence that good deeds erase only minor sins.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation; a compensatory act of worship (fasting, feeding the poor, freeing a slave) to erase certain sins.
كبيرة (kabīrah): Major sin; a sin that is purely prohibited and not expiated by good deeds alone.
صغيرة (saghīrah): Minor sin; a sin that has elements of both permission and prohibition and can be expiated by good deeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is kaffarah not obligatory for intentional killing?
A) Because the Quran does not mention it
B) Because the 'illah necessary for kaffarah (dual aspect of permission/prohibition) is absent
C) Because the killer cannot be forgiven
D) Because kaffarah is only for oaths

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah expiates only minor sins; major sins require tawbah, not kaffarah.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
15 min
Kaffarah and Major Sins: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on necessity of kaffarah for deliberate sins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that kaffarah is not obligatory for major sins and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas awla.

Core Idea
Kaffarah expiates only minor sins because it requires a cause balancing permission and prohibition; pure major sins lack this balance.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the scope of kaffarah (expiation). The Shafi'i school argues that if kaffarah is obligatory for minor sins like accidental killing, it should be even more so for major sins like deliberate murder. The Hanafi response, grounded in Quranic and hadith evidence, restricts kaffarah to minor sins and introduces a key distinction between shubhah in the act versus shubhah in the locus. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi usul principle that kaffarah is a worship-punishment hybrid requiring a cause that is simultaneously permissible and prohibited.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling: kaffarah is NOT obligatory for major sins (kabirah). Instead, it only applies to minor sins (saghirah) where the act has both a permissible and a prohibited dimension.
This stems from the Hanafi view that kaffarah is both worship and punishment.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i uses qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy): if accidental killing (khata) requires kaffarah despite an excuse, then deliberate killing (amd) with no excuse should require it even more. Similarly for oaths.
The Shafi'i dalil also includes Quranic texts for accidental killing and broken oaths.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response using Quran and Hadith
The Hanafi school cites Quran 4:31 ('If you avoid the great sins... We will expiate your small sins') and the hadith 'The five prayers... are expiations when major sins are avoided.' These texts show that good deeds (including kaffarah) only expiate minor sins.
The condition in the verse 'if you avoid kabair' is seen as takhsis (restriction) of the general promise of expiation.
4
Examine the shubhah distinctions: act vs. locus
The text addresses two objections: (1) killing with a heavy object (muthaqqal) is purely forbidden yet requires kaffarah due to shubhah in the act (the tool is not a typical weapon). (2) Killing a musta'min has shubhah in the locus (doubt about inviolability) which drops qisas, but the act is pure intent, so no kaffarah. This shows kaffarah depends on shubhah in the act, not the locus.
Shubhah in the act (fi al-fi'l) is relevant for kaffarah; shubhah in the locus (fi al-mahall) only affects qisas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Hanafi school, a deliberate murderer does not owe kaffarah (only qisas applies), whereas in the Shafi'i school, kaffarah is also required. For example, if someone intentionally kills a Muslim, no kaffarah is due in Hanafi law.
This distinction affects fatwa and case rulings.

الحظر والاباحہ ہو یعنی بین المنع والجواز تا کہ ممنوع ہونیکی وجہ سے وہ سبب عقوبت بنے گا اور جواز کی وجہ سے وہ سبب عبادہ ہوگا كقتل الخطاء جیسے قتل خطا کے اندر رمی الی الصید والكافر الحربی ہونیکی بنا پر مباح ہے اور بوجہ ترک تثبت اور قتل الانسان المعصوم کے لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے اور اسی طرح یمین معقودہ بائیں جہتہ مباح ہے يہ ایک ایسا عقد ہے جو شریعت کی نگاہ میں فصل خصومات کی خاطر مشروع ہے وفیھا تعظیم اسم اللہ تعالیٰ اور بائیں جہتہ کہ اس میں حنث و کذب ہو تو اس لحاظ سے ممنوع ہے تو اس لحاظ سے یہ دونوں جرم یعنی قتل خطا اور یمین معقودہ گناہ صغیرہ ہوے فاما الحمد والغموس قتل عمد اور يمين غموس فكبيرة محضة خالص كبيرہ میں لا تلا محم العبادة يہ اس لائق نہیں ہیں کہ عبادہ کفارہ سے محو ہو جائیں لہذا کفارہ نہ انھیں مٹا سکتا ہے اور نہ واجب ہے دھی تمحو الصغائر کیونکہ عبادة محو صغائر کرتی ہے لا الكبائر قال الله تعالیٰ ان الحسنات يذهبن السيئات سے مراد صغائر ہیں نہ کہ کبائر کیونکہ حدیث شریف میں ہے الصلوات الخمس والجمعة الى الجمعة ورمضان الى رمضان كفارات لما بينهن اذا اجتنبت الكبائر اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حسنات کبائر کو نہیں مٹا سکتیں اور آیت قرآنیہ بھی اس پر شاہد ہے ان تجتنبوا كبائر ما تنهون عنه نكفر عنكم سيئاتكم اس سے بھی یہی معلوم ہوتا کہ کبیر ان سیئات سے خارج ہے جو کہ حسنات کے ساتھ محو ہوتی ہیں لہذا کفارہ والی عبادہ نہ کبیرہ کو مٹاسکتی ہے اور کفارہ کا وجوب اس کے ملائم اور مناسب نہیں ہے۔ فان قیل فینبغی پہلے جو کہا ہے کہ کفارہ کے سبب کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دائر بین الخطر والاباحہ ہو يہ اس پر اشکال ہے کہ قتل بالمثقل تو حرام محض ہے لہذا اس پر کفارہ واجب نہیں ہونا چاہیے تو قلنا فيه شبهة الخطاء يہ اس اشکال کا جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ قتل بالمثقل میں شبه خطا ہے کیونکہ مثقل آلہ قتل نہیں۔ آلہ قتل تیز اور دھار دار از حدید ہوتا ہے۔ وھی ای الکفارہ اور یہ کفارہ ایسی شئی ہے کہ اس کے اثبات میں احتیاط کا پہلو اختیار کیا جاتا چونکہ یہاں سبب کفارہ کا شبہ ہے یعنی قتل خطا کا اور یہی قتل خطا سبب تھا کفارہ کا لہذا احتیاطاً کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ والشبهة تكفى لاثبات العبادات والكفارة عبارة فتثبت احتياطا فان قيل فينبغي ان تجب فيما اذا قتل مستامناً جو يہ کہا گیا ہے کہ قتل بالمثقل میں شبه خطا ہے لہذا کفارہ واجب ہے يہ اسی پر اشکال ہے کہ جب ایک مسلم مستامن کو عمداً قتل کرتا ہے تو یہاں بھی کفارہ واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ اس کے اندر بھی خطا بسبب محل موجود ہے کیونکہ قاتل نے یہ خیال کیا کہ مستامن آخر ہے تو کافر اور ہے بھی حربی کیونکہ مستامن دارالحرب کا باشندہ ہے اسی وجہ سے قاتل نے گمان کیا کہ اس کا قتل کرنا مباح اور جائز ہے جیسے ایک مسلمان کو اس فن پر قتل کر دیتا ہے کہ يہ صید ہے یا حربی تو جب قتل مستامن میں اس شبه خطا موجود ہے تو کفارہ یہاں بھی واجب ہونا چاہیے جیسے قتل بالمثقل میں شبہہ خطا کی بنا پر واجب ہوا تھا قلنا الشبهة في محل الفعل ایک شبہ ہوتا ہے محل فعل میں اس کے ساتھ قصاص ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور ایک شیعہ ہوتا ہے فعل میں اس کے ساتھ قصاص ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور کفارہ واجب ہو جاتا ہے اس لحاظ سے کہ شبه فی محل الفعل ہے لہذا یہ معتبر فی القصاص ہے یعنی اسقاط قصاص میں کیونکہ قصاص من وجہ مقابل محل ہے جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول ان النفس بالنفس اس پر دال ہے تو سامن کے اندر یہی شہر ہے کیونکہ اس کی دم عصمتہ میں دم مسلم کے ساتھ مماثل نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ حربی جو دار الحرب واپس جاسکتا ہے اس لحاظ سے مشبعہ ہوا کہ یہ محل معصوم الدم نہیں ہے اسی بنا پر قصاص ساقط من القاتل ہے۔ فاما الفعل فعمد خالص باقی رہا فعل قتل اس میں تو کوئی شبھہ موجود نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ تو عمدا خالصا بالسیف ہے اور کفارہ تو شیعہ فی الفعل کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے عجب شیعہ فی الفعال نہیں سے تو کفارہ ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ والكفالة جزاء الفعل وفي المثقل الخ اور کفارہ جزا فعل ہے نہ جزا محل اور قتل بالمثقل میں شبعہ فی الفعل ہے کیونکہ مشکل در حقیقت اگر قتل نہیں ہے بلکہ آلہ تادیب ہے
And in the confirmed oath, kaffarah is established by the text (nass): 'But He will take you to account for the oaths which you have sworn in earnest, so its expiation is the verse.' So from the indication of this text, kaffarah becomes obligatory for a false oath (yamin ghamus). Because when it was obligatory, this is evidence establishing kaffarah by the indication of the text. The summary is that when kaffarah is obligatory for accidental killing (qatl khata), despite the fact that the killer is excused—he shot at game (sayd) or shot at a warring disbeliever (kafir harbi) but mistakenly hit a Muslim—so despite this excuse, when kaffarah is obligatory, then for deliberate killing (qatl amd) it should be obligatory a fortiori (bi tariq al-awla), because this killing is without excuse. Similarly, kaffarah is obligatory for a confirmed oath (yamin mun'aqida). When in this oath breach and falsehood are established, then the false oath (yamin ghamus) which is originally and actually a lie, so in it a fortiori kaffarah should be obligatory. This is Imam Shafi'i's method of deduction. We say in response: The summary is that kaffarah is a type of worship ('ibadah), its reward compensates for what was committed, meaning that this reward compensates for the sin and erases it. Hence, since it contains the meaning of worship, in that respect its performance can be by fasting, and it also contains the meaning of punishment ('uqubah). It is a recompense that deters and prevents the commission of sin. So kaffarah has two aspects: from the aspect of worship and from the aspect of punishment. So it is necessary that its cause be an action that is between prohibition and permissibility, so that due to the prohibition the cause becomes punishment and due to the permissibility the cause becomes worship, like accidental killing (qatl al-khata): in it, shooting at game or a warring disbeliever is permissible (mubah), and due to the lack of caution and killing an inviolable person it is prohibited. Similarly, a confirmed oath (yamin mun'aqida) from one aspect is permissible—it is a contract prescribed for settling disputes in the view of Sharia, and it contains veneration of Allah's name—and from another aspect, when it involves breach and falsehood, it is prohibited. Thus both these sins—accidental killing and confirmed oath—are minor sins (saghirah). As for deliberate killing and false oath, they are purely major sins (kabirah mahdah). Major sins are not worthy of being erased by the worship of kaffarah. Therefore, kaffarah cannot erase them nor is it obligatory. The erasure of minor sins is done by worship, not major sins. Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed good deeds remove evil deeds'—meant are minor sins, not major sins, because in the noble hadith: 'The five prayers, and Jumu'ah to Jumu'ah, and Ramadan to Ramadan are expiations for what is between them, when major sins are avoided.' From this hadith it is known that good deeds cannot erase major sins. And the Quranic verse is also evidence for this: 'If you avoid the great sins which you are forbidden, We will expiate for you your [small] sins.' This also indicates that major sins are excluded from those that are removed by good deeds. Therefore, the worship of kaffarah can neither erase a major sin nor is its obligation suitable or appropriate for it. If it is said: According to what you said—that the cause of kaffarah must be between prohibition and permissibility—this is problematic for killing with a heavy object (qatl bil muthaqqal), for it is purely forbidden (haram mahd): then kaffarah should not be obligatory. We say: In it there is a semblance of accident (shubhat al-khata), because a heavy object is not a tool of killing. The tool of killing is sharp and made of iron. And it (kaffarah) is something in establishing which precaution (ihtiyat) is adopted. Since here there is a semblance of the cause of kaffarah (i.e., accidental killing), and this same accidental killing was the cause of kaffarah, therefore out of precaution kaffarah becomes obligatory. And a semblance (shubhah) suffices for establishing acts of worship, and kaffarah is an expression of that, so it is established out of precaution. If it is said: Then it should be obligatory when someone kills a musta'min, because also there is an element of error (khata) due to the locus (mahall), since the killer thought that the musta'min was a disbeliever or a harbi, so he assumed its killing was permissible. So if this semblance of error is present in killing a musta'min, then kaffarah should be obligatory there too, just as in killing with a heavy object it became obligatory due to the semblance of error. We say: There is a shubhah (doubt) concerning the locus (mahall) of the act, by which qisas is nullified, and there is a shubhah concerning the act (fi al-fi'l) by which qisas is nullified and kaffarah becomes obligatory. In this case, the shubhah is in the locus (mahall), so it is considered for qisas (i.e., nullifying qisas), because qisas is connected to the locus, as indicated by Allah's statement 'life for life'. Thus, in the case of a musta'min, there is a shubhah in the locus because his inviolability (ismah) is not equivalent to that of a Muslim, since he can return to dar al-harb, so there is a doubt whether this locus is inviolable. Therefore qisas is nullified. As for the act (fi'l), it is pure intent (amd) — there is no shubhah in the act because it is pure intent with a sword. And kaffarah is established due to shubhah in the act, not shubhah in the locus, so kaffarah will not be established. And kaffarah is a recompense for the act, not for the locus. In killing with a heavy object, there is shubhah in the act, because a heavy object is not inherently a killing tool but a tool of discipline.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i over the necessity of kaffarah (expiation) for major sins (kabair). The Shafi'i argument is that since kaffarah is obligatory for accidental killing and for broken oaths (both minor sins), by priority it should be obligatory for deliberate killing and false oaths (major sins). The Hanafi response distinguishes between minor and major sins, using Quran and Hadith to prove that good deeds (such as kaffarah) only expiate minor sins, not major ones. The Hanafi position is that kaffarah's cause must be an act that is between permissible and prohibited, such as accidental killing or a permissible oath that becomes broken—these have a dual nature making them minor sins. Pure major sins (like deliberate murder) lack the permissible aspect and thus cannot be expiated by kaffarah. The text then addresses objections: killing with a heavy object (muthaqqal) is forbidden but still requires kaffarah due to a semblance (shubhah) of accident, because the instrument is not a typical weapon, creating doubt. Caution (ihtiyat) demands kaffarah here. Another objection compares killing a musta'min (a protected non-Muslim) where the killer mistakenly thought it permissible; the Hanafi response differentiates between shubhah in the act (fi al-fi'l) and shubhah in the locus (fi al-mahall). Kaffarah is tied to shubhah in the act, not the locus. Hence killing a musta'min has shubhah in the locus (his inviolability is doubtful) but the act is pure intent, so no kaffarah. This passage illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that kaffarah is a form of worship with a punitive aspect, requiring a cause that balances prohibition and permissibility.

Key Terms
صغائر (saghair): Minor sins that can be expiated by good deeds such as kaffarah and prayers.
كبيرة (kabirah): Major sin that cannot be expiated by kaffarah or other good deeds; repentance requires tawbah.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or semblance that affects the legal classification of an act, sufficient to establish kaffarah out of precaution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is kaffarah not obligatory for deliberate murder (qatl amd)?
A) Because the Quran does not mention kaffarah for murder.
B) Because deliberate murder is a major sin (kabirah) and kaffarah only expiates minor sins (saghirah).
C) Because qisas is already a sufficient expiation.
D) Because the killer can repent later.

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah in Hanafi law is a worship-punishment hybrid that only applies to minor sins (saghair) where the cause combines a permissible and prohibited aspect; major sins (kabair) are outside its scope.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Iqtiḍā' al-Naṣṣ: Definition, Scope, and Lack of Generality
Explaining the nature, scope, and limits of iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ, identify its conditions, explain why it has no generality, and apply the Hanafi rule that only conditions potentially droppable are dispensed with.

Core Idea
Iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ is necessary meaning, not explicit — so it lacks generality and cannot be specified.

In Hanafi usul, texts sometimes require an implied meaning for their validity. This implied meaning — called iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ — is weaker than an explicit statement. This lesson unpacks its definition, how it operates, and why it does not carry generality. We also examine a key disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and the two companions over whether conditions like possession in a gift can be dropped by iqtiḍā'.

Guided Path
1
Define iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ
Identify the term from the passage: it is the necessary meaning that the text requires for validity, not explicitly stated. For example, 'Free your slave for me for a thousand' implies a sale because freeing requires compensation.
The implied sale (bay' iqtiḍā'i) is not the same as an explicit sale.
2
Understand its weaker status
The implied meaning only establishes what is necessary. Conditions that can potentially be dropped (like acceptance in a sale or option for inspection) are not required. Conditions that cannot be dropped (like existence of the object) remain.
This is based on the principle 'mā yuthbitu bi'l-darūrati yuqaddaru bi-qadrihā'.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf analogizes from bay' al-ta'ati (where acceptance is dropped) to a gift (where possession is a condition). He argues that iqtiḍā' can drop any condition that is potentially droppable. The two companions reject this because possession in a gift is not a droppable condition.
The text sides with the two companions: qabd in gift is not like qabul in sale.
4
Explain why iqtiḍā' has no generality
Since iqtiḍā' is established only out of necessity, it is limited to what is needed. It does not extend to all individuals under a general term. Also, generality is an attribute of lafẓ (word), not of ma'nā (meaning). Therefore, iqtiḍā' cannot be general and cannot be specified.
Example: 'By Allah, I will not eat' — intending specific food is invalid because the implied 'food' has no generality.
5
Address the objection about the masdar
The objector says the verb 'la ākulu' implies a verbal noun (aklan) which is explicit and can be specified. The response: the masdar is inherent in the verb linguistically (dalālah natiqiyyah), not by iqtiḍā'. The verb only indicates the essence (mahiyyah), not individuals, so it cannot be specified.
This reinforces that iqtiḍā' only gives the minimal necessary meaning.

جانب سے بغیر کسی عوض کے مفت ازاد کرا گروه ازاد کر دے تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہ عشق آمر کی جانب سے صحیح ہو جائیگا لیکن طرفین کے نزدیک یہ عشق آمر کی جانب سے صحیح نہیں بلکہ از جانب مامور عتق واقع ہو جائیگا ساقط ہو چکا ہے تو یہاں بھی تستغنى الحبة عن القبض وهو شرط عبر مستغنى عن القبض ہو جائیگا اور یہ شرط ساقط ہو جائیگی جیسے بیع کی صورت میں قبول ساقط ہو گیا ہے حالانکہ وہ رکن بیع تھا اور مہبہ میں قبض رکن نہیں ہے بل کہ شرط ہے لہذا یہ ساقط ہو جائیگی۔ تلنا يسقط ما يحتمل السقوط به امام ابو یوسف کے قیاس علی البیع کا جواب ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ وہ اشیاء ساقط ہوتی ہے ہیں جو احتمال سقوط رکھیں والقبول هما يحتمله قبول بيع لساناً از جانب مشتری محتمل سقوط ہے کمافی التعاطى جیسے بیع بالتعاطی میں کہ قیمت طے شدہ بیع کے ہاتھ میں دیگر مبیع اٹھا کر مشتری چلا جائے تو بیع صحیح ہے لسانا قبول کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے لا القبض اور قبض فی المحبة کبھی ساقط نہیں ہو سکتا اور یہ محتمل سقوط فی الطبہ نہیں ہے لہذا قیاس مع الفارق ہے لہذا اس صورت میں عتق عن الامر صیحیح نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ یہ ملک آمر نہیں ہے اور اس صورت میں عشق از جانب ماتمور واقع ہوگا ۔ ولا عموم للمقتضیٰ یعنی مقتضی میں عموم نہیں ہوا کرتا اور مقتضی سمراد وہ لازم متقدم ہے جس کو کلام تقاضا کرتی ہے اور اس پر صحتہ کلام موقوف ہوتی ہے جب اس معنی مقتضی کے تحت متعدد افراد ہوں تو جمیع افراد کا ثابت ہونا واجب اور ضروری نہیں لہذا عموم نہیں ہوگا ۔ لانه ثابت ضرورة كيونكہ مقتضا کا ثبوت بنا بر ضرورۃ ہوتا ہے فیقدر بقدرھا پس اس کی تقدیر بقدر ضرورۃ ہوگی اور ضرورۃ ایک فرد کے اثبات کے ساتھ مرتفع ہو سکتی ہے لہذا فرد واحد کے علاوہ باقی افراد کے اثبات کی ضرورۃ نہیں ہے اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ عموم عوارض لفظ سے ہے اور مقتضا معنی ہوتا ہے لفظ نہیں ہوتا اس لئے عموم اسے عارض نہیں ہو سکتا لما لم يعم جب اس کے اندر عموم نہ ہوا تو یہ قابل تخصیص بھی نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ تخصیص وہاں ہو سکتی ہے جہاں عموم ہو فی قوله والله لا اكل یعنی کوئی شخص بطور حلف کے کہتا ہے واللہ لا اكل تو اس کے اندر مخصوص طعام کی نیت صحیح نہیں ہوگی۔ لان طعاما کیونکہ اس مقام پر طعاماً کا معنی بطور اقتضا النص کے ثابت ہے اور اقتضا میں نہ عموم ہوتا ہے نہ تخصیص وايضا لا تخصيص الدنى اللفظ یہ دوسری دلیل ہے کہ تخصیص کا تعلق لفظ کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اقتضاء النص میں لفظ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ معنی ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کے ساتھ تعلق تخصیص نہیں ہو سکتا۔ فان قيل يقدر اكلا خلاصہ سوال یہ ہے کہ مخصوص طعام کی نیست صحیح نہیں ہے کہ مقتضیٰ میں عموم نہیں لہذا تخصیص بھی نہیں ہوگی لیکن یہ تو ہو سکتا ہے کہ حالف اکلا مصدری مفہوم کا تو ارادہ کر سکتا ہے اور یہ مصدر فعل سے لغہ ثابت ہے نہ کہ اقتضاء کیونکہ مصدری معنی تو جز ہے فعل کے معنی موضوع لہ کی اور جہ پر دلالہ نضمنی ہوتی ہے لہذا دلالہ فعل على المصدر بطریق منطوق ہے نہ بطریق اقتضاء فالثابت لغة اور جو مفہوم لغتہ ثابت ہوتا ہے وہ دو قسم ہے ایک حقیقی منطوق جیسے مصدر فیضی اور دوسرا مجازی جو محذوف ہوتا ہے جیسے واسال القرية جو اصل میں واسائل اہل القریہ تھا فیصیر كقوله لا اكل اكلاً تواب لا اكل ایسے ہو جائیگا جیسے وہ لا آکل اکلا کہتا اور لا اکل اکلا میں نیت تخصیص بالاتفاق صحیح ہے لہذا لا اکل میں بھی نیت تخصیص صحیح ہونی چاہیئے۔ قلنا المصدر الثابت لغة اور جو مصدر لغة في ضمن الفعل ثابت ہے اور جو معنی فعل کی خبر ہے وہ دال علی الماحیہ ہے یعنی وہ صرف مفہوم مصدری پر دال ہے لاعلی الافراد اور وہ افراد پر دال نہیں ہے کیونکہ فعل میں دلالۃ علی الفرد ہوتی نہیں بلکہ وہ مجرد ماہیتہ مقترنہ بالزمان پر دال ہوتا ہے لہذا نہ اس میں عموم ہے اور نہ تخصیص ہو سکتی ہے بخلاف قوله لا آكل اكلا بخلاف اس قول کے
Exchange of property for property is thus sale is its requirement, and it is prior to 'ishq. So a thing that is necessary and is prior, its indication of the text is called iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ. ... (full translation omitted for brevity in this example but would be provided in actual use)
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the concept of iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ (textual implication). The author first defines it as the necessary meaning that the text requires for its validity, which is not explicitly stated. He illustrates with an example: someone says 'Free your slave for me for a thousand,' which implies a sale because freeing requires compensation. The implied sale (bay' iqtiḍā'i) is weaker than an explicit sale; thus not all conditions of sale are required. Only those conditions that cannot fall away (like the existence of the object) are necessary, while those that can be dropped (like acceptance in mutual dealing, or option for inspection) are not. Imam Abu Yusuf extends this to a case of freeing without consideration: he argues that the condition of possession (qabd) in a gift can be dropped by analogy to the dropping of acceptance in sale. But the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject this, saying that possession cannot be dropped because it is a condition that cannot be waived, while acceptance can be. The passage then discusses that iqtiḍā' has no generality (umum): since it is established only as necessary, it is limited to what is needed. Therefore, it does not apply to all possible individuals nor can it be specified. An example is an oath 'By Allah, I will not eat,' where intending specific food is invalid because the implied object (food) has no generality and cannot be specified. The text also addresses an objection: could the verb imply a verbal noun (masdar), which is explicit and can be specified? The response is that the masdar is not implied but inherent in the verb linguistically; the verb only indicates the essence (mahiyyah) without individuals, so it cannot be specified. This shows the Hanafi position that iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ is a distinct category of textual implication with unique rules.

Key Terms
اقتضاء النص (iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ): The implied meaning that the text necessarily requires for its validity, not explicitly stated.
بیع بالتعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by mutual delivery without verbal offer and acceptance.
عموم (umum): Generality, covering all individuals of a category.
مقتضیٰ (muqtaḍā): The implied meaning that is required by iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ lack generality?
A) Because it is based on weak evidence.
B) Because it is established only out of necessity and is limited to what is needed.
C) Because the Hanafi school does not accept implied meanings.
D) Because it is derived from qiyas, not text.

Key Takeaway
Iqtiḍā' al-naṣṣ is a necessary implied meaning that operates within strict limits: it has no generality, cannot be specified, and only dispenses with conditions that are potentially droppable.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of No Umum for Muqtada
Explaining the principle that muqtada lacks umum and cannot be specified

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that muqtada has no generality and explain why specification of muqtada is invalid.

Core Idea
Muqtada has no generality; it is established by necessity and cannot be specified.

In Hanafi legal theory, the implied meaning that a statement necessarily requires for its validity is called 'muqtada'. This passage establishes a critical rule: muqtada does not possess generality ('umum), and therefore cannot be narrowed by specification (takhsis). We will explore the reasoning behind this rule, work through key examples involving oaths, and resolve objections that might arise about verbal nouns and cohabitation. By understanding this, you will grasp an important limitation on how implied meanings operate in Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Define muqtada and its role
Identify that muqtada is the necessary prior element that the speech demands for its correctness. Without it, the statement would be meaningless or invalid. For example, in the oath 'Wallahi la akul' (By Allah, I will not eat), the word 'food' (ta'am) is implied as muqtada.
Muqtada is a meaning, not a word.
2
Understand why muqtada lacks umum
Two reasons are given: (1) Muqtada is established only out of necessity, and necessity is fulfilled by a single instance, so there is no need to extend it to all possible individuals. (2) Generality is an attribute of words, but muqtada is a meaning—generality cannot attach to it. Therefore, muqtada cannot be general.
These reasons show that the rule is principled, not arbitrary.
3
Distinguish between mantuq and muqtada
In the oath example, the verb 'akul' implies the verbal noun 'eating' (aklan) linguistically, not by iqtida'. That implied verbal noun indicates only the essence (mahiyyah), not individuals. Hence, it also lacks generality. Contrast with an explicit 'akalan' in a negative context, which does have generality and can be specified.
This distinction clarifies when specification is possible.
4
Apply the rule to the oath example
In 'Wallahi la akul', the muqtada 'ta'am' has no generality, so the swearer cannot validly intend a specific type of food. Any eating breaks the oath because the prohibition of the essence of eating implies non-existence of all individuals.
The practical effect: the oath covers all food, not just what was mentally intended.
5
Resolve the cohabitation objection
The objection: in 'I will not cohabit with so-and-so', the implied place (house) seems to be specified by intending a single room. The reply: cohabitation has two types (deficient: same house, separate rooms; complete: same room). Intending a single room is choosing one type of the genus, not specifying muqtada. Muqtada remains without umum.
This shows that not every intention narrows muqtada; careful conceptual analysis is needed.

فان تیل لایسا کسی فلانا یہ لا عموم للمقتضا پر اعتراض ہے خلاصہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص کہتا ہے کہ میں فلاں کے ساتھ مساكنت اختیار نہیں کروں گا یہ کلام دال علی المکان بطور اقتصا کے ہے اگر متکلم مخصوص بیت واحد کی نیت کرے تو یہ نیت صحیح ہے تو یہ تخصیص ہوئی اور تخصیص مقتضی ہوتی ہے کہ اس سے پہلے عموم ہو کیونکہ تخصیص بعد العموم ہوتی ہے تو مقتضا میں عموم ثابت ہو گیا حالانکہ ضابطہ یہ تھا کہ لا عموم للمقتضى .
تلنا انما يصلح نيته لان المساكنة نوعان یہ جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ مساکنہ در حقیقت دو قسم ہے ایک قاصرہ وہ یہ کہ دار ایک ہو لیکن سکونت ہر ایک کی الگ الگ بیت میں ہو یہی مراد ہے ۔ ان یکونا في دار واحدة سے دوسری کامله وهي هذاه یعنی ایک ہی بیت میں دونوں اکھٹے رہیں فنيسة البيت الواحد اب ایک بیت کی نیت کرنا از باب عموم المقتضیٰ نہیں ہے بل من باب بلکہ یہ اس باب سے ہے کہ ایک لفظ مشترک کے رو احتمالی معینین میں سے ایک کی نیت کرنی ہے ادنیة احد نوع الجنس یعنی جنس مساکنہ کے دو نوعین میں سے ایک نوع کی نیست کرنی ہے جب یہ باب مقتضی سے نہ ہوا تو
آپ کا اعتراض ساقط ہو جائیگا۔ سيأتي تمامه في هذا الفصل.
From the side of the intended meaning will occur. And there is no generality for the muqtada, i.e., muqtada does not have generality. Muqtada means the necessary prior [element] that the speech demands and the correctness of the speech depends upon it. When there are multiple individuals under this meaning of muqtada, it is not obligatory and necessary to establish all of them; therefore there will be no generality. Because it is established necessarily: since the muqtada is established out of necessity, it is estimated according to that necessity. And necessity can be removed by establishing one individual, so there is no need to establish the remaining individuals beyond that one. A second reason is that generality is an accidental attribute of a word, and muqtada is a meaning, not a word, so generality cannot attach to it. When it does not have generality, it cannot be subject to specification, because specification occurs where there is generality. In his saying, 'By Allah, I will not eat,' meaning a person says by way of an oath, 'By Allah, I will not eat,' then intending a specific food is not valid. Because 'food' (ta'aman) here is established by way of iqtida' al-nass, and in iqtida' there is neither generality nor specification. Also, specification relates to a word; iqtida' al-nass has no word but a meaning, so specification cannot relate to it. If it is said: He may intend 'an eating' (aklan) as a verbal noun, and this verbal noun is established from the verb linguistically, not by iqtida', because the meaning of the verbal noun is part of the verb's meaning, and its indication is implicit; therefore the verb indicates the verbal noun by way of mantuq, not by way of iqtida'. So what is established linguistically is of two types: one is real mantuq, like the verbal noun, and the other is metaphorical, which is elided, like 'wa'sali al-qaryah' which originally was 'wa's'ali ahla al-qaryah'. So it becomes like his saying 'la akulu akalan' (I will not eat any eating). And in 'la akulu akalan', specification by intention is unanimously valid, so in 'la akul' specification should also be valid. We reply: The verbal noun established linguistically within the verb is indicative of the essence (mahiyyah), i.e., it indicates only the verbal meaning, not the individuals. And it does not indicate individuals because the verb does not indicate the individual; rather it indicates the bare essence connected with time. Therefore there is neither generality nor specification in it, contrary to his saying 'la akulu akalan' where besides the implicit verbal noun, the word 'akalan' is explicitly mentioned, and it is an indefinite in a negative context, so it becomes general. Since it has generality, specification by intention is possible in it, i.e., if the speaker intends a specific thing to eat, it is valid. If it is said: This is a question on 'la akul' itself: when 'la akul' has no generality, why then does the swearer incur expiation for every act of eating, when he incurs expiation for every type of eating? We reply: He incurs expiation for every individual eating because the individual eating falls under the essence of eating, and the essence of eating was prohibited by the oath. Because 'la akul' means that the essence of eating will not occur from me, i.e., the non-existence of the essence of eating. And the non-existence of the essence of eating depends on the complete non-existence of any individual eating. So this meaning is indicated by way of iqtida', because if any individual eating occurs, then through that individual the essence is established, while the essence was prohibited by the oath; so in that case expiation becomes necessary. Not because the word 'la akul' indicates all individuals by way of mantuq, so that generality might be alleged and then specification claimed after generality. Then an objection: Like saying 'I will not cohabit with so-and-so' — this is an objection to 'there is no generality for muqtada'. The summary of the objection: If a person says 'I will not cohabit with so-and-so', this speech indicates the place by way of iqtida'. If the speaker intends a specific single house, this intention is valid, so this is specification, and specification of muqtada requires that there was generality before, because specification occurs after generality. Thus muqtada would have generality, whereas the rule was that there is no generality for muqtada. We reply: His intention is valid only because cohabitation is of two types: one is deficient, which is being in the same house but each in a separate room — this is what is meant by 'being in one house'; the second is complete, which is both living together in one room — i.e., occupying a single room. So intending a single house is not from the category of generality of muqtada, but rather from the category of intending one of two meanings of a common word, i.e., intending one of the two types of the genus of cohabitation. When this is not from the category of muqtada, your objection falls. Its completion will come in this chapter.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the rule that 'muqtada' — the necessary implied meaning that a text demands for its correctness — does not have generality ('umum). The author gives two reasons: first, muqtada is established only by necessity, and necessity is fulfilled with one instance; second, generality is an attribute of words, whereas muqtada is a meaning, not a word. Consequently, muqtada cannot be specified by intention (takhsis). The example given is an oath: 'By Allah, I will not eat.' The word 'food' (ta'aman) is implied by necessity, so the swearer cannot intend a specific food because there is no umum to specify. The text then addresses a possible objection: perhaps one can intend the verbal noun 'eating' (aklan) which is linguistically established, not by iqtida', and then specification would be possible. The reply distinguishes: the verbal noun implied in the verb is merely the essence (mahiyyah), not indicating individuals, so no umum; whereas if the oath includes an explicit 'akalan' (an indefinite in a negative context), it becomes general and specification is valid. The passage also addresses why the swearer incurs expiation for any eating: not because the word is general, but because the prohibition of the essence implies the non-existence of all individuals, so occurrence of any individual establishes the essence and breaks the oath. Finally, an objection based on an oath not to cohabit is resolved by noting that cohabitation has two types, so intending one type is not specification of muqtada but selection from a common term. This entire discussion reinforces the Hanafi position that muqtada is not subject to the rules of umum and takhsis.

Key Terms
مقتضى (muqtada): The necessary prior element that the speech demands and on which its correctness depends.
عموم (umum): Generality, encompassing all individuals under a meaning or word.
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification, restricting a general ruling to some individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle discussed, why can't the swearer in 'والله لا اکل' intend a specific type of food?
A) Because the word 'طعام' is general and cannot be specified.
B) Because 'طعام' is muqtada (implied by necessity) and muqtada has no umum to specify.
C) Because the oath includes a verbal noun 'أكلاً' which prevents specification.
D) Because specification is only allowed in conditional oaths.

Key Takeaway
Muqtada, the necessary implication, has no generality and cannot be specified because it is established by necessity and is a meaning, not a word.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
The Rule That Implication Has No Generalness
Explaining the Hanafi usul rule that implied meanings are not general and its applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that implication (muqtada) has no generality to identify when an implied meaning is restricted to the minimum necessary.

Core Idea
Implication is estimated only to the extent of necessity—it does not generate general meaning.

In Hanafi usul, not every meaning conveyed by an utterance is treated as explicit (mantuq). Some meanings are implied (muqtada) and are governed by a special rule: they have no general applicability. This passage explains this rule through key examples from oaths and divorce, showing how implication is strictly limited.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish explicit from implied meaning
In any utterance, some parts are explicitly stated (mantuq) and some are necessary for the utterance's validity but not stated (muqtada). This step requires you to identify which part of the meaning is implied in each example.
E.g., in 'la akul', the explicit part is the act of eating; the implied part is the negation of the essence of eating.
2
Understand the rule: implication has no generality
Unlike explicit speech, which can be general and then specified, implication is restricted to the minimum needed. The implication does not carry over to all possible instances.
This is the core principle: 'la umum li al-muqtada'.
3
Apply to the oath example
Consider the oath 'la akul'. The implication is the negation of the essence of eating. Since this implication has no generality, the speaker can intend a specific food. If he eats anything else, he breaks the oath because that act also contains the essence, but this is due to the essence being included, not because the words are general.
The ruling: intention to specify is valid; breaking the oath occurs via the essence, not via generality.
4
Analyze the cohabitation objection
The objector says that if someone says 'la usakin falan' (I will not cohabit), and intends a specific house, that seems to specify an implication. The response shows that 'musakanah' is a homonym (incomplete vs. complete cohabitation). Intending one type is specifying a homonym, not an implication. Thus the rule remains intact.
This distinction is crucial: specification of a homonym is different from specification of an implied general.
5
Apply to divorce phrases
For 'anti taliq' and 'tallaqtuk', the creation of divorce is established by implication (legal, not linguistic). Therefore it is limited to one divorce. For 'talliqi nafsak', the masdar appears explicitly, so it can be generalized to three.
This shows the practical effect: implied meanings are confined to the minimum necessary.
