ومنہ اى من مفهوم المخالفة یہ خبر مقدم ہے هذه المسئلة یہ مبتدا مؤخر ہے دھی اور وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے ان تخصیص ایشی یعنی ایک ٹٹی کی کسی حکم میں تخصیص بالوصف كرنا يدل على نفى الحكم عما عداه عند الشافعی" ی تخصیص اس پر دال ہے کہ عند الشوافع یہ حکم ماعدا وصف سے منتفی ہوگا یعنی جہاں یہ وصف نہیں ہوگی وہاں حکم مذکور ثابت نہیں ہوگا او نقول یہ عبارة مذکور کی ترکیبی حالت دوسری طریق پر واضح کر یہ ہے ہیں ایک تو وہی جو تحریر ہو چکی ہے دوسری یہ ہے کہ منہ خبر مقدم ہے اور اس کا مبتدأ هذه المسئلہ نہ نکالا جائے بلکہ اس کا مبتدا تخصیص الشئی کا لفظ ہو اور منہ اس کی خبر مقدم ہو۔ وقوله يدل یہ خبر ہو مبتدا محذوف کی ای مو یعنی وہ لفظ ھو ہے جو راجع ہے تخصیص الشی کی طرف وتوله عما عداء یعنی عما عدا ذلك الوصف والمراد یعنی خلاصہ یہ کہ حکم اسی نشتی سے بدون ذلك الوصف منتفی ہو جائیگا یعنی جہاں یہ وصف نہیں ہوگی وہاں حکم مذکور ثابت نہیں ہوگا جیسے اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول من فتياتكم المؤمنات ہے خص الحل یعنی نکاح کا حلال ہونا ان فتیات کے ساتھ مختص کیا گیا ہے جو مؤمنات ہوں فیلزم عندهم تو شوافع کے نزدیک ان فتیات سے نکاح صحیح نہیں ہو گا جو مومنات
And from it, i.e., from mafhum al-mukhalafah, this sentence 'hādha al-mas'alah' is the predicate advanced, and 'hādhihi al-mas'alah' is the subject delayed. And that issue is: that specification of a thing (takhsis al-shay') i.e., in a ruling, specification by a description indicates the negation of the ruling from what is besides that description, according to the Shafi'is. This specification indicates that according to the Shafi'is, this ruling is negated from what is besides the description, meaning that where this description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not proven. And we say: this mentioned expression has two ways of syntactical clarity: one is what has been written, and the second is that 'minhu' is the predicate advanced, and its subject should not be taken as 'hādhihi al-mas'alah', but rather its subject is the word 'takhsis al-shay'' and 'minhu' is its predicate advanced. And his saying 'yadullu' is the predicate of an omitted subject, i.e., the word 'huwa' which refers to 'takhsis al-shay''. And his saying 'amma 'adāhu' means besides that description. And the intended meaning is that the ruling from this text is negated without that description, i.e., where that description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not proven. Like the saying of Allah Almighty: 'min fatayātikumu al-mu'mināt' (from your believing slave girls). He specified permissibility (i.e., the permissibility of marriage) with those slave girls who are believing. So, according to them (the Shafi'is), marriage is not valid with slave girls who are not believing.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the types of mafhum al-mukhalafah. The second type is 'takhsis bi al-wasf' (specification by description). According to the Shafi'is, when a ruling is attached to a thing by a specific description, it indicates that the ruling is negated for anything that does not possess that description. The commentator analyzes the syntax of the author's words, explaining two possible grammatical constructions. The meaning is that the ruling is confined to the described case. The example given is from the Quran: 'min fatayātikumu al-mu'mināt' (from your believing slave girls). According to the Shafi'is, this specification by the description 'believing' implies that marriage is not permissible with non-believing slave girls. The Hanafi position is not explicitly stated in this passage, but from the earlier discussion, the Hanafis generally reject such loose reliance on mafhum al-mukhalafah. The passage ends abruptly, likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالوصف (takhsis bi al-wasf): Specification by a description; attaching a ruling to a thing along with a qualifier, which is claimed to indicate the negation of the ruling for things without that qualifier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shafi'i position presented in this passage, what is the implication of the Quranic verse 'min fatayātikumu al-mu'mināt' for marrying non-believing slave girls?
A) Marriage is permissible because the verse does not explicitly forbid it.
B) Marriage is not permissible because the description 'mu'mināt' specifies that only believing slave girls are allowed.
C) Marriage is permissible only if they convert to Islam.
D) The verse has no bearing on the ruling of marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Shafi'i usul, specification by description (takhsis bi al-wasf) is considered a type of mafhum al-mukhalafah, implying that the ruling is confined to the described case and negated for all others.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Hanafi Rejection: The Hadith of Water and Lam al-Istighraq
Explains the Hanafi refutation using the hadith of water and lam al-istighraq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school uses lam al-istighraq to argue that the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' does not support mafhum al-mukhalafa and identify the evidence for ghusl from the meeting of circumcised parts.

Core Idea
The Ansar's understanding was based on lam al-istighraq, not mafhum al-mukhalafa — proof of ghusl comes from the meeting of circumcised parts as evidence of insal.

This passage clarifies a key usul dispute. The hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' was understood by the Ansar to mean that ghusl is only required when water (semen) is visible. The Hanafi school explains that their reasoning was not based on mafhum al-mukhalafa but on a linguistic feature: the lam of istighraq in the word 'al-ma''. This lesson unpacks that explanation and shows how specification by description does not automatically negate the ruling from other cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consequence of accepting mafhum al-mukhalafa
Recognize that if mafhum al-mukhalafa were valid, it would block qiyas on unspecified cases because qiyas cannot contradict a text. The Hanafi position avoids this problem.
Qiyas is a key tool for extending rulings; mafhum al-mukhalafa would severely restrict it.
2
Examine the hadith and the Ansar's interpretation
The Prophet ﷺ said 'al-ma' min al-ma'' (water from water). The Ansar understood that ghusl is only obligatory when water (semen) is emitted. The text clarifies their reasoning.
The Ansar did not rely on mafhum al-mukhalafa but on the lam of istighraq.
3
Analyze the Hanafi explanation using lam al-istighraq
The word 'al-ma' (water) with the definite article 'al-' for istighraq means every individual of water. Thus, the hadith implied that every ghusl janaba is tied to the existence of semen. The Ansar concluded that without semen, no ghusl.
This is a linguistic interpretation, not a logical implication of negation.
4
Understand the evidence of insal from al-taqa' al-khitanayn
The Hanafi response solves the objection: When there is no visible semen but the circumcised parts meet (al-taqa' al-khitanayn), that is evidence of insal (emission). Since insal is established, ghusl becomes obligatory.
Thus, the ruling is not based on the description 'water' alone but on the evidence of emission.
5
See the analogy with the rukhsah of travel
Just as the concession of qasr prayer and not fasting is tied to travel (the cause), not to actual hardship, here the cause of ghusl is emission, which can be proven by evidence (al-taqa' al-khitanayn).
This shows that the description is not the exclusive cause.

مخالف ہے جو متبادر الی اهل العرف ہے ۔ ولتكثير الفائدہ یہ دوسری وجہ ہے مفہوم مخالفتہ کے اعتبار کرنے کی حاصل یہ کہ مفہوم مخالفتہ کے اعتبار کرنے میں تکثیر فائدہ ہے یعنی وصف مذکور پر حکم ثابت کرنا اور اس کے انتفاء پر انتظار حکم کرنا اس میں فائدہ کثیر ہے بنسبت اس کے که صرف وصف مذکور بر حکم ثابت کیا جائے اور بس اسی پر اکتفا کیا جائے اور تکثیر فائدہ موجب ہے کہ اسے ترجیح حاصل ہونی چاہئے ۔ ولانه لو لم تكن فيه تلك الفائدة الخير تيسرى وجه ہے اس کی کہ تخصیص با لوصف نفی حکم از ما عداہ پر دلالت کرتی ہے حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ اگر تخصیص بالوصف نفی حکم از ما عدا الوصف پر دال نہ ہو تو اس سے یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ ماعدا الوصف میں بھی حکم ثابت ہوگا تو پھر وصف کے ذکر نے میں کوئی فائدہ نہ ہوا تو اس صورت میں ذکر و صف ترجیح بلا مرج ہوگا کیونکہ جو مرجحات ماقبل میں مذکور ہوتے ہیں خروج مخرج العادۃ وغیرہ وہ تو ہیں نہیں پھر اس وصف کے ذکر کے لئے کوئی فائدہ مرجمہ موجود نہ ہوا یہ بلغار کی کلام میں بھی نہیں ہو سکتا باری تعالیٰ کی کلام میں کیسے ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک وصف بلا فائدہ ذکر کی جائے ۔ ولان مثل هذا الكلام يدلى الخ اس جیسی کلام سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جہاں ایک موصوف بالصفہ پر حکم کیا جائے تو وہ دال ہوتی ہے کہ یہی وصف علتہ برائے حکم ہے جیسے فی الابل السائمہ زکوۃ یہ تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ وصف سائمہ علہ ہے برائے وجوب زكوة فينعدم الحكم عند عدم الوصف كييونكہ انتفاء علیہ کے ساتھ معلول منتفی ہو جاتا ہے ۔ وعندنا لا يدل یعنی ہمارے نزدیک تخصیص بالوصف نفی حکم عما عدا الوصف پر دال نہیں ہے۔
It is not indicative of the opposite because if the opposite implication were valid, then the text would negate by way of opposite implication, and then establishing the ruling by qiyas on what is other than the specified would not be correct, because qiyas that contradicts the text has no validity. And they understood that from 'water from water' - this is the answer to that reasoning. Summary: The Ansar's understanding that ghusl is not obligatory was not by way of opposite implication, but because the word 'al-masa' (water) with the lam of istighraq meant that every instance of ghusl from janaba is obligatory due to semen, so they thought that when semen is not apparent, ghusl is not required. Then 'ghayr an al-ma' is an answer to an objection: when the lam is for istighraq, then the meaning is that all instances of ghusl janaba occur when semen exists, but when there is al-taqa' al-khitanayn without existence of semen, then ghusl should not be obligatory. The answer is that ghusl without water (semen) is not established, but the existence of semen is sometimes established visually and sometimes by indication, and al-taqa' al-khitanayn is evidence of insal (emission), and insal is a subtle matter, so the ruling is established by the evidence of insal, and the evidence of insal is al-taqa' al-khitanayn; wherever this evidence exists, ghusl becomes obligatory. And from this, like the concession (rukhsah) of qasr prayer and leaving fast was based on hardship, the evidence of hardship was made as travel; wherever travel occurs, this concession is established whether actual hardship exists or not. And 'minhu' i.e. from the opposite implication - this is the predicate (khabar muqaddam), 'hazihi al-mas'ala' is the subject (mubtada mu'akhkhar). And that matter is: 'Specifying a thing by description indicates negation of the ruling from what is other than it' according to al-Shafi'i. That specification indicates that according to the Shafi'is, the ruling is negated from what is other than the description, i.e., wherever this description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not established. And we say: This phrase's syntactic state is clarified in two ways: one as already written, the second is that 'minhu' is the predicate and its subject should not be 'hazihi al-mas'ala' but rather the subject is the word 'takhsis al-shay' and 'minhu' is its predicate. And his saying 'yadullu' is the predicate of a deleted subject, i.e., 'huwa' referring back to 'takhsis al-shay'. And his saying 'amma 'adahu' i.e., other than that description, and the meaning is that the ruling is negated from that thing without that description, i.e., wherever this description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not established, like Allah's saying 'min fatayatikum al-mu'minat' - He specified the permissibility of marriage to those slave girls who are believers. So according to them, marriage is not valid with those slave girls who are not believers, and 'fatayat' means female slaves. For validity (li al-sarf), these are the proofs regarding the validity of opposite implication on the place of description that the Shafi'i scholars present. The conclusion is that from specification by description, common custom understands that the ruling is confined to that description. For example in the statement 'al-insan al-tawil la yatir' - this is evidence establishing the mentioned custom. Therefore it is said that what is understood from it is what we mentioned, i.e., the opposite implication we mentioned is what is mentally perceived, i.e., the tall man does not fly, but the non-tall flies. And because of this, it is said that the rational people consider it ugly; the reason is only that in this statement, the negation of flying is attributed to the man with the description 'tall'. If he says 'A man, whether tall or non-tall, does not fly', then rational people would not consider it ugly. So it is known that the ugliness is only because it implies that the non-tall man flies; this is the opposite implication that is mentally perceived by people of custom. And for increasing benefit (takthir al-fa'ida) - this is the second reason for considering opposite implication valid. The conclusion is that considering opposite implication has great benefit: establishing the ruling on the mentioned description and negating the ruling upon its absence yields greater benefit compared to only establishing the ruling on the mentioned description and stopping there. And increasing benefit necessitates that it should be given preference. And because if there were not that benefit, then another face: specification by description indicates negation from what is other than it. The conclusion is that if specification by description did not indicate negation from what is other than the description, then it would necessitate that the ruling is also established in what is other than the description, so there would be no benefit in mentioning the description. In that case, mentioning the description would be preference without a preferrer, because the preferred factors mentioned earlier like coming in the customary manner etc. are not present, so no beneficial preferred exists for mentioning this description. This cannot be in the speech of a mortal, how can it be in the speech of Allah Almighty that a description is mentioned without benefit? And because speech like this indicates that the description is the cause ('illa) for the ruling, like 'fi al-ibil al-sa'ima zakah' - this requires that the description 'sa'ima' is the cause for the obligation of zakah, so the ruling is absent when the description is absent, just as the effect is absent with the absence of the cause. But according to us (Hanafis), it does not indicate - i.e., specification by description does not indicate negation of the ruling from what is other than the description.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the famous usul issue of mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication), specifically regarding specification by description (takhsis bi al-wasf). The text begins by explaining a key consequence: if mafhum al-mukhalafa were accepted, then any specification would negate the ruling for all other unspecified cases, making qiyas (analogy) on those cases invalid because qiyas cannot contradict the text. The author then revisits the well-known hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' (water from water) where the Ansar understood that ghusl is not obligatory unless semen is visibly emitted. The text clarifies that their understanding was not based on mafhum al-mukhalafa but on the lam of istighraq in the word 'al-ma'', implying that every instance of ghusl is linked to semen. The answer to this is that while ghusl is typically proven by visible semen, it can also be proven by indication (dalala) — here, the meeting of the two circumcised parts (al-taqa' al-khitanayn) is accepted as evidence of insal (emission), thus establishing ghusl. This is compared to the rukhsah of travel: although the concession (qasr, not fasting) is based on hardship, the legal cause is travel itself, irrespective of actual hardship. The main dispute is then introduced: the Shafi'i principle that 'specifying a thing by description indicates negation of the ruling from what is other than it'. The Shafi'is cite the Quranic verse 'min fatayatikum al-mu'minat' (from your believing slave girls) to argue that marriage is only permitted with believing slave girls, not others. The Hanafi position (stated at the end) is that specification by description does not indicate negation of the ruling from what is other than that description ('indana la yadull'). The text then presents the Shafi'i four proofs for mafhum al-mukhalafa: (1) customary usage ('urf) — e.g., the statement 'the tall man does not fly' implies that non-tall men do fly, and rational people find it absurd to include non-tall in the negation; (2) increasing benefit (takthir al-fa'ida) — it provides more information; (3) if it did not indicate negation, mentioning the description would be pointless, which is impossible in divine speech; (4) such speech indicates that the description is the 'illa (cause) for the ruling, as in 'fi al-ibil al-sa'ima zakah' — the description 'sa'ima' is the cause, so zakah is not due on non-sa'ima camels. The Hanafi school rejects all these arguments, maintaining that specification by description does not automatically negate the ruling for other descriptions; the ruling may apply to other descriptions through other evidence.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implication that the ruling is restricted to the description mentioned, and negated for what is other than that description.
لام استغراق (lam al-istighraq): The definite article 'al-' used to indicate that the word encompasses all individuals of its kind.
التقاء الختانين (al-taqa' al-khitanayn): The meeting of the two circumcised parts (male and female) during intercourse, which is evidence of insal (emission).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi explanation in this lesson, why did the Ansar think that ghusl is not obligatory unless water (semen) is visible?
A) They relied on mafhum al-mukhalafa from the description 'water'.
B) They misunderstood the hadith because the word 'al-ma' has lam al-istighraq, implying ghusl is tied to water.
C) They rejected the hadith altogether.
D) They used qiyas on a similar case.

Key Takeaway
Specification by description does not automatically negate the ruling; the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' is explained by lam al-istighraq, and ghusl can be proven by evidence of insal like al-taqa' al-khitanayn.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Four Shafi'i Proofs for Mafhum al-Mukhalafa and the Hanafi Response
Presents the four Shafi'i proofs for mafhum al-mukhalafa and the Hanafi rejection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four Shafi'i proofs for the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa in specification by description and state the Hanafi response to each.

Core Idea
The Shafi'is cite custom, benefit, necessity, and cause; Hanafis reject each as inconclusive.

This lesson presents the four arguments the Shafi'i school uses to prove that specification by description indicates negation of the ruling for other cases (mafhum al-mukhalafa). The Hanafi school responds that these proofs are not decisive. Understanding this debate clarifies how each school approaches textual interpretation and the role of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four Shafi'i proofs
List the four proofs: (1) customary usage ('urf) - e.g., 'the tall man does not fly'; (2) increasing benefit (takthir al-fa'ida) - mentioning a description adds information; (3) avoiding pointlessness - if it doesn't negate, why mention?; (4) description as cause ('illa) - e.g., 'al-ibil al-sa'ima' for zakah.
These proofs are presented in the passage as arguments for mafhum al-mukhalafa.
2
Analyze the first proof: customary usage
The Shafi'is argue that in common speech, saying 'the tall man does not fly' implies that non-tall men fly. Rational people find it absurd to include non-tall. The Hanafi response is that custom ('urf) is not a definitive proof; the Quran and Sunnah may override it.
The Hanafi school does not deny the custom but says it can be overridden by other evidence.
3
Analyze the second proof: increasing benefit
The Shafi'is argue that mentioning the description and negating the ruling for others provides more information (takthir al-fa'ida), which is a benefit. The Hanafi response is not explicitly given here but generally that benefit alone does not necessitate legal validity.
The Hanafi school may respond that the description could be mentioned for other reasons, like the most common case.
4
Analyze the third proof: avoiding pointlessness
If mentioning a description does not negate, then it is pointless, which cannot be in divine speech. The Hanafi response is that the description may be mentioned for reasons other than restriction, such as the most common occurrence, or to establish a cause that can also be proven otherwise.
The Hanafi school does not accept that every description is restrictive.
5
Analyze the fourth proof: description as cause
The Shafi'is argue that a description functions like an 'illa (cause), as in 'fi al-ibil al-sa'ima zakah' - the description 'sa'ima' indicates the cause, so zakah is only on pasturing camels. The Hanafi response is that the cause is not always established by mere mention; often it is established by other evidence or by qiyas.
The Hanafi school uses qiyas even when a description is present, provided there is a common cause.

عند عدم الوصف كييونكہ انتفاء علیہ کے ساتھ معلول منتفی ہو جاتا ہے ۔ وعندنا لا يدل یعنی ہمارے نزدیک تخصیص بالوصف نفی حکم عما عدا الوصف پر دال نہیں ہے۔
It is not indicative of the opposite because if the opposite implication were valid, then the text would negate by way of opposite implication, and then establishing the ruling by qiyas on what is other than the specified would not be correct, because qiyas that contradicts the text has no validity. And they understood that from 'water from water' - this is the answer to that reasoning. Summary: The Ansar's understanding that ghusl is not obligatory was not by way of opposite implication, but because the word 'al-masa' (water) with the lam of istighraq meant that every instance of ghusl from janaba is obligatory due to semen, so they thought that when semen is not apparent, ghusl is not required. Then 'ghayr an al-ma' is an answer to an objection: when the lam is for istighraq, then the meaning is that all instances of ghusl janaba occur when semen exists, but when there is al-taqa' al-khitanayn without existence of semen, then ghusl should not be obligatory. The answer is that ghusl without water (semen) is not established, but the existence of semen is sometimes established visually and sometimes by indication, and al-taqa' al-khitanayn is evidence of insal (emission), and insal is a subtle matter, so the ruling is established by the evidence of insal, and the evidence of insal is al-taqa' al-khitanayn; wherever this evidence exists, ghusl becomes obligatory. And from this, like the concession (rukhsah) of qasr prayer and leaving fast was based on hardship, the evidence of hardship was made as travel; wherever travel occurs, this concession is established whether actual hardship exists or not. And 'minhu' i.e. from the opposite implication - this is the predicate (khabar muqaddam), 'hazihi al-mas'ala' is the subject (mubtada mu'akhkhar). And that matter is: 'Specifying a thing by description indicates negation of the ruling from what is other than it' according to al-Shafi'i. That specification indicates that according to the Shafi'is, the ruling is negated from what is other than the description, i.e., wherever this description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not established. And we say: This phrase's syntactic state is clarified in two ways: one as already written, the second is that 'minhu' is the predicate and its subject should not be 'hazihi al-mas'ala' but rather the subject is the word 'takhsis al-shay' and 'minhu' is its predicate. And his saying 'yadullu' is the predicate of a deleted subject, i.e., 'huwa' referring back to 'takhsis al-shay'. And his saying 'amma 'adahu' i.e., other than that description, and the meaning is that the ruling is negated from that thing without that description, i.e., wherever this description is not present, the mentioned ruling is not established, like Allah's saying 'min fatayatikum al-mu'minat' - He specified the permissibility of marriage to those slave girls who are believers. So according to them, marriage is not valid with those slave girls who are not believers, and 'fatayat' means female slaves. For validity (li al-sarf), these are the proofs regarding the validity of opposite implication on the place of description that the Shafi'i scholars present. The conclusion is that from specification by description, common custom understands that the ruling is confined to that description. For example in the statement 'al-insan al-tawil la yatir' - this is evidence establishing the mentioned custom. Therefore it is said that what is understood from it is what we mentioned, i.e., the opposite implication we mentioned is what is mentally perceived, i.e., the tall man does not fly, but the non-tall flies. And because of this, it is said that the rational people consider it ugly; the reason is only that in this statement, the negation of flying is attributed to the man with the description 'tall'. If he says 'A man, whether tall or non-tall, does not fly', then rational people would not consider it ugly. So it is known that the ugliness is only because it implies that the non-tall man flies; this is the opposite implication that is mentally perceived by people of custom. And for increasing benefit (takthir al-fa'ida) - this is the second reason for considering opposite implication valid. The conclusion is that considering opposite implication has great benefit: establishing the ruling on the mentioned description and negating the ruling upon its absence yields greater benefit compared to only establishing the ruling on the mentioned description and stopping there. And increasing benefit necessitates that it should be given preference. And because if there were not that benefit, then another face: specification by description indicates negation from what is other than it. The conclusion is that if specification by description did not indicate negation from what is other than the description, then it would necessitate that the ruling is also established in what is other than the description, so there would be no benefit in mentioning the description. In that case, mentioning the description would be preference without a preferrer, because the preferred factors mentioned earlier like coming in the customary manner etc. are not present, so no beneficial preferred exists for mentioning this description. This cannot be in the speech of a mortal, how can it be in the speech of Allah Almighty that a description is mentioned without benefit? And because speech like this indicates that the description is the cause ('illa) for the ruling, like 'fi al-ibil al-sa'ima zakah' - this requires that the description 'sa'ima' is the cause for the obligation of zakah, so the ruling is absent when the description is absent, just as the effect is absent with the absence of the cause. But according to us (Hanafis), it does not indicate - i.e., specification by description does not indicate negation of the ruling from what is other than the description.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on the famous usul issue of mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication), specifically regarding specification by description (takhsis bi al-wasf). The text begins by explaining a key consequence: if mafhum al-mukhalafa were accepted, then any specification would negate the ruling for all other unspecified cases, making qiyas (analogy) on those cases invalid because qiyas cannot contradict the text. The author then revisits the well-known hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'' (water from water) where the Ansar understood that ghusl is not obligatory unless semen is visibly emitted. The text clarifies that their understanding was not based on mafhum al-mukhalafa but on the lam of istighraq in the word 'al-ma'', implying that every instance of ghusl is linked to semen. The answer to this is that while ghusl is typically proven by visible semen, it can also be proven by indication (dalala) — here, the meeting of the two circumcised parts (al-taqa' al-khitanayn) is accepted as evidence of insal (emission), thus establishing ghusl. This is compared to the rukhsah of travel: although the concession (qasr, not fasting) is based on hardship, the legal cause is travel itself, irrespective of actual hardship. The main dispute is then introduced: the Shafi'i principle that 'specifying a thing by description indicates negation of the ruling from what is other than it'. The Shafi'is cite the Quranic verse 'min fatayatikum al-mu'minat' (from your believing slave girls) to argue that marriage is only permitted with believing slave girls, not others. The Hanafi position (stated at the end) is that specification by description does not indicate negation of the ruling from what is other than that description ('indana la yadull'). The text then presents the Shafi'i four proofs for mafhum al-mukhalafa: (1) customary usage ('urf) — e.g., the statement 'the tall man does not fly' implies that non-tall men do fly, and rational people find it absurd to include non-tall in the negation; (2) increasing benefit (takthir al-fa'ida) — it provides more information; (3) if it did not indicate negation, mentioning the description would be pointless, which is impossible in divine speech; (4) such speech indicates that the description is the 'illa (cause) for the ruling, as in 'fi al-ibil al-sa'ima zakah' — the description 'sa'ima' is the cause, so zakah is not due on non-sa'ima camels. The Hanafi school rejects all these arguments, maintaining that specification by description does not automatically negate the ruling for other descriptions; the ruling may apply to other descriptions through other evidence.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The implication that the ruling is restricted to the description mentioned, and negated for what is other than that description.
تخصیص بالوصف (takhsis bi al-wasf): Specifying a ruling by attaching a description (e.g., 'believing slave girls') rather than a general category.
علة ('illa): The effective cause or rationale for a ruling. In usul, the 'illa is used to extend rulings via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, what is the main reason they reject the Shafi'i fourth proof (description as 'illa)?
A) They agree that description is the cause but still allow qiyas.
B) They argue that the description alone does not establish the cause; other evidence is needed.
C) They reject the example 'al-ibil al-sa'ima' as weak.
D) They accept mafhum al-mukhalafa but only for Quranic verses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects all four Shafi'i proofs for mafhum al-mukhalafa, maintaining that specification by description does not automatically negate the ruling for other cases.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Debate on Mafhum Mukhalafa: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents Shafi'i proofs for mafhum mukhalafa and Hanafi refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Shafi'i arguments for mafhum mukhalafa via takhsis bil wasf, explain the Hanafi refutation that reasons for specification are not limited, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf in a concrete example.

Core Idea
Specification by description does not necessarily negate the ruling for other cases; many reasons for specification exist beyond indicating a cause.

In this usul dispute, the Shafi'i school argues that when a ruling is attached to a specific description, common custom understands that the ruling applies only to that description and is negated for others. The Hanafi school counters that the reasons for mentioning a description are not limited to negation—they may include definition, praise, blame, or emphasis. This lesson presents the Shafi'i proofs, the Hanafi refutation, and the practical consequences of adopting either position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
The core issue is whether specifying a ruling by a description (takhsis bil wasf) implies that the ruling is negated for cases lacking that description (mafhum mukhalafa).
The Shafi'is generally accept this implication; the Hanafis reject it as a default.
2
List the Shafi'i proofs
The Shafi'is present four main proofs: common custom ('urf), increased benefit (kathrat al-fa'idah), avoidance of redundancy (otherwise the description would be pointless), and analogy to causal language (where the description acts like an 'illa).
Each proof is discussed in the text with examples like 'the tall man does not fly' and 'in grazing camels, zakat is due'.
3
Examine the Hanafi refutation
The Hanafis argue that reasons for specification are not limited to the four Shafi'i conditions; description may serve definition (as for a body's dimensions), praise, blame, emphasis, or other purposes, none of which necessitate negation.
The text gives the example of 'الجسم الطويل العريض العميق متحيز' where the description is for definition, not negation.
4
Apply the dispute to an example
Consider 'في الإبل السائمة زكاة'. For Shafi'is, the description 'grazing' negates zakat from non-grazing camels. For Hanafis, the description may have another purpose, so zakat may still be due if other evidence indicates.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf: a real difference in fiqh rulings.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that in any text with a descriptive condition, Shafi'is will automatically exclude non-described cases, while Hanafis will require external evidence for exclusion.
The Hanafi position is more cautious, preserving generality unless specification is proven.

The reasons for the validity of the concept of opposite meaning (mafhum mukhalafa) which the Shafi'is present. The summary is that specification by description ('takhsis bil wasf') is understood by common custom ('urf 'amm') to negate the ruling when the description is absent. For example, in the statement 'The tall man does not fly', the common custom understands that the non-tall man flies. And this is why rational people consider this statement ugly (i.e., it implies something false). For increasing benefit: i.e., affirming the ruling for the described case and negating it for others brings greater benefit than simply affirming it for the described case alone. And if the description did not indicate negation of the ruling from other than the described, then the mention of the description would be without benefit, leading to preference without a preferred (tarjeeh bila murajjah). And also such speech indicates that the description is the cause ('illa) for the ruling, as in 'In grazing camels, zakat is due' implying that grazing is the cause, so when the cause is absent, the effect is absent. According to us (Hanafis), specification by description does not indicate negation of the ruling from other than the description. Because the reasons for specification are not limited to those mentioned. Indeed, I know that the proponents of mafhum mukhalafa mention conditions: that the specification does not come out of the usual mode of speech (kharaja 'an makhraj al-'adah), is not in response to a question, does not occur in an incident, the speaker knows the listener is ignorant of the specific ruling, and the specification is not based on that. They confined the reasons for specification to these four. If these four are not present, then the reason for specification is only to negate the ruling from other than the specification. I say: the reasons for specification are not limited to those mentioned. For example, the statement 'a body that is long, wide, deep, occupies space' – none of the four reasons exist, yet according to them mafhum mukhalafa would apply, but it cannot because if specification indicated negation, then a body without these three dimensions would not occupy space, which is impossible since no body exists without them. The description is only for definition and to reveal its essence. And sometimes a description is brought for praise or blame. And such cases, negation of the ruling from other than the description is not intended even though the four reasons are not present. Also for emphasis, like 'the recurring yesterday does not return' – the description is only for emphasis. And other reasons. In any case, specification...
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over the validity of 'mafhum mukhalafa' (concept of opposite meaning) in cases of specification by description (takhsis bil wasf). The Shafi'is argue that when the Lawgiver mentions a description alongside a ruling, the default custom ('urf) indicates that the ruling applies only to that description and is negated for others. They support this by: (1) rational custom: e.g., 'the tall man does not fly' is understood to mean non-tall men fly, otherwise the statement would be trivial; (2) benefit: affirming the ruling for the described and negating for others brings more benefit than just affirming for the described; (3) if the description had no effect, it would be redundant, which is impermissible in divine speech; (4) similarity to causal language: e.g., 'in grazing camels, zakat is due' indicates that grazing is the cause, so when absent, zakat is not due. The Hanafi response (presented here) is that specification by description does not necessarily negate the ruling from other descriptions, because the reasons for mentioning a description are not limited to indicating negation. There are many possible reasons: to define (like the dimensions of a body), to praise or blame, to emphasize, etc. In such cases, the four conditions set by the Shafi'is (not used in usual mode, not in answer to a question, not in an incident, speaker knows listener ignorant) are absent, yet negation does not follow. For example, 'a long, wide, deep body occupies space' — here the description cannot negate that shorter bodies occupy space because all bodies have these dimensions. So the Hanafi position is that mafhum mukhalafa is not a reliable indicator unless proven by external evidence. The passage affirms the Hanafi usul principle that the general rule (al-'amm) remains general until evidence specifies it.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The inferred meaning that the ruling is negated for cases other than the one explicitly mentioned, particularly when a description is attached to the ruling.
تخصيص بالوصف (takhsis bil wasf): Specifying a ruling by mentioning a particular description or attribute along with it.
موجبات التخصيص (mujibat al-takhsis): The reasons or causes that necessitate specification, i.e., why a particular description is mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, why does the description 'long, wide, deep' for a body not negate the ruling of occupying space from other bodies?
A) Because the description is not relevant to the ruling.
B) Because the description is meant for definition since no body can exist without these dimensions.
C) Because the ruling applies only to bodies with those dimensions.
D) Because the description was used for praise.

Key Takeaway
Specification by description does not automatically imply negation; the Hanafi position holds that other reasons for specification must be considered, making mafhum mukhalafa unreliable without supporting evidence.

Hanafi Defense of Mafhum al-Mukhalafa via Takhsis bi al-Wasf
Refuting objections to Hanafi acceptance of mafhum al-mukhalafa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle to distinguish between genuine mafhum al-mukhalafa and alternative explanations (sukut fi maqam al-hajah, shubhah) in cases of specification by description.

Core Idea
Hanafis accept mafhum al-mukhalafa only when the description is not superfluous and silence is not in a place of need.

This passage addresses a common objection: that Hanafis contradict their own usul by using mafhum al-mukhalafa in certain cases. The commentator defends the Hanafi position by analyzing two illustrative examples—one about lineage, one about testimony—showing that the apparent use of mafhum is actually explained by other principles. By the end, you will see how Hanafis navigate this nuanced issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and the two cases presented
The objectors claim Hanafis rely on mafhum al-mukhalafa in two cases: (1) a slave owner claiming only his eldest child, implying others are not his; (2) witnesses limiting testimony to a specific land, implying heirs elsewhere.
These cases are chosen to test the Hanafi stance.
2
Analyze the first case using Hanafi principles
The commentator explains that the negation of lineage for the younger children is not due to mafhum but due to two factors: (a) the master's silence in a place of need (sukut fi maqam al-hajah) indicates denial; (b) lineage requires an explicit claim (da'wah), which he did not make.
The condition of multiple wombs ensures the children are not automatically linked via umm walad.
3
Analyze the second case using Hanafi principles
The witnesses' mention of a specific land is superfluous (la hajata ilayh), so it creates only a shubhah (doubt) of mafhum. Hanafis do not deny that shubhah can affect rulings, but they do not consider it as strong proof. Imam Abu Hanifah accepts the testimony because it is impossible to know heirs in all lands—silence here is not in a place of need.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad reject due to shubhah.
4
Extract the Hanafi usul principle
The Hanafi position is that mafhum al-mukhalafa is not automatically binding. It can be negated by alternative explanations: silence in a place of need, the superfluous nature of the description, or the impossibility of full knowledge.
This refutes the claim that Hanafis contradict themselves.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i approach
Shafi'is would accept mafhum al-mukhalafa directly, making the negation of ruling from the specification alone. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is seen in the acceptance/rejection of testimony in the second case.
Hanafis avoid relying on mafhum unless the context clearly demands it.

عادہ یہی ہے کہ مومن مرد مومنہ عورت سے نکاح کرتا ہے اور جہاں وصف خارج مخرج العادۃ تھی شوافع وہاں مفہوم مخالف کو معتبر نہیں سمجھتے تھے تو یہاں اپنے مسلک کا خلاف کر رہے ہیں۔ تم اورد مستلقین یہ دو مسئلے پیش کئے گئے ہیں جن سے تو ھم ہوتا تھا کہ احناف بھی قائل ہیں کہ تخصیص بالوصف نفی حکم عبا عدا الوصف پر دال ہے۔ مصنف نے رفع تو ھم کی خاطر انھیں پیش کیا ۔ نقال ولا یلزم علینا یعنی ایک شخص کی لونڈی تین بچے مختلف بطون میں جنتی ہے مختلف بطون سے مراد یہ ہے کہ بین الواردین چھ ماہ یا اس سے زیادہ کا فاصلہ ہو ، فقال المولى الاكبر منی تو مولی دعوی کرتا ہے اور کہتا ہے کہ ولد اکبر مجھ سے ہے فانه نفی الاخیرین تو اس دعوی کے ساتھ اس نے اخیرین کے نسب کی نفی کہ دی ہے اور بظاہر اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس نے اپنے دعوی میں والد کے ساتھ اکبر کی وصف لگائی ہے اور جن میں اکبر کی وصف نہیں ہے ان سے نفی نسب اس لئے ہو رہی ہے کہ ان میں وصف اکبر موجود نہیں ہے تو یہ نفی وصف پر نفی حکم ہو رہا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ تخصیص بالوصف نفی حکم عماعدا الوصف پر دال ہوتی ہے یہی مفہوم مخالفہ ہے جو احناف نے یہاں معتبر سمجھا ہے اس کا جواب دیا۔ لا یلزم علینا یعنی یہ اشکال ہمارے اوپر لازم نہیں آنا لان هذا ليس لتخصيصة يد لا يلزم علینا کی دلیل ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ نفی اخیرین اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ تخصیص نفی حکم ما عداہ پر دال ہے جبل لان بلکہ اس لئے ہے کہ سکوت مقام حاجتہ میں بیان ہو جاتا ہے یعنی اگر ولد اس سے ہوتا تو اس کے لئے بیان یعنی دعوۃ نسب ضروری ہوتا ہے جب اس نے اس دعوۃ سے سکوت اختیار کر لیا ہے تو یہ سکوت بیان ہو گا اس امر کا کہ یہ ولدین میرے نہیں ہیں ۔ دایضا یہ دوسری وجہ ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اخیرین کا نسب اس لئے منتفی ہوا ہے کہ ثبوت نسب کے لئے دعوۃ ضروری شرط ہے جب اس نے ان کے متعلق دعوی نہیں کیا تو اس بنا پر نسب منتفی ہو رہا ہے۔ لالانہ انتظار نسب کی یہ وجہ نہیں ہے کہ بطور مفہوم مخالف کے وہ نفی کر رہا ہے۔
وانما قال فی بطون مختلفة یعنی بطون مختلفہ کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ اگر ان بچوں کی پیدائش ایک بطن میں ہے تو پھر ایک ولد کے دعوۃ نسب کرنے سے یہ جمیع کے متعلق دعوہ ہو جاتا ہے پھر جمیع ولدان کا نسب ثابت ہو جائیگا اور بطن واحد سے مراد یہ ہے بین الولد ین فصل سنہ اشھر سے کم ہو ۔ لا يقال لاحاجة الى البیان خلاصہ اس سوال کا یہ ہے کہ اخیرین میں بیان اور دعوی نسب کی حاجت ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ لونڈی ولد اول جو اکبر ہے اس کے ساتھ ام ولد ہو چکی ہے ۔ نیثبت نسب الاخيرین کیونکہ لونڈی جب ایک بار اُم ولد ہو جائے تو اس کے بعد جو بچے پیدا ہوں ان کا نسب مولی سے بغیر دعوۃ کے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اخیرین میں دعوہ کی ضرورت نہیں ۔ بلاد حوہ نسب ثابت ہو جائیگا لانه یہ جواب ہے سوال کا خلاصہ یہ کہ آپ کا یہ سوال نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ یہ اس وقت ہو سکتا تھا جب ولد اکبر کے متعلق دعوی نسب ولادة اخیرین سے قبل ہوتا ۔ اما مهنا فلا اس ہمارے مسئلہ میں ایسے نہیں ہے ۔ خان دعوۃ الاکبر کیونکہ اکبر کے متعلق دعوی نسب ہمارے اس مسئلہ میں ولادة اخیرین سے متاخر ہے فلايكون الاخيران پس دو آخری بچے ام ولد کے بچے نہیں ہیں بل هما ولد الامة بلکہ یہ دونوں لونڈی کے بیٹے ہیں فیحتاج لثبوت نسبهما الى الدعوة ان كا ثبوت نسب محتاج الى الدعوۃ ہے اس کے بغیر نسب ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا لفظ دعوة بكسر الدال ہے یہ اس دعوی کے ساتھ مختص ہے جو نسب کے متعلق ہو دلایلزم ہمارے اوپر دو مسئلوں کے ساتھ اشکال تھا ایک دعوہ کا یعنی دعوائے نسب کا وہ تو واضح ہو چکا ہے دوسرا شھادۃ کے متعلق تھا اس ثانی مسئلہ کو پیش کیا ولا یلزم سے اذا قال الشعود خلاصہ اس اشکال کا یہ ہے کہ جب شہود اپنی شہادت میں کہتے ہیں لا نعلم له وارثاً في امراض كذا لفظ فی ارض کذا یہ وارثاً کی صفہ ہے یعنی شاہد کہتے ہیں کہ ہم میت کیلئے کوئی ایسا وارث نہیں جانتے جو فلاں ارض اور علاقہ میں ہو لا تقبل الشهادة عندهما صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ شمارہ قبول نہیں ہوگی نصذا یہ شمارہ کی عدم قبولیت اس پر مبنی ہے کہ ان التخصيص یعنی جو فی ارض کذا کی تخصیص واقع ہوئی ہے دال علی ما قلتا یہ اسی مفہوم مخالفہ پر دال ہے جو ہم کہتے ہیں یعنی نفی الحکم عما عدا التخصیص کیونکہ اس کلام سے یہ مفہوم ہوتا کہ شعور اس میت کا وارث جانتے ہیں جو اس ارض کے علاوہ دوسری ارض یعنی دوسرے علاقہ میں موجود ہے اس بنا پران کی شھادۃ مقبول نہیں ہوئی اور یہ ہی مفہوم مخالفہ ہے۔ لان الشاهد یہ لا یلزم کی دلیل ہے یعنی ہمارے اوپر یہ اشکال لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ لما ذكر ما لاحاجة اليه جاء شبهة چونکہ شاہد نے جو ارض كذا " کا لفظ ذکر کیا ہے یہ زائد از ضرورت اور بلا حاجتہ اور بے فائدہ ہے البتہ اس کی بنیاد پر صرف شبه مفهوم مخالف کا ہو سکتا ہے ونحن لا نتفى الشبهة هم تخصيص بالوصف میں نفى الحكم عما عداہ کے شبہ کی نفی نہیں کرتے تو جب عما عدا الوصف سے نفی حکم کا شبہ پیدا ہوا تو اس کے ساتھ شھادۃ رد ہو سکتی ہے اور شھادۃ کی عدم قبولیت کے لئے یہ شعر کافی ہے ۔ ولاحاجة الى الدلالة اس کی ضرورت نہیں ہے کہ نفی وصف کو نفی حکم پر دال ہونا تسلیم کیا جائے کما ھو مذھبكم وقال ابو حنيفة امام ابو حنیفہ " اس مسئلہ میں قبول شہادہ کے قائل ہیں وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ارض مذکورہ کے غیر سے انھوں نے جو سکوت اختیار کیا ہے یہ سکوت فی موضع الحاجہ نہیں کیونکہ دوسرے علاقہ کی معرفہ محال
It is the custom that a believing man marries a believing woman, and where the description is outside the custom, the Shafi'is do not consider mafhum mukhalafah valid, so here they contradict their own madhhab. Two issues were presented by the objectors from which there was doubt that the Hanafis also hold that takhsis bi al-wasf indicates negation of the ruling from other than the description. The author presented them to remove the doubt. He said: 'wa la yalzim alayna' i.e., a person's slave girl gives birth to three children in different wombs (different wombs means between the births there is a gap of six months or more). Then the master says, 'The eldest child is mine,' so with this claim he has negated the lineage of the latter two. Apparently, the reason is that he attached the description 'eldest' to his claim, and from those who do not have the description 'eldest', the negation of lineage occurs because the description 'eldest' is not present in them. So this is a negation of ruling based on negation of description. Thus it is known that takhsis bi al-wasf indicates negation of ruling from other than the description. This is the mafhum mukhalafah that the Hanafis consider valid here. He responded: 'la yalzim alayna' i.e., this objection does not apply to us. The proof of 'la yalzim alayna' is that the negation of the latter two is not because takhsis indicates negation of ruling from other than it, but rather because silence in a place of need is an explanation. That is, if the child was from him, then explanation (i.e., claiming lineage) would be necessary. When he remained silent about that claim, then this silence is an explanation that these two children are not from me. Also, the second reason is that the lineage of the latter two is negated because for establishing lineage, a claim is a necessary condition. When he did not claim regarding them, on this basis lineage is negated. It is not because he is negating by way of mafhum mukhalafah. And he said 'in different wombs' meaning the condition of different wombs is attached because if the births were in one womb, then claiming lineage for one child would be a claim for all, and the lineage of all children would be established. One womb means the interval between the births is less than a year. Do not say that there is no need for explanation: the summary of this question is that there is no need for explanation and claim of lineage for the latter two because the slave girl has become umm walad with the first child who is the eldest. The lineage of the latter two is established because when a slave girl becomes umm walad once, then the children born after that have their lineage established from the master without claim. Therefore, the latter two do not need a claim. He responded: This is the answer to the question. Its summary is that your question cannot stand because it could only be if the claim of lineage for the eldest was before the birth of the latter two. But here, in our case, it is not so. The claim of the eldest is after the birth of the latter two, so the latter two are not children of umm walad, but rather they are children of the slave girl. Therefore, establishing their lineage requires a claim; without it, lineage cannot be established. The word 'da'wah' is with a kasra on the dal; it is specific to the claim related to lineage. So the objection does not apply to us. There were two objections: one about claim of lineage, which is clear; the second about testimony. He presented the second issue with 'wa la yalzim' from 'idha qala al-shuhud'. The summary of this objection is that when witnesses say in their testimony, 'We know no heir for him in such-and-such land' (the word 'in such-and-such land' is a description of 'heir'), i.e., the witnesses say, 'We do not know any heir for the deceased who is in such-and-such land.' The testimony is not accepted according to the Two. The non-acceptance of this testimony is based on the fact that the specification (i.e., the specification 'in such-and-such land') indicates what we say, i.e., mafhum mukhalafah, meaning negation of ruling from other than the specification, because from this speech the understanding is that the witnesses know an heir for the deceased who is in another land besides this land. On this basis, their testimony is not accepted. And this is the mafhum mukhalafah. 'Li anna al-shahid' is the proof of 'la yalzim'. That is, this objection does not apply to us because when the witness mentioned what is not needed, a doubt (shubhah) arises. Since the witness mentioned the word 'in such-and-such land', which is superfluous and without need, only a shubhah of mafhum mukhalaf can arise from it. And we do not deny the shubhah. In takhsis bi al-wasf, we do not negate the shubhah of negation of ruling from other than it. So when the shubhah of negation of ruling from other than the description arises, the testimony can be rejected, and for the non-acceptance of testimony, this shubhah is sufficient. There is no need for indication (that the negation of description indicates negation of ruling) as is your madhhab. And Abu Hanifah said: In this issue, he is of the opinion of acceptance of testimony. He says: Their silence about other than the mentioned land is not silence in a place of need, because knowledge of another land is impossible.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Hanafi position on mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite meaning) in the context of takhsis bi al-wasf (specification by description). The commentator addresses two objections raised by opponents (likely Shafi'is) who argue that the Hanafis, in certain cases, rely on mafhum al-mukhalafa, which they claim contradicts the Hanafi stance that mafhum al-mukhalafa is generally not valid. The first case involves a man who has a slave girl giving birth to three children in separate pregnancies (more than six months apart). He claims only the eldest is his. The opponents argue that this implies the other two are not his, which is a use of mafhum al-mukhalafa. The commentator responds that the negation of lineage for the latter two is not due to mafhum al-mukhalafa but because the man remained silent about them when he needed to speak (sukut fi maqam al-hajah), and silence in such a case is an indication of denial. Additionally, establishing lineage requires a specific claim (da'wah), which he did not make for the latter two. The passage also differentiates between births in one womb versus multiple wombs, and notes that if the claim for the eldest is made after the births of the others, the latter two are not considered children of umm walad. The second case involves witnesses testifying that they know no heir for the deceased in a specific land. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), such testimony is rejected because the specification of the land creates a mafhum mukhalafa that they know an heir elsewhere. The commentator responds that the mention of the land is superfluous (la hajata ilayh) and creates only a shubhah (doubt) of mafhum mukhalafa. Since the Hanafis do not deny that such a shubhah can affect rulings, the testimony may be rejected on that basis without admitting the full validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa. Imam Abu Hanifah, however, accepts the testimony because the silence about other lands is not in a place of need—it is impossible to know all heirs in all regions. This shows that Hanafis do not categorically reject mafhum al-mukhalafa; they consider it in cases where the description is not superfluous and the context indicates intent. The passage clarifies the nuanced Hanafi approach to this usul principle.

Key Terms
تخصیص بالوصف (takhsis bi al-wasf): Specification of a ruling by attaching a description to the subject; used to indicate that the ruling applies only to the described category.
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The opposite meaning derived from a conditional or descriptive statement, i.e., that the ruling applies only to the specified condition and its opposite is negated.
سکوت مقام حاجتہ (sukut fi maqam al-hajah): Silence in a situation where one is expected to speak; this silence is considered an indication of denial or negation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of the slave girl's children, why does the master's claim that the eldest is his negate the lineage of the latter two according to the Hanafi commentator?
A) Because mafhum al-mukhalafa requires it.
B) Because his silence about the latter two in a place of need indicates they are not his.
C) Because the latter two are not biologically related.
D) Because he explicitly denied them.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis distinguish between genuine mafhum al-mukhalafa and alternative explanations such as silence in need or superfluous description, maintaining a nuanced position.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Ta'liq bil-Shart: The Dispute on Negation of Ruling
Discusses whether absence of condition negates the ruling under ta'liq bil-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ta'liq bil-shart and apply the concept of adam asli to explain why absence of a condition does not automatically negate a ruling.

Core Idea
Absence of a condition does not automatically negate the ruling; the ruling remains under original non-existence unless the condition is a cause.

A key usul dispute concerns the logical implication of conditional clauses. When a ruling is linked to a condition, does the absence of that condition imply the ruling is void? Imam Shafi'i argued yes, but the Hanafi school distinguishes between conditions that are mere prerequisites and those that are actual causes. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of shart
Recognize that 'shart' can refer either to a condition external to the thing upon which it depends (e.g., wudu for prayer) or to a cause upon which the ruling is suspended.
The first type does not entail the existence of the thing; the second does.
2
Understand original non-existence (adam asli)
Grasp the Hanafi concept that when a cause is absent, the thing is simply non-existent in its original state (adam asli), not legally negated.
Contrast with legal non-existence (adam shar'i) which requires a proof.
3
Apply to the wudu-prayer example
Consider prayer without wudu: wudu is a condition (shart) for validity but not a cause. Absence of wudu does not mean prayer is legally negated; it means valid prayer does not exist (adam asli).
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.

ومن التعليق بالشرط اسی مفہوم مخالفہ میں سے تعلیق بالشرط ہے ۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک عدم شرط کیساتھ حکم منعدم ہو جائیگا ۔ عملاً بشرطیته یعنی اس کے شرط ہونے پر عمل کیا جائیگا۔ کیونکہ شرط اسے کہتے ہیں جس کے انتقام کے ساتھ حکم منتفی ہو جائے ، عندنا العدم لا يثبت به ہمارے نزدیک اس تعلیق بالشرط کے سبب حکم منعدم نہیں ہوتا۔ بل يبقى الحكم بلکہ حکم عدم اصلی کے تحت آجائیگا یعنی جب علہ وجود نہ ہو تو وہ شئی عدم اصلی کے تحت رہیگی یہی کہا جائیگا چونکہ اس کے موجود ہونیکی کی علتہ نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ معدوم ہے تو یہ عدم اصلی ہے عدم شرعی نہیں ہے۔ جیسے ہم تخصیص بالوصف کے مسئلہ میں ذکر کر آئے ہیں اور ثمرات اختلاف جو وہاں تھے وہی یہاں بھی ہوں گے ۔ لان الشرط یہ استدلال مذکور سے جواب دیا جارہا ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ شرط کا اطلاق مختلف معانی پر آتا ہے ایک یہ کہ شرط ایسے امر کو کہا جاتا ہے جو خارج عن الشئی ہو اور مہبی شنی اس پر موقوف ہو لیکن اس پر وہ شئی مرتب نہ ہو یعنی وہ شرط اس شئی کے وجود کا سبب نہ ہو جیسے وجود مسبب مترتب على وجود السبب ہوتا ہے نہ ہو. کالوضوء للصلوۃ جیسے وضو شرط صلواۃ ہے کہ صحت صلوۃ اس پر موقوف ہے لیکن یہ وجود صلوۃ کے لئے سبب نہیں ہے اور نہ وجود صلوۃ وجود وضو پر مرتب ہے۔ وقد يقال للمعلق بہ اور شرط کبھی ایسے امر کو کہا جاتا ہے جس کے ساتھ حکم کو معلق کر دیا جاتا ہے اور یہ سبب للحکم ہوتی ہے اور حکم اس شرط کے وجود پر مترتب تو ہوتا ہے لیکن اس پر موقوف اور متوقف
And from ta'liq bil-shart: it is from mafhum mukhalafah. According to Imam Shafi'i, with the absence of the condition, the ruling becomes non-existent, acting upon its conditionality. Because a condition is something by whose removal the ruling is negated. According to us (Hanafis), the absence does not establish [negation] by means of ta'liq bil-shart. Rather, the ruling remains under original non-existence. That is, when the cause does not exist, the thing remains in original non-existence. This is said: since there is no cause for its existence, it is non-existent, and this is original non-existence, not legal non-existence. As we mentioned in the issue of takhsis by description, and the consequences of difference that were there will also be here. Because 'shart' (condition) has different meanings. One is that a condition is something external to the thing upon which the thing is dependent, but the thing is not entailed by it; the existence of the effect is not contingent upon the existence of the condition like wudu for prayer. Wudu is a condition for prayer in that the validity of prayer depends on it, but it is not a cause for the existence of prayer, and the existence of prayer is not entailed by the existence of wudu. And sometimes the term is used for that upon which a ruling is suspended (mu'allaq bih); it is a cause for the ruling, and the ruling is entailed by its existence, but it is also dependent on it.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on whether the absence of a condition in a conditional statement (ta'liq bil-shart) logically implies the negation of the ruling. Imam Shafi'i holds that if a condition is explicitly stated, its absence means the ruling does not apply. The Hanafi position distinguishes between two types of conditions: (1) a condition that is external and necessary but not a cause (like wudu for prayer), and (2) a condition that is a cause and upon which the ruling is suspended. In the first type, the absence of condition does not automatically negate the ruling; the ruling remains under the principle of original non-existence (adam asli). The Hanafis argue that without a cause, the thing is simply non-existent in itself, not that it is legally negated. This aligns with the earlier discussion on takhsis by description. The difference has practical consequences (thamarat al-ikhtilaf) in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
تعلیق بالشرط (ta'liq bil-shart): Suspending a ruling upon the existence of a condition.
عدم اصلی (adam asli): Original non-existence; the inherent state of a thing before any cause brings it into existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view on ta'liq bil-shart, what happens to the ruling when the condition is absent?
A) The ruling is legally negated.
B) The ruling remains under original non-existence.
C) The ruling becomes invalid.
D) The ruling is suspended until the condition appears.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the absence of a condition in a conditional statement does not automatically negate the ruling; the ruling instead remains under original non-existence unless the condition is a cause.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Conditional Clauses
Usul dispute on conditional clauses (Hanafi vs Shafi'i)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on conditional clauses (shart) and apply the Hanafi principle that condition and consequence form a single speech to derive the ruling on marrying a slave woman when one can afford a free woman.

Core Idea
Conditional clauses do not imply negation when the condition is absent; the Hanafi school treats condition and consequence as one speech.

This passage tackles a foundational usul dispute: does a conditional statement (shart) imply that the ruling is negated when the condition is absent (mafhum mukhalafa)? The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i over a single Quranic verse (4:25) reveals deeper principles about how legal language functions. By working through this dispute, you will sharpen your ability to identify when a text is ‘speaking’ and when it is merely silent – a skill critical for istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two meanings of shart
The author first separates shart as a prerequisite for existence (e.g., wudu for prayer) from shart as a mere connector in a conditional sentence. Only the second type is in dispute. Understand that when the condition is a prerequisite, its absence naturally negates the conditioned; but when it is a connector, absence does not necessarily negate.
This distinction is key to the entire argument.
2
Examine the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the conditional
Imam Shafi'i holds that the consequence (mashrut) alone is a complete speech carrying the ruling; the condition merely restricts that ruling to a specific scenario, and its absence implies negation of the ruling. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that condition and consequence together form one single speech, which only establishes the ruling upon the condition's occurrence and remains silent about other scenarios.
This difference is driven by whether one accepts mafhum mukhalafa as a valid proof.
3
Apply the positions to Quran 4:25
The verse permits marrying a slave woman only for those who cannot afford a free woman. Shafi'i: since the condition (inability) is stated, when ability exists the permission is negated → marrying a slave woman becomes prohibited. Hanafi: the verse grants permission only when inability exists; it is silent about ability, so the general permissibility from Quran 4:24 remains → marrying a slave woman remains permissible.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the usul dispute.
4
Trace the foundational principle
The dispute reduces to one usul question: is the ruling carried by the consequence alone (Shafi'i) or by the combination of condition and consequence (Hanafi)? The author illustrates with the conditional divorce example: 'If you enter, you are divorced' – according to Hanafi, 'you are divorced' without the condition is not a complete speech, so divorce can still occur through other means (e.g., a direct pronouncement).
This shows that the Hanafi view is more flexible and does not restrict the ruling to the conditional scenario alone.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The text clearly sides with the Hanafi position ('at us' عندنا). The author explains that the Shafi'i reliance on mafhum mukhalafa is insufficient because the Quranic condition does not indicate negation. Thus the operative rule for Hanafi fatwa is that conditional clauses do not negate the ruling when the condition is absent, unless there is additional evidence.
This principle applies across many fiqh chapters, including divorce, sales, and contracts.

Source Text

جو معلق بالشرط
It is not so, for the condition in the sense of that external matter on which the existence [of the conditioned] depends – what you mentioned means the conditioned is negated by its negation, like wudu which was a condition for the validity of prayer, so with the negation of wudu the validity of prayer is negated. But the negation of the conditioned with the negation of the condition in this sense is not a legal ruling; rather, the invalidity of prayer when wudu is absent is an original non-existence, i.e., the prerequisites for the validity of prayer are not present, so validity of prayer did not come into existence. Nevertheless, the absence of wudu indicates the invalidity of prayer, not in the second sense, i.e., the condition in the second sense upon which the conditioned was consequent but not dependent – such a condition's negation does not indicate the negation of the conditioned. Because the conditioned can exist without the condition, as in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced': despite the absence of entry, divorce can occur due to another cause, e.g., the woman did not enter the house but the husband uttered 'You are divorced' unconditionally, so divorce occurs even though entry did not happen. Thus it becomes known that the negation of the condition cannot be evidence for the negation of the conditioned. So His statement 'And whoever among you cannot afford [to marry] free believing women...' (Quran 4:25). According to Imam Shafi'i, when one has the means to marry a free woman, marrying a slave woman is not permissible. Permissible according to us – and according to us, even at the time of having means for a free woman, marrying a slave woman is permissible. Allah said: 'And whoever among you cannot afford...' In this verse, the permissibility of marrying slave women is made conditional on the condition that one does not have power over marrying a free woman. If power over marrying a free woman is established, then according to Imam Shafi'i, marrying a slave woman is not permissible because he adheres to the opposite implication (mafhum mukhalafa). So according to Imam Shafi'i, the implication of this verse will become a specification (takhsis) for the general verse 'Lawful for you are all beyond those mentioned' (Quran 4:24), because that verse generally requires that every woman except prohibited ones is valid for marriage, whether free or slave, so in every case it is permissible. So this verse 'Whoever cannot afford' would specify its generality, that marrying a slave woman is valid only in this specific circumstance, otherwise not. According to us, since 'whoever cannot afford' does not indicate the impermissibility of marrying a slave woman, it can neither be a specifier nor an abrogator for 'Lawful for you are all beyond those mentioned'. And this difference traces back to this foundational dispute: whether the ruling is solely in the consequence and the condition is a restriction for it, like an adverb or circumstantial qualifier, so then the consequence becomes the complete speech carrying the ruling, and the condition becomes merely a restriction; or whether the ruling is neither in the consequence nor in the condition, but rather between the condition and the consequence, and the combination of condition and consequence is a single speech, merely indicating the connection of the consequence to the condition, i.e., the establishment of the consequence on the supposition of the condition's establishment, and it does not indicate the negation of the consequence when the condition is negated. Imam Shafi'i holds the first opinion, and Imam Abu Hanifa holds the second. The author has made this clear. Indeed, al-Shafi'i considered the conditioned alone, i.e., Imam Shafi'i considers only the conditioned, not the condition. The intent is that Imam Shafi'i considers the conditioned alone as perfect speech carrying the ruling, and in this complete speech he does not consider the condition, but considers it only as like a restriction or adverbial qualifier. For he makes the ruling obligatory [by the consequence]. So according to this view, the conditioned – i.e., the consequence – becomes a ruling-maker on all suppositions. Thus conditional suspension restricts this ruling to a specific supposition. And its absence – i.e., of the ruling – on suppositions other than that specific one would negate the ruling. So for him, the conditional suspension has effect in the negation of the ruling. For example, the permissibility of marrying a slave woman has been restricted to the specific supposition of inability to marry a free woman. When ability exists, the condition 'cannot afford' is absent, so the permissibility of marrying a free woman is also negated. But we consider the conditioned along with the condition – i.e., we consider the conditioned with the condition. According to us, the conditioned and the condition together form a single speech which carries the ruling. So the condition is one part and the conditioned is another part of the speech; when these two parts combine, the single speech is complete. It makes the ruling obligatory only on one supposition, which is the occurrence of the condition, and is silent about other suppositions. So the conditioned without the condition is only one part of the speech, not a complete speech, like the word 'you' in 'You are divorced'. For our statement 'You are divorced if you enter the house' – the phrase 'You are divorced' which is the conditioned, when isolated from the condition, its status is like the word 'you' in 'You are divorced', because it is not a complete speech; rather, the combination of condition and consequence is a single speech. So it is not a ruling-maker on all suppositions as al-Shafi'i claimed; rather, it makes the ruling only on one supposition, i.e., on the supposition of the condition's occurrence. So based on this principle – i.e., since Imam Shafi'i considers the conditioned without the condition, and we consider the conditioned with the condition – under this foundational rule, the suspended upon condition is suspended upon the condition, like in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced', the phrase 'you are divorced' is suspended upon the condition.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the interpretation of conditional clauses (shart) in legal texts. The core issue is whether a conditional statement implies that the ruling (hukm) exists only when the condition is present and is negated when the condition is absent (mafhum mukhalafa), or whether the conditional merely establishes a connection without implying negation. The author first explains two meanings of 'shart': the first meaning is a condition that is a prerequisite for existence (e.g., wudu for prayer), where absence of the condition necessarily means absence of the conditioned. The second meaning is a condition in a conditional statement (like 'if you enter, you are divorced'), where the absence of the condition does not necessarily negate the conditioned, because the conditioned could occur through other means. The passage then applies this to the Quranic verse about marrying slave women (4:25). Imam Shafi'i, who adheres to mafhum mukhalafa, argues that when one has the means to marry a free woman (i.e., the condition 'cannot afford' is absent), marrying a slave woman is impermissible. The Hanafi position, held by Imam Abu Hanifa, is that the verse only permits marrying slave women when the condition of inability is present, but does not prohibit it when the condition is absent; thus it remains permissible in all cases. The reason for this difference is a foundational usul principle: Shafi'i considers the consequence (mashrut) alone as the complete speech carrying the ruling, with the condition serving only as a restriction; Hanafi considers the condition and consequence together as forming a single speech that carries the ruling only for the scenario where the condition occurs, remaining silent about other scenarios. The author clarifies that this principle affects not only this verse but all conditional legal statements, such as conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The passage is a clear exposition of how different usul principles lead to different fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that may be either a prerequisite for existence (like wudu for prayer) or a clause in a conditional statement that links the consequence to a specific circumstance.
مفہوم مخالفتہ (mafhūm mukhālafa): The implication that when a condition or attribute is mentioned, the ruling is negated when that condition or attribute is absent.
مشروط (mashrūṭ): The conditioned thing or consequence in a conditional statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, why does the absence of the condition in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' not necessarily negate the divorce?
A) Because the condition is not a legal cause; divorce can occur through other means.
B) Because the consequence alone is a complete speech that carries the ruling.
C) Because the verse 'Lawful for you are all beyond those mentioned' abrogates the conditional verse.
D) Because the condition 'entry' is a prerequisite for existence, like wudu.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a conditional clause does not imply the negation of the ruling when the condition is absent; the condition and consequence form a single speech that only speaks about the scenario where the condition occurs.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Dispute on Ta'liq: When Does a Suspended Cause Become Effective?
Explains the dispute on ta'liq between Hanafi and Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on suspended causes, explain the Hanafi rule that the cause is not contracted before the condition, and apply this to cases of divorce, vows, and expiations.

Core Idea
A cause is not a cause until all its parts are present — condition is part of the cause.

This passage unpacks a core disagreement in usul al-fiqh: does a suspended legal cause (sabab mu'allaq) come into existence at the moment the condition is uttered, or only when the condition occurs? The answer determines the validity of many common legal statements, from conditional divorces to vows and oaths. Understanding this difference sharpens your ability to trace how each school constructs 'cause' and 'condition'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The dispute is: when a ruling is suspended on a condition (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced'), does the cause (the utterance) become effective immediately, or only when the condition exists?
This is a question about the definition of sabab.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its rationale
Imam Shafi'i holds that the cause is contracted at the moment of utterance; the condition only delays the ruling. The passage explains that the conditional statement necessitates the ruling in all scenarios, but suspension restricts it. This leads to the view that in 'if you enter, you are divorced,' the divorce cause exists immediately.
Shafi'i considers the core utterance as the sabab; the shart is separate.
3
State the Hanafi position and its rationale
The Hanafi school insists that the cause is not contracted until the condition exists. The condition is part of the cause; without it, only a part exists, and a partial cause is no cause. Analogous to sale: offer alone is not a cause for ownership without acceptance.
Hanafis integrate the condition into the sabab itself.
4
Examine the branches: divorce, vow, oath
The passage applies the dispute to three areas. For divorce on ownership (e.g., 'if I marry you, you are divorced'), Shafi'i says the cause is contracted but void if ownership absent; Hanafi says no cause until ownership. For a suspended vow, Shafi'i allows hastening performance before the condition; Hanafi does not. For oath expiations, Shafi'i permits financial expiation before violation (cause is oath), but not bodily expiation; Hanafi rejects hastening altogether.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical rulings differ in each scenario.
5
Analyze the reasoning and tarjih
The Hanafi argument rests on the definition of sabab as that which leads to the hukm. Before the condition, it does not lead, so it is not a sabab. The Shafi'i view conflates existence with effect. The text clearly favors the Hanafi position, calling it 'us' (Hanafi) and referring to Shafi'i statements as 'a refutation'.
Note the use of first-person plural (عندنا) to indicate the Hanafi school.
