جائے۔
According to Imam Shafi'i, the cause [sabab] of the occurrence of divorce has already been contracted. However, the suspension (ta'liq) delays the ruling of the occurrence of divorce until the time of the existence of the condition. And this, based on what we mentioned, is the explanation of Imam Shafi'i's school: that according to him, the conditional statement without the condition necessitates the ruling in all scenarios, and the suspension restricts this ruling to a specific scenario and negates the ruling in other scenarios. So this negation is, according to him, a necessary implication (mafhum min al-nass). Thus he does not consider it a ruling in the Qur'an, since he believes in the specification (taqdir). So 'if you enter the house, you are divorced' — the ruling is not 'you are divorced' [absolutely]; rather, 'you are divorced' has become a firmly established cause. And the effect of the suspension is only to delay the ruling, because the suspension does not prevent the causality; the cause for the ruling exists, and the ruling is only delayed until the existence of the condition. Then: suspension of divorce and manumission on ownership — this is a branch of this. That the conditional [statement] suspended on a condition has its cause contracted and present according to him, i.e., according to Shafi'i, provided that ownership exists at the time of the existence of the cause, by consensus. If ownership does not exist at the time of the cause's existence, the cause becomes void. And the suspension of a contract on a cause — according to Imam Shafi'i, the suspended, i.e., the conditional, has become a cause for the ruling and is present. When one suspends divorce or manumission on ownership, e.g., saying to a foreign woman 'if I own you' or 'if I marry you, you are divorced,' or to a slave not owned by him 'if I own you, you are free,' then this suspension, according to him, is a completed and present cause. But at that time ownership does not exist. Therefore, according to him, such suspensions are void. Thus, later if that woman comes into his marriage or that slave comes into his ownership, divorce and manumission will not occur. It is permissible to hasten the suspended vow (nadhr mu'allaq). For example, a person says, 'If Allah heals this sick person, then I owe fasting three days.' If he fasts the three days before the patient's recovery, the vow is fulfilled because the suspended [phrase] has become a cause for obligation; however, the obligation of performance is delayed until the time of recovery. Hastening [the act] after the existence of the cause but before the obligation of performance is valid by consensus. Here, the performance of the vow is after the cause of obligation, so it is valid, just as a person who owns one nisab[?] and gives zakat before the lapse of a year is valid, because it is after the cause of obligation — the cause of obligation is ownership of nisab, which exists. Similarly, the vow is the cause of obligation, so performance after the suspended [condition] is valid because it is also after the cause. According to Shafi'i, expiations of the oath when they are financial — i.e., other than fasting, whether freeing a slave or feeding ten poor people or clothing them — if performed after the oath but before the violation, is valid according to Imam Shafi'i, because the oath is the cause of the obligation of expiation, and the violation is the cause of the obligation of performance. Since the very obligation [of expiation] comes from the oath, therefore performing the expiation before the violation is after the existence of the cause of obligation, so it is valid. Because financial [obligations] admit separation between the very obligation and the obligation of performance, like in sale: with the contract, the price becomes obligated in the liability, but the obligation of performance does not occur; rather, the obligation of performance is deferred to the seller's demand. Therefore, in financial expiations, separation between the very obligation and the obligation of performance is possible, so financial expiation before violation is valid. Contrary to bodily [obligations], like fasting: in that, separation and disconnection between the very obligation and the obligation of performance are not possible, so bodily expiation before violation is not valid because both the very obligation and the obligation of performance occur together with the violation. And as for his statement 'one of them is not separated from the other,' if it is said that in bodily worship separation between the very obligation and the obligation of performance is not possible, then it will come in the chapter [that] in bodily worship separation is possible. And according to us (Hanafis), the cause is not contracted except upon the existence of the condition. Because the cause is that which is a path to the ruling and leads to it, and before the existence of the condition it is not so, as we have established earlier from the principle: we consider the conditional [statement] together with the condition. Therefore it cannot necessitate occurrence without the condition, as we mentioned: the position of the consequence (jaza') is like the word 'you' in 'you are divorced.' So only one part of the cause exists, and with the existence of one part of the cause, the cause does not exist until all its parts exist. Just as sale does not become a cause for ownership with only the offer until acceptance exists, so here too it cannot be a cause for the ruling until the condition exists. So when the condition exists, at that moment the suspended [statement] becomes a cause for the ruling, and before the existence of the condition it cannot be a cause. Thus the ruling differs in the mentioned issues: according to us, the ruling will not be what it was according to Imam Shafi'i; rather, it will be the opposite ruling. And as for the oath that Imam Shafi'i considered a cause for the obligation of expiation, this is a refutation of it. The summary is that the contract of an oath is for the sake of fulfilling it, meaning the purpose of the oath is to fulfill it.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i on the core issue of whether a suspended cause (sabab mu'allaq) becomes effective before the condition exists. The author first explains Imam Shafi'i's position: in a conditional statement like 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' the cause of divorce (the utterance) is immediately contracted; the suspension merely delays the ruling until the condition. Thus, for Shafi'i, the cause exists even without the condition, but the ruling is postponed. This leads to the ruling that if the condition is never met, no divorce occurs, but if it is met, divorce is effective. He extends this to suspended divorce/manumission on ownership (e.g., saying to a stranger 'if I marry you, you are divorced'): Shafi'i says the cause is contracted, but since ownership does not exist at the time, the cause is void, so later marriage does not cause divorce. The passage then discusses suspended vows and oath expiations, showing how Shafi'i applies the same principle: the cause (vow or oath) is contracted, so performing the act before the condition/violation is valid for financial expiations but not bodily ones. Then the author presents the Hanafi position: the cause is not contracted until the condition exists. The reasoning is that a cause is only a valid path to the ruling when all its parts are present; the condition is an integral part of the cause. Therefore, before the condition, no cause exists. This results in opposite rulings in all discussed scenarios. For example, in the Hanafi view, the vow or oath is not a cause until the condition/violation occurs, so hastening the act is invalid. The passage concludes with a summary that the purpose of an oath is to fulfill it, not to create a cause for expiation.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal ruling (hukm) upon a condition (shart), such that the ruling is delayed until the condition occurs.
سبب (sabab): That which is a path to the ruling and leads to it; the effective cause whose existence gives rise to the ruling.
شرط (shart): A condition whose existence is necessary for the sabab to produce its effect. Not part of the sabab itself in Shafi'i; part of the sabab in Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a suspended cause (sabab mu'allaq) become effective?
A) At the moment of utterance, but the ruling is delayed.
B) Only upon the existence of the condition.
C) Never, unless the condition is explicitly stated in a specific form.
D) Only after the condition is fulfilled and a separate cause is created.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines sabab as including its condition; thus, a suspended cause does not exist until the condition occurs, a principle with far-reaching effects on divorce, vows, and expiations.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Words Conveying Hukm: Khabr, Insha', Amr, and Fi'l
Analyzes types of speech and the nature of command and act as sources of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khabr and insha', define amr with its conditions, and explain the dispute over whether 'amr' applies literally to acts, and the implications for deriving obligation from the Prophet's actions.

Core Idea
Amr is literally the command 'Do!' but some argue it also literally means the act, which would make the Prophet's actions obligatory.

This lesson breaks down the Hanafi classification of speech into report (khabr) and performative (insha'), with special attention to the command (amr) and the debate over its application to acts (fi'l). Understanding these linguistic categories is foundational for deriving rulings from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish khabr from insha'
Identify the criterion: khabr is susceptible to truth/falsehood; insha' is not. Note how the Sharia uses reports for emphasis.
The example Quran 2:233 uses report form to stress obligation.
2
Understand the rationale for reports
Explain mubalaghah: a report implies the action already exists, making the command more compelling to avoid attributing falsehood to the Lawgiver.
3
Define amr and its conditions
State the definition: the speaker's statement 'Do!' with superiority (isti'la). Exclude request (iltimas) and supplication (du'a). Recognize that nahy is the opposite.
Amr is only considered if from a superior.
4
Explore the dispute over applying 'amr' to acts
Majority of Hanafis: application to acts is metaphorical (majaz). Some scholars: it is literal (haqiqah), citing Quran 11:97 where 'amr' means 'act'.
The dispute hinges on whether a qarina (context) for metaphor exists.
5
Analyze the subsidiary ruling
If acts are literally amr, then the Prophet's actions indicate obligation (wujub) because amr indicates wujub. Evidence includes the hadith 'Pray as you have seen me praying'.
The minority view derives obligation from the Prophet's acts; the majority requires additional evidence.

الباب الثاني في افادتة الحكم الشرعي لفظ جو حکم شرعی یعنی وجوب اور حرمتہ و غیر معما کا افادہ کرتا ہے۔ یہ باب ثانی ان ہی اسحاث کے متعلق ہے اللفظ المفید لہ یعنی وہ لفظ جو افادہ حکم کرتا ہے . اما خبر یا وہ خبر ہوگا اگر وہ لفظ من حيث هو هو محتمل صدق و کذب ہو تو وہ خبر ہے من حیث ھو ھو سے مراد یہ ہے کہ لفظ کو من حيث اللفظ اور کلام کو من حیت کلام دیکھنا ہے اسی حیثیت سے وہ محتمل صدق و کذب ہو۔ مع قطع النظر عن العوارض یعنی عوارض اور دلائل خارجیہ سے قطع نظر مثلاً یہ نہیں دیکھنا کہ متکلم کون ہے اور مخبر صادق و مصدوق ہے صرف کلام محتمل صدق و کذب ہو یہ خبر ہے ۔ اوانشاء یا وہ لفظ مفید انشاء ہوگا اگر محتمل صدق و کذب نہ ہو . واخبار الشرع یعنی شریعت کسی حکم کو بصورت خبر ذکرے تو یہ نسبت انشاء کے زیادہ مؤکہ ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے والوالدات يرضعن اولاد ھن بجائے امر و انشاء کے جملہ خبریہ استعمال کیا گیا ہے ۔ لانه اول علی الوجود کیونکہ خبر وجود مخبر به پر قومی الدلالہ ہے گویا کہ مخبر بہ موجود ہو چکا ہے اور متکلم اس کی خبر دے رہا ہے اور انشاء اس قسم کے مفہوم سے خالی ہوتا ہے اس لئے خبر ثبوت حکم پر ادل ہے ۔ اعلم ان اخبار الشارع اصل یہ ہے کہ شارع احکام کے متعلق جو خبر دیتا ہے ۔ یراد به الامر مجازاً مجازا اس سے مراد امر ہوتا ہے لیکن صریح لفظ امر سے عدول الی الاخبار اس لئے کیا جاتا ہے کہ اخبار میں اگر مخه به موجود ہو تو کذب شارع لازم آئیگا اور امر میں اگر مامور بہ موجود نہ ہو تو کذب شارع لازم نہیں آتا ۔ فاذا اريد المبالغة جب مبالغه في وجود الحكم المامور بہ کا ارادہ ہو تو عدول الى لفظ الاخبا کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ متبعین شارع یہ برداشت نہیں کرتے کہ کذب منسوب الى الشارع ہو لہذا وہ ضرور اس مامور بہ کو وجود میں لانیکی پوری جدوجہد کریں گے واما الانشاء انشاء کی اگر چہ قسمیں بہت ہیں لیکن افادة حکم شرعی کے بارہ میں اس کے اقسام میں سے صرف امر اور نہی معتبر ہیں ۔ فالامر قول القائل استعلاء یعنی وائل اپنے آپ کو عالی اور بلند مقام سمجھ کر کہہ افعل خواہ وہ قائل في نفس الامر عالی ہو یا عالی نہ ہو تو اس کا قول افعل امر ہوگا استعلا کے لفظ کے ساتھ التماس جو علی طریق التاوی ہوتی ہے اور دعا جو علی طریق الخضوع من القائل ہوتی ہے ان سے احتراز کرنا مقصود ہے ۔ اور نہی قائل کے قول لا تفعل کو کہا جاتا ہے بشرطیکہ استعلاء ہو . والامر حقيقة الخ یعنی امر کا اطلاق اسی قول افعل پر علی سبیل الحقیقۃ ہے بالاتفاق او بر فعل پر اطلاق امر جمہور کے نزدیک علی سبیل المجاز، وعند البعض اور بعض کے نزدیک فعل پر اطلاق امر علی سبیل الحقیقۃ ہے یعنی فعل بھی حقیقتا امر ہے۔ نمایدل على انه الخ یعنی فعل چونکہ ان بعض کے نزدیک حقیقتاً امر ہے اب جو دلائل اس پر دال ہیں کہ امر برائے ایجاب ہوتا ہے وہی دال ہیں کہ فعل رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم برائے ایجاب ہے کیونکہ آپ کا فعل حقیقتاً امر ہے اور برامر برائے ایجاب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا فعل رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم برائے ایجاب ہے ۔ واحتجوا علی الاصل یعنی اصل دعوی کہ امر حقیقت ہے فی الفعل یعنی فعل پر امر کا اطلاق حقیقی ہے اس پر وہ احتجاج کرتے ہیں بقولہ تعالیٰ دما امر فرعون برشید یہاں امر سے مراد فعل ہے کیونکہ رشید صفت فعل ہوتی ہے صفت قول نہیں ہے تو یہاں امر کا اطلاق علی الفعل ہے اور اطلاق بھی علی سبیل الحقیقہ ہے کیونکہ مجاز کا کوئی قرینہ موجود نہیں ہے ۔ وعلی الفرع اور فرع پر یعنی اس پر کہ فعل رسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم برائے ایجاب ہے فرع اس لئے کہا کہ یہ مسئلہ اسی پر متفرع ہے کہ فعل حقیقتا امر ہو اس فرع پر ان کا احتجاج بقولہ علیہ السلام ہے صلوا کما رایتمونی اصلی یوم الخندق رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے اربع صلوات قضا ہوگئی تھیں پھر ان کی قضا بالترتیب کی تھی تو رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم
The second chapter on conveying the legal ruling: The word that conveys the legal ruling, i.e., obligation, prohibition, etc. This second chapter concerns the topics of the word that conveys the ruling. Either it is a report (khabr) if the word in and of itself is susceptible to truth and falsehood; then it is a report. By 'in and of itself' it is meant that the word is considered in terms of its wording, and speech in terms of its nature; from that aspect it is susceptible to truth and falsehood, disregarding external circumstances and external evidence. For example, we do not consider who the speaker is or whether the informant is truthful; simply if the speech is susceptible to truth and falsehood, it is a report. Or it is a performative (insha') if it is not susceptible to truth and falsehood. And the reports of the Sharia: when Sharia mentions a ruling in the form of a report, it is more emphatic than a performative. Like (Quran 2:233) 'And mothers shall suckle their children' which is used in the form of a report instead of a command or performative. Because report has strong indication of the existence of the reported matter, as if the reported matter already exists and the speaker is reporting it, while performative lacks this meaning. Therefore report is more indicative of the establishment of the ruling. Know that the reports of the Lawgiver: the principle is that when the Lawgiver gives a report concerning rulings, it is meant as a command metaphorically. The shift from the explicit word of command to the report is done for exaggeration in emphasizing the existence of the commanded act, because the followers of the Lawgiver cannot tolerate falsehood being attributed to the Lawgiver, so they will strive to bring the commanded act into existence. As for performative, although it has many types, for conveying legal rulings only command (amr) and prohibition (nahy) are considered. So amr is the statement of a speaker with superiority (isti'la), i.e., the speaker says 'Do!' considering himself higher, whether or not he is actually superior. The word 'isti'la' is used to exclude request (iltimas) which is based on interpretation, and supplication (du'a) which is based on humility of the speaker. And nahy is the speaker's statement 'Do not do!' on condition of superiority. And command is, in reality, applied to the statement 'Do!' by consensus. As for applying the word command to the act, according to the majority it is metaphorical. But according to some, the application of command to the act is real, i.e., the act is also truly a command. That which indicates that command is for obligation also indicates that the act of the Messenger, peace be upon him, is for obligation, because his act is truly a command, and command is for obligation. Therefore the act of the Messenger is for obligation. And they argue for the original claim (that command is real in act) with His saying, high is He, 'What the command of Pharaoh was not right' (Quran 11:97). Here 'amr' means act, because 'right' (رشید) is an attribute of an act, not of speech. So here 'amr' is applied to act, and it is applied in the real sense because there is no context indicating metaphor. And for the subsidiary claim (that the Prophet's act is for obligation) they argue with his saying, peace be upon him, 'Pray as you have seen me praying' on the day of the trench. The Messenger missed four prayers, then he made them up in order.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is from the second chapter of a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work, focusing on how words convey legal rulings (hukm shar'i). The author distinguishes between khabr (declarative speech) and insha' (performative speech). Khabr is susceptible to truth/falsehood; insha' is not. The Sharia often uses khabr forms to express commands for emphasis, because khabr implies that the action already exists, making it more forceful. For example, Quran 2:233 uses 'mothers shall suckle' rather than 'suckle!' to stress the obligation. The shift from explicit command to report is for mubalaghah (exaggeration) in emphasizing the commanded act.

The author then defines amr (command) as the speaker's statement 'Do!' with superiority, excluding request and supplication. Nahy is 'Do not!' with superiority. The literal application of 'amr' is to the utterance 'Do!' by consensus. However, some scholars hold that the word 'amr' can be applied literally to the act (fi'l) itself, citing Quran 11:97 where 'amr' means 'affair/act'. If act is truly amr, then the Prophet's actions (fi'l) would indicate obligation (wujub), since amr indicates obligation. The passage provides arguments: the Quranic verse where 'amr' is used for act, and the hadith 'Pray as you have seen me praying' which was a command to pray like him, implying obligation. The text notes that the Prophet's own practice of making up missed prayers in order shows the obligation of order.

Key Terms
خبر (khabr): Speech that is susceptible to truth or falsehood, considered in itself.
انشاء (insha'): Speech that is not susceptible to truth or falsehood; it brings about a legal effect.
امر (amr): The command 'Do!' uttered with superiority.
فعل (fi'l): Act; some scholars argue it is literally called 'amr' when performed by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Sharia sometimes use the form of a report (khabr) instead of a command (amr) for obligations?
A) To allow for interpretation that it is not obligatory.
B) To emphasize the obligation by implying the action already exists.
C) Because the Prophet disliked direct commands.
D) To make the ruling easier to follow.

Key Takeaway
The form of a word (khabr or insha') affects the strength of the ruling, and the literal application of 'amr' to acts is disputed, impacting how we derive obligation from the Prophet's actions.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Is the Prophet's Action a Command? The Hanafi Position on 'Amr and Fi'l
Debate whether the Prophet's actions are literal commands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the literal meaning of 'amr, identify the opponent's proofs from Quran and Hadith, and apply the Hanafi linguistic arguments to evaluate when the Prophet's actions carry obligatory force.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that 'amr is literal only for verbal commands; applying it to actions is metaphorical, preserving linguistic consistency.

This lesson explores a fundamental debate in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: does the word 'amr (command) apply literally to actions, or only to speech? The answer has direct consequences for the legal force of the Prophet's actions. The Hanafi school insists that 'amr is literal only for the verbal formula 'if'al', and any application to action is metaphorical. This position is defended with strong linguistic and logical arguments, which we will examine in detail.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that the Hanafi school holds 'amr to be literal only for the verbal command (qawl), not for actions (fi'l). Applying 'amr to actions is metaphorical (majaz).
2
Identify the opponent's view and proofs
The opponent argues that action is literally 'amr, citing Quran 11:97 and the Prophet's action of praying in sequence on the Day of the Trench.
Quran 11:97: 'What amr of Pharaoh was not right' – they claim 'right' describes actions. Hadith: 'Pray as you have seen me praying' – obligation of sequence deduced.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Quranic proof
The Hanafis offer two interpretations: either 'amr in the verse is metaphorical (cause applied to effect) or it refers to Pharaoh's speech and the description is transferred metaphorically.
No literal application or homonymy is needed.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Hadith proof
The Prophet's action alone does not constitute a command; the obligation may derive from the verbal command in the hadith, not the action itself.
Additional evidence is required to establish obligation from action.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: For Hanafis, not every prophetic action indicates obligation; for opponents, every action is obligatory.
Crucial for distinguishing sunnah from wajib in the Prophet's practice.

کا فعل اسم ہے اس کام کا جو شخص سے صادر ہوا ثانی دلیل جو پیش کی گئی اس سے صرف یہ ظاہر ہوتا کہ امر جو مصدر ہے اس کا اطلاق حقیقی فعل پر نہیں ہوتا جو یہ بھی مصدر ہے اس دلیل سے یہ ثابت نہیں ہوا کہ امر جو اسم ہے اس کا اطلاق حقیقی اس فعل پر نہیں ہے جو اسم ہے اور بمعنی شان کے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ پہلی دلیل عام ہے اور وہی امر کا اطلاق حقیقی علی الفعل کو روکتی ہے۔ و تسميته امرا مجازاً خصم نے جو احتجاح وما امر فرعون برشید سے کیا تھا کہ یہاں امر کا اطلاق بغرینہ رشید فعل پر ہے تو یہ اس کا جواب ہے کہ فعل کو یہاں تسمیہ امر مجازا کیا گیا ہے یعنی اطلاق امر علی الفعل اس مقام پر اطلاق مجازی ہے. اذا الفعل یہ علاقہ مجاز ہے حاصل یہ کہ فعل امر قولی کے ساتھ واجب ہو جاتا ہے تو امر سبب ہوا اور فعل مسبب ہوا لہذا اطلاق اسم السبب على المسبب کیا گیا ہے جو کہ علاقہ مجاز ہے تو اس استدلال کا ایک اور جواب بھی دیا گیا ہے کہ یہاں امر سے مراد فعل فرعون نہیں ہے بلکہ قول مراد ہے اور اس پر اس کا ما تقدم یعنی فاتبعوا امر فرعون دال ہے کہ کیونکہ اس کا معنی یہی ہے اطاعوا فرعون فیما امر ہم بہ اور وما امر فرعون سے مراد امر قولی ہے البتہ قول کی وصف جو رشید کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے یہ مجاز ہے وصف الشئ بوصف صاحبہ ہے جیسے الاسلوب الحکیم میں ہے یعنی چونکہ فرعون رشید نہیں تھا اس لئے اس کا قول بھی رشید نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ سلمنا انه حقيقة فيه اى فى الفعل چونکہ یہ بات کہ امر حقیقہ ہے فی الفعل یہ ایک لغوی مبحث تھا جس کا نقل عن ائمۃ اللغۃ اور شیوع استعمال کے ساتھ ممکن تھا تو مصنف اسے تسلیم کر کے
And insha is devoid of this type of meaning, therefore khabar is stronger in establishing a ruling. Know that the fundamental principle regarding the reports of the Lawgiver is that when He gives a report about rulings, it is intended as a command metaphorically. However, turning away from the explicit word of command to reports is done because in reports, if the commanded thing does not exist, a lie would be attributed to the Lawgiver, whereas in a command, if the commanded thing does not exist, a lie is not necessary. So when exaggeration is intended — exaggeration in the existence of the commanded ruling — then one turns to the word of report, because the followers of the Lawgiver cannot bear that a lie be attributed to the Lawgiver; hence they will strive fully to bring that commanded thing into existence. As for insha, although it has many types, only command and prohibition are valid for conveying a legal ruling. So amr is the speaker's statement 'do' with superiority, meaning the speaker, considering himself high and lofty, says 'do', whether in reality the speaker is high or not; his saying 'do' would be a command. The request that is figurative and supplication that involves humility on the part of the speaker are excluded. And nahy is the speaker's statement 'do not do' with the condition of superiority. And 'amr in reality' means the application of 'amr to the statement 'do' is literal by consensus. But applying 'amr to an action is metaphorical according to the majority, and according to some, applying 'amr to an action is literal, meaning action is also literally amr. So the evidence that indicates that amr is for obligation — that same evidence indicates that the action of the Messenger, peace be upon him, is for obligation, because his action is literally amr, and amr is for obligation. Therefore the action of the Messenger is for obligation. And they argued for the original claim that amr is literal in action by His statement 'What amr of Pharaoh was not right' — here by 'amr' action is meant because 'right' is a description of action, not of speech. So here 'amr' is applied to action, and the application is literal because there is no context of metaphor. And for the branch — that the action of the Messenger is for obligation — they argued with his saying: 'Pray as you have seen me praying on the Day of the Trench.' The Messenger had four prayers made up, then he made them up in order. So obligation of sequence was established by his action, thus the action of the Messenger is for obligation. We said: It is not literal in action. The summary: The application of 'amr to action is not literal, otherwise 'amr would have two meanings, and the application of 'amr to speech is literal by consensus, so then the word 'amr would be homonymous between two meanings, and homonymy is contrary to the principle. Indeed, using a word in its literal and metaphorical senses is preferable to homonymy. And because when a person does an action and does not say 'do', it is linguistically and customarily correct to say he did not command (lam ya'mur). If action were literally 'amr, then when he did the action, negating 'amr would not be correct, but it is correct. And from this evidence it appears that the word 'amr is a verbal noun from amara ya'muru meaning to command; similarly fi'l (action) is a verbal noun from fa'ala yaf'alu meaning to do. And also that 'amr is a noun for the word 'if'al', and fi'l is a noun for the action that emanates from a person. The second evidence only shows that 'amr as a verbal noun is not applied literally to action which is also a verbal noun; it does not prove that 'amr as a noun is not applied literally to action which is a noun used in the sense of 'affair'. However, the first evidence is general and it prevents the literal application of 'amr to action. And calling it 'amr metaphorically — the opponent argued with 'What amr of Pharaoh was not right' that here 'amr is applied to action with the context of 'right', so this is its answer: action is here called 'amr metaphorically, i.e., the application of 'amr to action is metaphorical. Because the action becomes obligatory with a verbal command, so the command is the cause and the action is the effect, thus the name of the cause is applied to the effect, which is a metaphorical relationship. Another answer is also given: here 'amr does not mean the action of Pharaoh but speech, and the preceding verse 'So they followed the amr of Pharaoh' indicates that, because its meaning is 'they obeyed Pharaoh in what he commanded them', and 'What amr of Pharaoh' means the verbal command. However, describing the speech with 'right' is metaphorical, describing a thing with the description of its owner, like in the style of wisdom — because Pharaoh was not right, so his speech cannot be right. We concede that it is literal in action — since this matter of 'amr being literal in action was a linguistic discussion which could be transmitted from the imams of language and widespread usage, so the author accepts it and...
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether the term 'amr (command) is applied literally (haqiqah) to actions (fi'l) as opposed to speech (qawl). The author presents the view of the majority (jumhur) that 'amr is only literal when applied to the word 'if'al' (do), while applying it to an action is metaphorical (majaz). Some scholars, however, hold that action is literally called 'amr. The discussion has important implications for the evidentiary value of the Prophet's actions: if his actions are literally 'amr, then they carry the same obligatory force as a verbal command. The opponents argue that since the Prophet's action of praying in order on the Day of the Trench established obligation of sequence, his actions are binding. The Hanafi response offers two main arguments: (1) If 'amr were literal for both speech and action, the word would be homonymous (mushtarak), which is disfavored since using words in their original meaning and a metaphorical extension is preferable. (2) Linguistically, if someone performs an action without saying 'do', it is correct to say 'he did not command', which would be false if action were literally a command. The author also addresses the opponent's proof-text 'What amr of Pharaoh was not right' (Quran 11:97), explaining that 'amr there is applied to action metaphorically or alternatively refers to speech. The passage concludes by acknowledging that this is a linguistic matter, and the author concedes the possibility of literal application after citing linguistic authorities.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): The speaker's statement 'do' (if'al) with superiority (isti'la), whether the speaker is actually superior or not. It is a type of insha' (performative speech) that indicates obligation (wujub) in the Hanafi view.
الفعل (al-fi'l): An action performed by a person, distinct from speech. The debate is whether actions can be called 'amr (command) literally.
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): Literal usage of a word in its original meaning without metaphorical context.
المجاز (al-majaz): Figurative usage of a word for something related to its original meaning, with a contextual clue (qarinah).
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): Homonymy — a single word having multiple equally literal meanings. The text argues this is disfavored (khilaf al-asl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, why is the application of 'amr to actions considered metaphorical rather than literal?
A) Because the Quran does not use 'amr for actions.
B) Because if 'amr were literal for both speech and action, the word would become homonymous (mushtarak), which is disfavored, and linguistically one can say 'he did not command' of someone who acts without speaking.
C) Because the Prophet's actions are only recommended, not obligatory.
D) Because the majority of scholars hold that actions are not commands, so it is a matter of consensus (ijma).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'amr is literal only for the verbal command; applying it to actions is metaphorical, requiring additional evidence for obligation.

The Sixteen Meanings of the Imperative and the Tawaqquf Dispute
Enumeration of meanings of the imperative form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least fourteen meanings of the imperative form (صيغة افعل) and explain why Ibn Surayj (Shafi'i) advocated tawaqquf, contrasting it with the Hanafi default of obligation.

Core Idea
The imperative can indicate up to sixteen legal meanings; Hanafis default to obligation while Ibn Surayj suspends judgment.

This passage from the usul text enumerates the multiple possible meanings of the Arabic imperative form (صيغة افعل), ranging from obligation (الإيجاب) to wish (التمني). It also introduces a critical dispute: should we suspend judgment (التوقف) until contextual clues clarify which meaning is intended, as argued by the Shafi'i scholar Ibn Surayj? The Hanafis, on the other hand, generally hold that the imperative indicates obligation unless there is a clear contextual indicator (قرينة) to the contrary. Understanding this list and the dispute is essential for correctly interpreting commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute on tawaqquf
Notice the opening: Ibn Surayj argues for suspending judgment on the meaning of an imperative until context clarifies it. The Hanafis disagree, considering obligation the default.
This is a key ikhtilaf between the schools.
2
Memorize the list of meanings
Go through each of the fourteen enumerated meanings (the text claims sixteen but only fourteen are listed; two are missing). For each, note the example given in the passage.
Use the Arabic terms and examples for easier recall.
3
Group meanings by category
Some meanings convey similar ideas: obligation, recommendation, permission etc. Group them to see patterns (e.g., ibaha, ibaha?).
This helps with memorization and understanding.
4
Apply the dispute to a practical scenario
Imagine a command like 'أقيموا الصلاة' without context. Hanafi: it is obligatory. Ibn Surayj: suspend until context (like a prior obligation) is found.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Reflect on the usul principle
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that the original (الأصل) in commands is obligation. The other meanings are exceptions requiring evidence.
This principle guides Hanafi istinbat.

Then the author, after explaining the real meaning of the word amr, presents what is the actual usage of amr, i.e., the imperative form افعل, and what is its real meaning. He said that its effect (the resulting ruling) is suspension according to Ibn Surayj, who is from the Shafi'is, until it becomes clear what is meant by the usage of amr, because amr is used in different meanings, and they are approximately sixteen meanings, so without context one cannot be certain. These sixteen meanings are: (1) obligation like 'establish prayer', (2) recommendation like 'write them', (3) disciplinary instruction like 'eat from in front of you', (4) guidance like 'and seek witness' [Quran 2:282], (5) permission like 'eat', (6) warning like 'do what you will', (7) bestowal of favor like 'eat from what Allah has provided you', (8) honor like 'enter in peace', (9) challenge like 'bring a surah', (10) subjugation like 'be apes', (11) humiliation like 'taste, indeed you are the mighty, the noble', (12) equality like 'be patient or not', (13) supplication like 'O Allah forgive me', (14) wish like 'O long night, depart'.

Commentary
This passage lists fourteen distinct meanings of the imperative form (although the text claims sixteen, only fourteen are enumerated; possibly two are missing due to OCR). The author mentions that Ibn Surayj (a Shafi'i scholar) advocated tawaqquf (suspension of judgment) regarding the meaning of an imperative until contextual clues clarify which meaning is intended, due to the multiplicity of possible meanings. The Hanafis generally hold that the imperative is for obligation unless there is a context indicating otherwise, but they acknowledge the existence of other meanings. The list includes: obligation (ijab), recommendation (nadb), disciplinary instruction (ta'dib), guidance (irshad), permission (ibaha), warning (tahdid), bestowal of favor (imtinan), honor (ikram), challenge (ta'jiz), subjugation (tashkhir), humiliation (ihanat), equality (taswiya), supplication (du'a), and wish (tamanni). Each is illustrated with Quranic or Prophetic examples.

Key Terms
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment; waiting until contextual clues determine the meaning of an ambiguous term.
الإيجاب (al-ijab): Obligation; the primary meaning of amr according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imperative form (صيغة افعل) can bear up to sixteen different legal meanings; the Hanafi school defaults to obligation unless evidence shifts the meaning, while Ibn Surayj (Shafi'i) suspends judgment until context clarifies.

Refuting Tawaqquf: The Hanafi Argument from Nahy
Usul dispute: Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i tawaqquf stance on amr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi argument against tawaqquf using the analogy with nahy, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in interpreting Quranic commands.

Core Idea
If multiple meanings forced us to pause, we would have to pause for nahy too—but we don't.

A central dispute in usul al-fiqh is whether the imperative form (amr) has a default meaning or requires pause (tawaqquf) until contextual clues appear. The Shafi'i scholar Ibn Surayj argued for tawaqquf because amr can mean obligation, recommendation, permission, and more. The Hanafi school, however, rejects this, claiming it is inconsistent: prohibition (nahy) also has multiple meanings, yet no one pauses there. This lesson examines that argument and its practical consequences for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
Understand that the issue is whether the imperative form (sigha al-amr) automatically indicates obligation (wujub) or requires pausing before assigning any meaning. The Hanafi position is that the default is wujub unless a contextual clue (qarina) shifts it.
The opponent is Ibn Surayj (Shafi'i), who lists sixteen possible meanings of amr.
2
List the Sixteen Meanings of Amr
Review the meanings enumerated in the text: wujub, nadb, ta'dib, irshad, ibaha, tahdid, imtinan, ikram, ta'jiz, taskhir, ibanat, taswiya, du'a, tamanni, ihtiqar, takwin. Note how they range from obligation to creation.
The author uses abjad letters to list them; this shows the multiplicity that supposedly creates uncertainty.
3
Compare with Nahy
Observe that the author then lists multiple meanings for nahy: tahrim, karaha, tanzih, tahqir, bayan al-aqiba, ya's, irshad, shafaqa. The key point: nahy is just as polysemous as amr.
If tawaqquf were required for amr due to multiple meanings, consistency would demand it for nahy as well.
4
Extract the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi rebuttal is that no school pauses for nahy, so it is inconsistent to pause for amr. Additionally, the difference between requesting action (amr) and requesting abandonment (nahy) is intuitively clear. Therefore, the default must be obligation for amr and prohibition for nahy.
The text also notes that some argue nahy is essentially a command to desist, collapsing the distinction, but the author dismisses this as the difference is obvious.
5
Apply to a Fiqh Example
Consider the Quranic imperative 'Aqimu al-salah' (establish prayer). According to the Hanafi default, this is immediately obligatory. A Shafi'i following tawaqquf would require additional evidence to confirm it is obligatory rather than recommended.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in how rulings are derived from the Quran.

جیسے و استشهد را از اتبالعتم اس استشہاد کے ساتھ دنیاوی معاملہ درست رہتا ہے (ھ) الاباحة جیسے کلو کھاؤ یعنی یہ ایک جائز فعل ہے (3) التحدید یعنی التخويف والانذار جیسے اعملوا ما شئتم اور جیسے قل تمتع (ط) التعجز یعنی اظهار العجز یہ ظاہر کرتا کہ مخاطبین عاجز ہیں اسی عجز کو ظاہ کرتا مقصود ہوتا ہے جیسے فاتوا بسورة (منی) التسخیر یعنی یہ ظاہر کرنا کہ مخاطبین ہمارے حکم کے مسخر اور تابع ہیں جیسے ہم ان سے چاہیں ویسے ہوگا۔ انھیں سرتابی کی طاقت نہیں ہے جیسے کو نوا قردة (5) الا بانت یعنی تذلیل کسی کی ذلتہ اور رسوائی کو ظاہر کرنا جیسے ذق انك انت العزيز الكريم ريت النسوية یعنی جانبین برابر ہیں کسی میں کوئی نفع نہیں ہے جیسے اصبروا اولا تصبروا ) الدعا یعنی عاجزانہ طور پر درخواست پیش کرنا جیسے اللهم اغفرلی (ید) التمنی جیسے الا ايها الليل الطويل الا انجلى ية انجلی تمنی ہے مصائب کی رات بڑی لمبی ہوتی ہے گویا اس کے انجلا کی توقع نہیں ہوتی اس لئے میاں انجلی تمنی کے لئے ہے (یه ) الاحتقار جیسے القواما انتم ملقون یعنی سحر جو ساحرین بمقابلہ موسی علیہ السلام ظاہر کرنے کا ارادہ رکھتے تھے اسی کے متعلق القوا کا امر برائے احتقار ہے یعنی بمقابلہ معجزہ ساحرین کا سحر ایک حقیر اور معمولی چیز ہے اسی کو ظاہر کرنا احتقار ہے (یو) التکوین یعنی الایجاد ایک شئی کو عدم سے نکال کر وجود میں لانا جیسے كن فيكون قلنا لو وجب التوقف هذا اصحاب توقف نے جو دليل توقف پیش کی تھی یہ اس کا جواب ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر امر میں توقف اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کثیر معانی میں مستعمل ہے تو پھر نہی میں بھی توقف کرنا لازم ہے کیونکہ وہ بھی کثیر معانی میں مستعمل ہے۔ دھی اور معانی یہ ہیں التحریم جیسے لاتاكلوا الربوا سود خوری حرام ہے جو اس آیت کے ساتھ اس کو حرام کیا گیا ہے ۔ والکڑھتہ جیسے نہی عن الصلوۃ فی الارض المغصوبه. والتنزيه نحول تمنن تستكرة يعنى یعنی احسان اس بنا پر نہ کرنا چاہتے کہ محسن علیہ سے کثیر شی ملے گی اس کثرت کے طلب اور خواہش کے پیش نظر احسان نہیں ہونا چاہئے یہ صرف تنزہ ہے تحریم نہیں ہے اور نہ مکروہ تحریمی . والتحقیر یعنی ایک شتی کی حقائرہ ظاہر کرنا جیسے لاتمدن عینیک اس سے یہ ظاہر کر مقصود ہے کہ کفار و مشرکین کے پاس جو دولت ہے یہ ایک حقیر اور معمولی شتی ہے ادھر نگاہ نہیں کرنی چاہئے یہ ان کفار کے محبوب مقبول ہونے کی دلیل نہیں ۔ دبیان العاقبة یعنی ایک شئی کا انجام اور نتیجہ ظاہر کرنا جیسے لا تحسبن اللہ غافلا عما يعمل الظالمون یعنی انھیں ان کے اعمال کا نتیجہ مل کے رہے گا ۔ دالیاس نا امید کرنا جیسے ولا تعتذروا یعنی تمہارے عذرات قبول نہیں کئے جائیں گے . والارشاد جیسے لا تسألوا عن اشیا والشفقة جیسے رواب کو کر اسی بنانے سے نہی ہے یعنی جانوروں کی پشت پر بیٹھے انھیں روکے ہوئے کافی دیر تک باتیں کرتے رہنے سے نہی بنا بر شفقت ہے یعنی جانوروں پر شفقت کرو لہذا انھیں کرسی نہ بناؤ یا جیسے مشی فی نعل واحد سے منع ہے یہ بھی بنا بر شفقہ ہے لہذا ان معانی کثیرہ میں مستعمل ہونے کی وجہ سے مقتضاء نہی میں بھی توقف ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ موجب نبی میں تو قف نہیں۔ دلان الفحصى امر بالانتهاء - اصحاب توقف پر معارضہ ہے کہ نہی درحقیقت امر بال انتھام ہے اور حکم ہے کف النفس عن الفعل کا تو پھر فرق باقی نہیں رہتا درمیان افعل اور لا تفعل کے ۔ لانہ بصیر کیونکہ دونوں کا موجب پھر توقف ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ امر و نہی دونوں درج فی الامر ہو گئے ہیں حالانکہ والفرق بین طلب الفعل جو مقتضائے امر ہے وطلب الترك جو مقتضائے نہی ہے ان میں فرق بداھہ ثابت ہے دھدا احتمال اس کے ساتھ اس مقدمہ قائلہ کو یعنی یہ کہ احتمال موجب
The obligation from the action of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is not derived from the action itself, but rather from his saying 'Pray as you have seen me pray.' Besides this, the Messenger of Allah observed continuous fasting (wisal) and the Companions followed suit, and he removed his sandals in prayer and the Companions did likewise. The Prophet disapproved of both these actions of the Companions. If action indicated obligation, he would not have disapproved. So it is known that action does not indicate obligation. After explaining the real meaning of the word 'amr' (command), the author presents that the apparent form of amr, i.e., the imperative 'if'al' (do), what is its real signification? He says that its requirement (muijab) is the effect that is established from it. 'Al-tawaqquf' (pause) according to Ibn Surayj, who is from the Shafi'is, until it becomes clear [what is intended], meaning that until contextual clues clarify what is meant by the usage of amr, one should pause; no intended meaning is affirmed. Because amr is used in different meanings, and they are approximately sixteen meanings. Therefore, without contextual clues, certainty about any one meaning is not possible. The sixteen meanings are: (1) obligatory (ijab) like 'establish prayer'; (2) recommendation (nadb) like 'write them'; (3) disciplinary instruction (ta'dib) like 'eat from your own front'; (4) guidance (irshad) — these three are close to each other: in nadb the reward of the hereafter is considered, ta'dib relates to refinement of character, and irshad relates to worldly interests. (5) permission (ibaha) like 'eat' i.e., it is a permissible act. (6) threat (tahdid) like 'do whatever you will' and like 'say: enjoy your disbelief'; (7) bestowal of favor (imtinan) i.e., showing favor and kindness upon the servants, like 'eat from what Allah has provided you' where 'what Allah has provided' is a clue that 'eat' is for showing favor, not just permission. (8) honoring (ikram) like 'enter in peace'; (9) incapacitation (ta'jiz) like 'bring a surah'; (10) subjugation (taskhir) like 'be apes'; (11) humiliation (ibanat) like 'taste, indeed you are the mighty, the noble'; (12) equalization (taswiya) like 'whether you are patient or impatient'; (13) supplication (du'a) like 'O Allah, forgive me'; (14) wish (tamanni) like 'O long night, will you not depart?'; (15) contempt (ihtiqar) like 'throw that which you are going to throw' i.e., the magic that the magicians wanted to show in contrast to Musa; the command 'throw' is for contempt, showing that the magicians' magic in contrast to the miracle is a contemptible thing. (16) bringing into existence (takwin) like 'be and it is'. We say: If pausing (tawaqquf) is necessary because of multiple meanings, then in prohibition (nahy) it would also be necessary, because it too is used in multiple meanings. And the meanings of nahy are: prohibition (tahrim) like 'do not consume usury'; disapproval (karaha) like prohibition of prayer in usurped land; abstention (tanzih) like 'do not give a favor expecting more' i.e., this is only abstention, not prohibition or makruh tahrimi; belittlement (tahqir) like 'do not extend your eyes' showing that the wealth of disbelievers is insignificant; showing consequence (bayan al-aqiba) like 'do not think Allah is unaware'; frustration (ya's) like 'do not offer excuses'; guidance (irshad) like 'do not ask about things'; compassion (shafaqa) like prohibition of making animals into seats. So because of these multiple meanings, pausing would also be required in nahy, but in nahy there is no pausing. The scholar (al-Fakhsi?) said nahy is actually a command to desist; then the difference between amr and nahy disappears because both become commands. And the difference between requesting action (the import of amr) and requesting abandonment (the import of nahy) is obviously established. This is the rebuttal of the possibility that probability necessitates.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary discusses the nature of the imperative form (sigha al-amr) and refutes the view of Ibn Surayj (a Shafi'i scholar) that one must pause (tawaqquf) before assigning a meaning to a command. The author begins by citing examples from the Prophet's actions to show that action does not automatically indicate obligation; rather, the Prophet's words (like 'pray as you have seen me') provide the basis. Then the author lists the sixteen possible meanings of the imperative, ranging from obligation to creation. The core argument against tawaqquf is that if we pause due to multiple meanings in amr, consistency requires the same for nahy (prohibition), which also has multiple meanings. Since no one pauses for nahy, pausing for amr is unwarranted. The author concludes by noting that some argue that nahy is essentially a command to refrain, collapsing the distinction, but the clear difference between requesting action and requesting abandonment is self-evident. This is a classic Hanafi rebuttal of the Shafi'i tawaqquf stance, affirming that the default meaning of amr is obligation unless a contextual clue indicates otherwise.

Key Terms
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): The stance of pausing and withholding judgment on the meaning of a command until contextual clues reveal the intended meaning.
الأمر (al-amr): The imperative form or command; its real meaning (madhul haqiqi) is obligation (wujub) according to Hanafis, but it can be used in other senses contextually.
النَّهْي (al-nahy): The prohibition form; its real meaning is prohibition (tahrim), but it can be used for other meanings like karaha, tanzih, etc.
الموجب (al-mujib): The necessary result or import of the imperative form, i.e., obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used by the Hanafi author to refute the Shafi'i position of tawaqquf (pausing) in interpreting the imperative (amr)?
A) The imperative form is used only for obligation.
B) Prohibition (nahy) also has multiple meanings, yet no one pauses for it.
C) The Prophet's actions prove that the imperative is not for obligation.
D) The Hanafi school has a consensus on this issue.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects tawaqquf because the same logic would require pausing for nahy, which no school does; the default meaning of the imperative is obligation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Refutation of Tawaqquf via Multiple Meanings of Nahy
Refutes the argument for tawaqquf in amr by showing nahy also has multiple meanings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the argument for tawaqquf and apply the Hanafi refutation using the parallel of nahy and the distinction between valid and invalid probabilities.

Core Idea
If tawaqquf were required for amr due to multiple meanings, it must also be required for nahy—but it isn't, so the argument collapses.

In this passage, the author refutes the claim that we must suspend judgment (tawaqquf) when interpreting a command (amr) because it can indicate obligation, recommendation, permission, etc. He shows that the same reasoning would apply to prohibitions (nahy), which also have many meanings, yet no scholar suspends judgment for nahy. This reveals the inconsistency of the tawaqquf position and underscores the Hanafi principle that amr is zahir in wujub.

Guided Path
1
State the opposing claim
The as'hab al-tawaqquf argue that amr requires suspension because it is used in multiple meanings (wujub, nadb, ibaha, etc.) and no single meaning can be determined without a contextual indicator.
This is the position being refuted.
2
Identify the Hanafi parallel: nahy also has multiple meanings
The author lists several meanings of nahy: tahrim (prohibition), karahah (disapproval), tanzih (relegation), tahqir (belittling), bayan al-'aqibah (statement of consequence), ya's (making hopeless), irshad (guidance), shafaqah (compassion).
This demonstrates that nahy is at least as polysemous as amr.
3
Apply the same logic to nahy
If multiple meanings necessitate tawaqquf, then nahy would also require suspension. But in practice, no scholar suspends judgment for nahy; they understand it primarily as prohibition (tahrim).
This exposes the inconsistency of the opposing argument.
4
Examine the Hanafi counter-arguments
The text addresses the objection that nahy is essentially a command to desist, blurring the distinction. It argues the difference between seeking action and seeking abstention is self-evident. Moreover, accepting such remote probabilities would undermine all certainties, leading to sophistry.
This strengthens the Hanafi position that amr is zahir in wujub.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
Hanafis do not claim amr is muhkam (unequivocal) but that it is zahir (manifest) in wujub. Only probabilities supported by evidence (qarinah) are considered; remote probabilities without evidence are disregarded.
This is the operative principle in Hanafi usul.

انجلی تمنی ہے مصائب کی رات بڑی لمبی ہوتی ہے گویا اس کے انجلا کی توقع نہیں ہوتی اس لئے میاں انجلی تمنی کے لئے ہے (یه ) الاحتقار جیسے القواما انتم ملقون یعنی سحر جو ساحرین بمقابلہ موسی علیہ السلام ظاہر کرنے کا ارادہ رکھتے تھے اسی کے متعلق القوا کا امر برائے احتقار ہے یعنی بمقابلہ معجزہ ساحرین کا سحر ایک حقیر اور معمولی چیز ہے اسی کو ظاہر کرنا احتقار ہے (یو) التکوین یعنی الایجاد ایک شئی کو عدم سے نکال کر وجود میں لانا جیسے كن فيكون قلنا لو وجب التوقف هذا اصحاب توقف نے جو دليل توقف پیش کی تھی یہ اس کا جواب ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اگر امر میں توقف اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کثیر معانی میں مستعمل ہے تو پھر نہی میں بھی توقف کرنا لازم ہے کیونکہ وہ بھی کثیر معانی میں مستعمل ہے۔ دھی اور معانی یہ ہیں التحریم جیسے لاتاكلوا الربوا سود خوری حرام ہے جو اس آیت کے ساتھ اس کو حرام کیا گیا ہے ۔ والکڑھتہ جیسے نہی عن الصلوۃ فی الارض المغصوبه. والتنزيه نحول تمنن تستكرة يعنى یعنی احسان اس بنا پر نہ کرنا چاہتے کہ محسن علیہ سے کثیر شی ملے گی اس کثرت کے طلب اور خواہش کے پیش نظر احسان نہیں ہونا چاہئے یہ صرف تنزہ ہے تحریم نہیں ہے اور نہ مکروہ تحریمی . والتحقیر یعنی ایک شتی کی حقائرہ ظاہر کرنا جیسے لاتمدن عینیک اس سے یہ ظاہر کر مقصود ہے کہ کفار و مشرکین کے پاس جو دولت ہے یہ ایک حقیر اور معمولی شتی ہے ادھر نگاہ نہیں کرنی چاہئے یہ ان کفار کے محبوب مقبول ہونے کی دلیل نہیں ۔ دبیان العاقبة یعنی ایک شئی کا انجام اور نتیجہ ظاہر کرنا جیسے لا تحسبن اللہ غافلا عما يعمل الظالمون یعنی انھیں ان کے اعمال کا نتیجہ مل کے رہے گا ۔ دالیاس نا امید کرنا جیسے ولا تعتذروا یعنی تمہارے عذرات قبول نہیں کئے جائیں گے . والارشاد جیسے لا تسألوا عن اشیا والشفقة جیسے رواب کو کر اسی بنانے سے نہی ہے یعنی جانوروں کی پشت پر بیٹھے انھیں روکے ہوئے کافی دیر تک باتیں کرتے رہنے سے نہی بنا بر شفقت ہے یعنی جانوروں پر شفقت کرو لہذا انھیں کرسی نہ بناؤ یا جیسے مشی فی نعل واحد سے منع ہے یہ بھی بنا بر شفقہ ہے لہذا ان معانی کثیرہ میں مستعمل ہونے کی وجہ سے مقتضاء نہی میں بھی توقف ہونا چاہیے حالانکہ موجب نبی میں تو قف نہیں۔ دلان الفحصى امر بالانتهاء - اصحاب توقف پر معارضہ ہے کہ نہی درحقیقت امر بال انتھام ہے اور حکم ہے کف النفس عن الفعل کا تو پھر فرق باقی نہیں رہتا درمیان افعل اور لا تفعل کے ۔ لانہ بصیر کیونکہ دونوں کا موجب پھر توقف ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ امر و نہی دونوں درج فی الامر ہو گئے ہیں حالانکہ والفرق بین طلب الفعل جو مقتضائے امر ہے وطلب الترك جو مقتضائے نہی ہے ان میں فرق بداھہ ثابت ہے دھدا احتمال اس کے ساتھ اس مقدمہ قائلہ کو یعنی یہ کہ احتمال موجب توقف ہے جہاں احتمال پیدا ہو جائے وہاں توقف کرنا لازم ہے اس کو باطل کر رہا ہے ۔ کہ اگر اس قسم کا احتمال معتبر سمجھا جائے تو یہ ایک ایسا احتمال ہے جو سطل الحقائق حقائق اشیا کو باطل کر دے گا یمکن ان یراد به یعنی یبطل الحقائق میں لفظ حقائق سے مراد حقائق الاشیاء ہوں یعنی اگر اس قسم کے احتمالات کو معتبر قرار دیا جائے تو پھر حقائق اشیاء باطل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ مجوز ان لا يكون زيد أ جو شخص زید ہمارے سامنے بیٹھا ہے یہ زید نہ ہو کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ زید منعدم ہو چکا ہو اور اس کی جگہ کوئی اور شخص پیدا ہو چکا ہے اگر اس قسم کا احتمال معتبر ہو تو پھر حقائق اشیاء ثابت نہیں سکتیں اور دھو عين مذهب السوفسطائية یہ بعینہ سو فسطانیہ کا مذہب ہے جو حقائق اشیاء کی نفی اور انکار کرتے ہیں ويمكن ان يراد به حقائق الالفاظ یعنی لفظ حقائق سے مراد حقائق الفاظ ہوں کیونکہ کوئی ایسا لفظ نہیں ہے جس کے اندر احتمال قریب یا بعید نسخ یا خصوص یا اشتراک یا مجازہ کا نہ ہو بلکہ سر لفظ میں اس قسم کا احتمال پیدا ہو سکتا ہے۔ فان اعتبرت هذه الاحتمالات اگر اس قسم کے احتمالات بلا قرینہ معتبر سمجھے جائیں تو پھر الفاظ کی دلالت اپنے معانی موضوع لہ پر باطل ہو جائے اور یہی دلالتہ علی الموضوع لہ الفاظ کی حقیقت ہے پھر یہ حقیقت ان احتمالات کی بنیاد پر باطل ہو جائیگی - وايضا لم تدع انه محکم یہ ایک اور جواب ہے حاصل یہ کہ ہم اس کے مدعی نہیں ہیں کہ امر کسی ایک معنی مثلاً وجوب میں محکم ہے جس کے خلاف احتمال بالکل نہ ہو۔ نہ ناشی بالدلیل نہ ناشی بلا دلیل بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ معنی وجوب میں ظاہبر کا درجہ رکھتا ہے جس میں احتمالات ناشی بلا دلیل پیدا ہو سکتے ہیں جو کہ معتبر نہیں ہوتے
The hope of relief from affliction - the night is long, as if its dawn is not expected. Therefore, 'انجلی' is for hope. (This is) al-ihTiqar (belittling), like 'القوا' (throw) you are sorcerers, meaning the magic that the sorcerers intended to show in contrast to Musa (peace be upon him) - the command 'القوا' is for belittling, i.e., compared to the miracle, the sorcerers' magic is a contemptible and trivial thing. Showing this is ihTiqar. (Also) al-takwin (creating), i.e., bringing something from non-existence into existence, like 'Kun fayakun'. We said: If tawaqquf were necessary, this is the answer of the as'hab al-tawaqquf who presented the evidence for tawaqquf. Summary: If tawaqquf in amr is necessary because it is used in multiple meanings, then tawaqquf in nahy is also necessary because it too is used in multiple meanings. These meanings are: al-tahrim (prohibition) like 'Do not eat riba'; al-karahah (disapproval) like the prohibition of prayer in usurped land; al-tanzih (relegation to the permissible) like 'Do not bestow favors expecting more' - this is only tanzih, not prohibition; al-tahqir (belittling) like 'Do not stretch your eyes' to show that the wealth of disbelievers is trivial; bayan al-'aqibah (statement of consequence) like 'Do not think Allah is unaware'; al-ya's (making hopeless) like 'Do not make excuses'; al-irshad (guidance) like 'Do not ask about things'; al-shafaqah (compassion) like the prohibition of using animals as seats, i.e., prohibition out of compassion. So due to these multiple meanings, the implication of nahy would also require tawaqquf, yet it does not. The as'hab al-tawaqquf object that nahy is actually a command to desist and a ruling for self-restraint from the action, so there remains no difference between 'do' and 'do not do'. Because both imply tawaqquf, since both are classified under command, while the difference between seeking action (implication of amr) and seeking abstention (implication of nahy) is self-evident. So this probability invalidates the proposition that probability necessitates tawaqquf. If such probability is considered valid, it is a probability that invalidates the realities of things. It is possible that 'realities' refers to realities of things: if such probabilities are considered valid, then realities of things become invalid, because one may suppose that Zaid sitting before us is not Zaid, as he might have ceased to exist and someone else appeared. This is exactly the doctrine of the Sophists who deny realities. Alternatively, 'realities' may refer to realities of words: there is no word in which there is no near or remote probability of abrogation, specification, homonymy, or metaphor. If these probabilities without context are considered valid, then the indication of words to their original meanings becomes invalid, and that is the reality of words; then this reality would be invalidated by these probabilities. Also, we do not claim that amr is muhkam (unequivocal) in one meaning like wujub with no opposing probability at all, whether evident by evidence or not. Rather, we say that it holds the rank of zahir in the meaning of wujub, in which probabilities without evidence may arise, but they are not considered valid.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the argument for tawaqquf (suspension of judgment) in the interpretation of amr (command) due to its multiple possible meanings. The refutation proceeds by showing that the same logic would apply to nahy (prohibition), which also has many meanings, yet scholars do not suspend judgment for nahy. The author lists nine meanings of nahy: tahrim (prohibition), karahah (disapproval), tanzih (relegation), tahqir (belittling), bayan al-‘aqibah (statement of consequence), ya’s (making hopeless), irshad (guidance), shafaqah (compassion), and possibly others. He then addresses the objection that nahy is essentially a command to desist, thus blurring the distinction. He argues that the difference between seeking action and seeking abstention is self-evident, so the probability argument fails. Furthermore, if such remote probabilities are considered valid, they would undermine all certainties, leading to the position of the Sophists. Finally, the passage clarifies that the Hanafi position does not claim amr is muhkam (unequivocal) but rather that it is zahir (manifest) in meaning wujub, and only probabilities without evidence are disregarded.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment or interpretation due to multiple possible meanings without a contextual indicator.
احتمال (ihtimal): Probability or possibility of a different interpretation, which if considered valid could undermine certainty.
حقيقة (haqiqah): Reality or literal meaning of a word; in this context, it refers both to realities of things and to the literal meanings of words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used to refute the necessity of tawaqquf in amr?
A) Amr has only one meaning, so no tawaqquf needed.
B) Nahy also has multiple meanings yet does not require tawaqquf, so the same logic applies to amr.
C) The Quran explicitly states that amr means wujub.
D) The majority of scholars agree on wujub, so tawaqquf is rejected.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis reject tawaqquf in amr because the same logic would apply to nahy, but it doesn't, and because accepting remote probabilities destroys certainty.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
The Imperative for Ibahah/Nadb: Haqiqah Qasirah or Majaz?
Dispute on amr for ibahah/nadb: haqiqah qasirah vs majaz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether amr used for ibahah/nadb is haqiqah qasirah or majaz, apply Fakhr al-Islam's reasoning to analyze a command, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Amr for ibahah/nadb is haqiqah qasirah: it indicates permissibility of act (part of wujub), not permissibility of leaving (derived elsewhere).

The imperative (amr) is agreed to be haqiqah for wujub. But when it conveys ibahah (permissibility) or nadb (recommendation), is that usage haqiqah or majaz? This lesson unpacks a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute. Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) defends haqiqah qasirah, while al-Karkhi and al-Jassas argue for majaz. The disagreement hinges on whether ibahah shares a component with wujub, and on the definition of 'majaz' itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed foundation
All parties agree that amr is haqiqah for wujub. The dispute begins when amr is used for other meanings like ibahah or nadb.
2
State the two positions
Al-Karkhi and al-Jassas: amr for ibahah/nadb is majaz because ibahah is distinct from wujub. Fakhr al-Islam and the author: it is haqiqah qasirah (incomplete real usage).
Haqiqah qasirah means using the word for part of its original meaning.
3
Analyze Fakhr al-Islam's reasoning
Ibahah has two components: permissibility of the act and permissibility of leaving. The imperative only indicates the first component (shared with wujub). The second component comes from absence of prohibition. Thus amr is applied to part of its original meaning – not majaz.
Key: amr does not indicate permissibility of leaving at all.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Al-Karkhi and al-Jassas see ibahah and wujub as mutually exclusive (mutabayin), so any use of amr for ibahah is for something entirely different, hence majaz.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If amr for ibahah is haqiqah qasirah, no qarinah (contextual indicator) is needed; if it is majaz, a qarinah is required. This affects interpretation of commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

بنده المسئلة اختلافاً ء میں ثانیا ذکر کیا ہے جو مختار عند فخر الاسلام تھا جس کو یہاں پیش کرتے ہوئے صراحة كبا وهو اطلاق اسم الکل علی الجزء لانا سے دلیل اصحبت پیش کی خلاصہ یہ کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں که اباحته مباین للوجوب ہے کیونکہ اباختہ کا معنی ہے جو از الفعل مع جواز الترک اور وجوب کا معنی ہے جواز الفعل مع حرمتہ الترک اگر چه اطلاق علی المباین مجاز ہوتا ہے کا طلاق الاسد علی الانسان - لكن معنى قولنا ان الامر للاباحة یعنی جہاں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ امر برائے اباحہ ہے تو اس سے معنی اور مراد یہ ہوتی ہے کہ یہ امرا باحتہ کی فقط ایک جزء یعنی جواز الفعل پر دال ہے یہ مراد نہیں ہوتی کہ اباحت کی دونوں اجزاء پر دال ہے کیونکہ امر جواز ترک پر اصلا دال نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ قبل انما یثبت بلکہ جواز ترک صرف اس بنا پر ثابت ہو گا کہ یہ امر وجوب کی دوسری جزیعنی حرمہ ترک پر دال نہیں ہے فیثبت جواز الترک جواز ترک اسی اصل پر ہیں نجواز الفعل جواز فعل جو اس امرا باحتہ کے ساتھ ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ معنی وجوب کی ایک جز ہے تو یہ اطلاق لفظ الکل علی الجز ہوا - وهذا معنى قوله لان الامر دال الخ معنی اور مراد یہ ہوگی کہ امر اباحہ جو از لئے کہ حرمیہ ترک پر دلیل نہیں ہے اور یہی حرمہ ترک معنی وجوب کی دوسری جز تھی امر اس پر دال نہیں تو بہر حال یہ اطلاق الکل علی الجز ہے جو حقیقہ قاصرہ ہے مجاز اور استعارہ نہیں ہے . هذا بحث رقیق ماهشه الا خاطری یہ بحث وقیق ہے جس تک مصنف کے ذہن کی رسائی ہوتی ہے اللہ دره ، هذا اذا استعمل واريد به الاباحة
It is like those who hold haqiqah qasirah say, because ibahah and nadb are distinct from wujub, because rulings like wujub, nadb, ibahah etc. are mutually exclusive rulings, so there cannot be a whole-part relationship between them, therefore ibahah is distinct from wujub and not a part of it. Know that there is detailed disagreement: The imperative (amr) is haqiqah for wujub, meaning its real intended meaning is wujub. When ibahah or nadb is intended with it, then it is by way of majaz, not haqiqah, because using the word for other than what it was placed for is majaz. Fakhr al-Islam mentioned disagreement in this issue: that intended nadb and ibahah being majaz is not agreed upon, rather there is disagreement. According to al-Karkhi and al-Jassas it is majaz in them [i.e., nadb and ibahah]. According to some it is haqiqah in both, but note that according to them it is not complete haqiqah, rather haqiqah qasirah, i.e., using the word for part of what it was placed for. Fakhr al-Islam chose this view, and the author later said 'the second is correct' and that is his interpretation. Now what is the interpretation of the statement that calls it haqiqah, while it is used for other than what it was placed for? He said: 'Majaz in their terminology' – according to Fakhr al-Islam, majaz is a word by which a meaning outside the original meaning is intended. But when a part of the original meaning is intended, he does not call it majaz, rather he calls it haqiqah qasirah. Evidence for this terminology is Fakhr al-Islam's statement that the meaning of ibahah and nadb is part of the meaning of wujub in origin. So it is partial, not distinct. Thus its indication is haqiqah qasirah, not majaz. Majaz is a meaning that is distinct from the original. In the terminology of other scholars, majaz is a word by which other than what it was placed for is intended, and 'other than what it was placed for' is general, whether it is a part of the original or a meaning outside it. And this definition is correct according to the author, but he restricts 'other than what it was placed for' to the external meaning. So in the definition of majaz, 'other than what it was placed for' means the meaning outside the original, and the word 'other' cannot be applied to a part. And indication of the part is not indication of other than what it was placed for. The definition of 'other' is as mentioned in kalam. But 'whole' means the separability of each from the other. Here if it is a part, it can be separable from the whole, but not separable from the part, so indication of the part is not indication of other than what it was placed for, but indication of part of what it was placed for, therefore it is not majaz but haqiqah qasirah. The outcome of the disagreement is whether the application of amr to ibahah and nadb is by way of applying the name of the whole to the part (which is haqiqah qasirah) or by way of metaphor (isti'arah) which is majaz, with the relation of majaz being a common attribute between the real and metaphorical meanings, like applying 'asad' to a brave man because of shared bravery. The second meaning referred to is what he mentioned second in his earlier phrase 'Fakhr al-Islam mentioned disagreement on this issue' which was the chosen view of Fakhr al-Islam, and he presents it here explicitly: it is applying the name of the whole to the part. The proof presented: we concede that ibahah is distinct from wujub, because ibahah means permission of the act with permissibility of leaving it, and wujub means permission of the act with prohibition of leaving it. Although applying to something distinct is majaz like applying 'asad' to a man, yet the meaning of our saying 'the imperative is for ibahah' is that the imperative indicates only one part of ibahah, i.e., permissibility of the act, not that it indicates both parts of ibahah, because the imperative cannot indicate permissibility of leaving at all. Rather, permissibility of leaving is established only because the imperative does not indicate the other part of wujub, i.e., prohibition of leaving. So permissibility of leaving is based on the principle that the imperative does not indicate prohibition of leaving. When there is no evidence for prohibition of leaving, then leaving is permissible based on that, not by the word of the imperative. The word of the imperative does not indicate permissibility of leaving, nor do we establish permissibility of leaving with it. The permissibility of the act that is established with this imperative for ibahah is one part of the meaning of wujub, so this is application of the word of the whole to the part. And this is the meaning of his statement 'because the imperative indicates' etc. The meaning is that the imperative for ibahah indicates permissibility of the act, which is one part of the meaning of ibahah and wujub, not permissibility of leaving, by which ibahah is distinct from wujub. But this permissibility of leaving is established due to lack of evidence for prohibition of leaving. That prohibition of leaving was the other part of wujub, and the imperative does not indicate it. So in any case, this is application of the whole to the part, which is haqiqah qasirah, not majaz or isti'arah. This is a subtle discussion, which only the author's mind can reach, may God bless him. This is when amr is used and ibahah is intended.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the nature of the imperative (amr) when used to indicate permissibility (ibahah) or recommendation (nadb). The disagreement centers on whether such usage is haqiqah (real) or majaz (metaphorical). The author presents the view of Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) who argues that it is haqiqah qasirah (incomplete real usage) because ibahah and nadb are considered parts (ajza') of the meaning of wujub (obligation) in a certain sense. According to Fakhr al-Islam, majaz applies only when the intended meaning is entirely outside the original meaning. If the intended meaning is a part of the original, it is haqiqah qasirah. Other scholars like al-Karkhi and al-Jassas consider it majaz. The author sides with Fakhr al-Islam, providing a detailed reasoning: when the imperative indicates ibahah, it only indicates the permissibility of the act (one part of wujub), not the permissibility of leaving it. The permissibility of leaving is derived from the absence of a prohibition, not from the imperative itself. Thus the imperative is applied to a part of its original meaning, making it haqiqah qasirah. This distinction preserves the integrity of the imperative's primary meaning (wujub) while allowing for its extended use without falling into majaz.

Key Terms
حقيقة قاصرة (haqiqah qasirah): Using a word for part of what it was originally placed for; it is haqiqah but incomplete because the intended meaning is a subset of the original meaning, not the whole.
مجاز (majaz): Using a word for a meaning that is entirely outside its original meaning (according to Fakhr al-Islam). For other scholars, it includes using the word for a part of the original meaning as well.
الأمر (al-amr): The imperative form, originally placed for obligation (wujub).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fakhr al-Islam, when the imperative (amr) is used to indicate ibahah (permissibility), what is the correct classification and why?
A) Majaz because ibahah is distinct from wujub
B) Haqiqah qasirah because it indicates permissibility of the act, which is part of the meaning of wujub
C) Haqiqah complete because ibahah is the same as wujub
D) It is not valid to use amr for ibahah

Key Takeaway
Amr used for ibahah/nadb is haqiqah qasirah according to Fakhr al-Islam because it indicates part of the original meaning (permissibility of act), while permissibility of leaving is from absence of prohibition.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Definitions of Umum and Takrar in Hanafi Usul
Definitions of umum and takrar with examples of interdependence and separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define umum and takrar, distinguish between them, and identify when they are interdependent or separable using Hanafi examples.

Core Idea
Umum and takrar are distinct concepts; interdependence is contextual, not inherent in an absolute command.

Before we can analyze whether an absolute imperative implies generality or repetition, we must understand exactly what these terms mean. This lesson establishes the technical definitions of umum and takrar as used by Hanafi usul scholars, illustrated with examples from prayer, fasting, and divorce. You will learn when these two concepts are necessarily linked and when they can be separated — a crucial foundation for the dispute that follows.

Guided Path
1
Define umum linguistically and technically
Note that umum means inclusion of all individuals of a category without exception. In the passage, the author describes it as 'شمول افراد کو کہا جاتا یعنی جمیع افراد کو یک باندگی شامل ہونا' (inclusion of individuals, i.e., including all individuals in one go).
Umum is a quantity-related concept — it answers 'how many?'
2
Define takrar linguistically and technically
Takrar is defined as 'وقوعہ مرة بعد اخری' (occurrence once after another) with regard to time. It is a temporal repetition of the same act.
Takrar is a time-related concept — it answers 'how often?'
3
Identify cases of interdependence
The author gives examples like prayer (صلاۃ) and fasting (صوم) where the command includes all individual acts of prayer/fasting over a lifetime, and they occur repeatedly over time. Here, umum and takrar are inseparable.
In these acts, the command is not absolute but tied to repetitive conditions (times).
4
Identify cases of separation
The divorce example (طلقی نفسک) shows that if umum is intended, three divorces can be pronounced at once; if takrar is intended, they must be separated temporally. Here, umum and takrar are separable.
The same linguistic form can be interpreted differently based on intent.
5
Connect to the absolute imperative debate
Now you understand that neither umum nor takrar is automatically present in a command. The question is whether an unqualified imperative (amr mutlaq) inherently carries either or both.
This sets the stage for the dispute in the next lesson.
