Section: The absolute imperative according to some necessitates generality and repetition. 'Umum' means inclusion of individuals, i.e. including all individuals in one go. 'Takrir' means occurrence once after another, and this is with regard to time, i.e. an action occurs at one time, then secondly the same action occurs at another time; this is called repetition. Sometimes umum and takrar are interdependent, like 'pray' and 'give charity' which include all individuals of prayer; for a lifetime, none is left out. 'Pray' includes all prayers of one's life, and similarly 'fast' and 'pray' and 'fast' occur with repetition of times one after another, so here umum and takrar are interdependent and cannot be separated. And sometimes they can be separated, like in 'divorce yourself' if umum is intended, then three divorces at once with one word is possible; in that case one must say 'I divorce you thrice'. And if takrar is intended, then it must be given one after another. So according to some, the absolute imperative, i.e. devoid of indications of takrar and umum, necessitates both umum and takrar. Because 'idrib' (strike) is an abbreviation of 'atlub minka al-darb' (I request from you striking), i.e. the verb is a masdar defined with 'al', and 'idrib' is a generic noun which is beneficial for umum, i.e. including all individuals. This is the proof for umum. And presenting proof for takrar, he said: 'And from the question of the questioner in the Hajj', it is narrated from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O people, Hajj has been prescribed for you, so perform Hajj.' Al-Aqra' ibn Habis said: 'Is it every year, O Messenger of Allah?' The author presented this hadith with these words: 'Is it for this year or forever?' Surraqa asked during the Farewell Pilgrimage, his words exactly: 'Is it for this year or forever?' The questioner, who is a linguist, understood from the command repetition, so it is known that the command necessitates repetition. We say: consider other acts of worship. This is the refutation of the proof for takrar. The summary is that the questioner compared Hajj to other acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat) thinking that since they have repetition, perhaps Hajj also has repetition, and also the questioner was confused that Hajj is tied to time and time repeats, so it should be repeated with time, but the cause of obligation is one, i.e. the House of Allah, and since the cause is not repeated, Hajj should not be repeated. So the question was based on this difficulty, not on the basis that the command necessitates repetition. Therefore your argument is incomplete. And according to al-Shafi'i, it is possible. That is, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the command does not necessitate umum and takrar, but it bears the possibility of takrar and umum. Because their proof is the same: the word 'idrib' is an abbreviation of 'atlub minka darban'. According to him, the masdar is indefinite and an indefinite in the context of affirmation is particular, but it bears the possibility of umum. And according to some of our scholars (from the Hanafis), it is not probable of takrar unless it is attached to a condition, then repetition follows the repetition of the condition, like 'if you are in a state of janaba, then purify yourselves', so with repetition of janaba, the command to purify is repeated. Or it may be specified by a description, i.e. the command is specified and restricted with the existence of a description, then repetition follows the repetition of the description, like 'establish prayer at the decline of the sun'; here the command for prayer is restricted with the description of the sun's decline, so with the repetition of the description, the command is repeated. And according to the majority of our scholars, it does not bear either at all. That is, most Hanafi scholars say the command is not likely of umum nor takrar. In this issue, there are four madhhabs: First: the command necessitates umum and takrar. Second madhhab...
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute examining whether the absolute imperative (amr mutlaq) indicates generality (umum) and repetition (takrar). The author first defines the terms: umum is inclusion of all individuals; takrar is occurrence of the act repeatedly over time. He distinguishes cases where umum and takrar are interdependent (like prayer, fasting) and where they can be separated (like divorce). Then he presents the position of some scholars (perhaps the Zahiris or some Hanafis) that the absolute imperative necessitates both umum and takrar. They argue linguistically: 'idrib' is a generic noun implying all instances of striking. They also cite the hadith about Hajj where a companion asked about repetition, implying the command was understood as repeating annually. The author refutes this by noting that the questioner's doubt was based on comparing Hajj to other repeated acts, not on the intrinsic nature of the command. Then he presents the Shafi'i position: the command does not necessitate but may bear the possibility of umum and takrar. Then the position of some Hanafis: the command only indicates takrar if conditional on a condition (like janaba) or specified by a description (like the decline of the sun). Finally, the majority of Hanafis (and this is the relied-upon position) hold that the absolute imperative indicates neither umum nor takrar; it simply denotes the performance of the act once, unless there is external evidence. The passage ends by listing four madhhabs (though only the first is fully mentioned).

Key Terms
الامر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): A command that is not accompanied by any indication (qarinah) specifying its extent, repetition, or generality.
العموم (al-umum): Inclusion of all individuals of a category without exception.
التكرار (al-takrar): Repeated occurrence of an action at different times.
معلق بالشرط (mu'allaq bi al-shart): A command that is attached to a condition, so that the command is repeated each time the condition occurs.
مخصوص بوصف (mukhtass bi wasf): A command that is specified by a description, so that the command is repeated whenever the description is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following are umum and takrar interdependent?
A) Divorce (طلاق)
B) Prayer (صلاۃ) and Fasting (صوم)
C) Striking (ضرب)
D) Hajj

Key Takeaway
Umum and takrar are distinct concepts; interdependence is contextual, not inherent in an absolute command.

The Hanafi Position on Amr Mutlaq: No Implied Umum or Takrar
Dispute on whether absolute imperative indicates umum and takrar, with proofs and Hanafi refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on the absolute imperative, identify the opposing proofs, and apply the Hanafi refutation using the hadith of Hajj.

Core Idea
The absolute command demands a single performance — unless a condition or description triggers repetition.

This lesson focuses on the central dispute: does an absolute imperative (amr mutlaq) inherently indicate generality (umum) or repetition (takrar)? We examine the proof from the hadith of Hajj, the Hanafi refutation, and the alternative positions within the Hanafi school. By the end, you will understand why the majority Hanafi view is that an unqualified command is fulfilled once.

Guided Path
1
Identify the majority Hanafi position
The passage clearly states: 'وعند عامة علمائنا لا يحتملها اصلا' — according to the majority of our scholars, it does not bear any probability of umum or takrar. The act is required once.
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
2
Examine the opposing proof for takrar
The opponents cite the hadith where the Prophet commanded Hajj, and Al-Aqra' ibn Habis asked 'A-kullu 'am?' (every year?). The opponents argue that the companion understood repetition from the command.
This is an ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The Hanafis respond: 'qaulna i'tabir bi sa'ir al-'ibadat' (we say: consider other acts of worship). The questioner's doubt arose from comparing Hajj to repeated acts like prayer; it was not based on the command itself. The cause of Hajj (the House) is not repeated, so the command is not repeated.
The refutation moves the debate from linguistics to usul (analogy).
4
Review subordinate Hanafi views
Some Hanafis allow takrar if the command is conditional on a condition (mu'allaq bi shart) or specified by a description (mukhtass bi wasf). But these are not absolute imperatives.
This is a minority view.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the command does not necessitate but may bear the probability of umum and takrar. This is a middle position between the extreme view (necessitation) and the majority Hanafi view (no probability).
The Shafi'i view is based on the indefinite masdar (nakirah) in the context of affirmation.

Section: The absolute imperative according to some necessitates generality and repetition. 'Umum' means inclusion of individuals, i.e. including all individuals in one go. 'Takrir' means occurrence once after another, and this is with regard to time, i.e. an action occurs at one time, then secondly the same action occurs at another time; this is called repetition. Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute examining whether the absolute imperative (amr mutlaq) indicates generality (umum) and repetition (takrar). The author first defines the terms: umum is inclusion of all individuals; takrar is occurrence of the act repeatedly over time. He distinguishes cases where umum and takrar are interdependent (like prayer, fasting) and where they can be separated (like divorce). Then he presents the position of some scholars (perhaps the Zahiris or some Hanafis) that the absolute imperative necessitates both umum and takrar. They argue linguistically: 'idrib' is a generic noun implying all instances of striking. They also cite the hadith about Hajj where a companion asked about repetition, implying the command was understood as repeating annually. The author refutes this by noting that the questioner's doubt was based on comparing Hajj to other repeated acts, not on the intrinsic nature of the command. Then he presents the Shafi'i position: the command does not necessitate but may bear the possibility of umum and takrar. Then the position of some Hanafis: the command only indicates takrar if conditional on a condition (like janaba) or specified by a description (like the decline of the sun). Finally, the majority of Hanafis (and this is the relied-upon position) hold that the absolute imperative indicates neither umum nor takrar; it simply denotes the performance of the act once, unless there is external evidence. The passage ends by listing four madhhabs (though only the first is fully mentioned).

Key Terms
الامر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): A command that is not accompanied by any indication (qarinah) specifying its extent, repetition, or generality.
العموم (al-umum): Inclusion of all individuals of a category without exception.
التكرار (al-takrar): Repeated occurrence of an action at different times.
معلق بالشرط (mu'allaq bi al-shart): A command that is attached to a condition, so that the command is repeated each time the condition occurs.
مخصوص بوصف (mukhtass bi wasf): A command that is specified by a description, so that the command is repeated whenever the description is present.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Imperative: Do Repetition and Generality Follow?
Linguistic dispute on amr's implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four positions on whether the imperative (amr) indicates repetition (takrar) and generality (umoom), and apply the majority Hanafi ruling to the example of 'طلقی نفسك' in divorce.

Core Idea
The imperative indicates a single occurrence and generality of the act, but not repetition; intention can extend it to the whole (e.g., three divorces), but not to a number like two.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, a key question is: when the divine command (or any imperative) is issued, does it require the action to be performed multiple times? And does it cover all individuals of that action? The passage below presents four scholarly positions on this issue, ranging from those who hold that the imperative necessitates both repetition and generality to those who deny both. The majority Hanafi view strikes a middle ground: the imperative indicates a single occurrence but includes all types or individuals of the act. This has direct practical consequences, especially in matters like divorce where a single ambiguous statement 'طلقی نفسك' (you divorce yourself) could be interpreted as one, two, or three divorces depending on the school and intention. Let us unpack the debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four madhahib
List the four schools of thought on whether the imperative implies repetition and generality. Note their key proponents: the first school (some scholars), the second (Imam al-Shafi'i), the third (some Hanafis), and the fourth (majority Hanafis).
The passage distinguishes absolute imperative vs conditional/qualified imperative for the third school.
2
Analyse the linguistic proof of the majority Hanafis
Understand the argument: the imperative is derived from a verbal noun (masdar) which is definite (with 'al') indicating a singular instance. Hence the command is for one occurrence. However, the verbal noun as a generic noun (ism al-jins) includes all individuals of the action, giving it generality.
The key phrase: 'لان المصدر فرد' (the verbal noun is a single instance).
3
Evaluate the hadith proof for repetition
Examine the hadith where a companion asked if Hajj is required every year. The first school uses this to argue that the imperative implies repetition. The Hanafi response shows that the question was based on analogy to other acts of worship and the repetitive nature of time, not on the imperative itself.
This is a crucial counter-argument: the companion's query was istifsar (seeking clarification) due to other factors.
4
Apply the ruling to the divorce case
Take the example 'طلقی نفسك' (you divorce yourself). According to each school: first school: three divorces; second (Shafi'i): probable for two or three; third: may indicate repetition if conditional; fourth (majority Hanafi): one divorce unless intention of three, but intention of two invalid.
The Hanafi position: the imperative gives one certain divorce; three is possible with intention (niyyah) because three is the total (majmoo') as an artificial unit, but two is a mere number (adad mahd) and not indicated.
5
Summarise the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference is clear: different schools yield different numbers of divorces. The text prefers the majority Hanafi view as the relied-upon position, supported by detailed linguistic analysis.
Note that the third school's position on conditional/qualified amr is distinguished from the absolute amr.

صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ایہا الناس قد فرض عليكم المجم محجوا فقال الاقرع بن الحابس الكل عام یا رسول اللہ الحدیث اسی کو مصنفہ نے پیش کیا ہے بایں الفاظ العامنا بذا ام اللابد البتہ سراقہ نے جو سوال حجۃ الوداع میں کیا ہے اس کے الفاظ بعینہ یہی میں اکنا منا بذا ام للابد مبہر حال اس سائل نے جو اہل لسان ہے امر سے تکرار سمجھا ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ امر مواجب تکرار ہے قلنا اعتبر بسائر العبادات یہ جواب از دلیل تکرار ہے حاصل یہ کہ اس سائل نے حج کو باقی عبادت صلوة وصوم و زکوۃ پر قیاس کیا کہ جب ان کے اندر تکرار ہے تو شاید اس میں بھی تکرار ہوگا اور سائل کے لئے یہ بھی موجب اشکال ہوا کہ حج متعلق بالوقت ہے اور وقت متکرر ہے تو تکرار وقت کے ساتھ اسے مشکریہ ہونا چاہتے اور سبب وجوب ایک ہے یعنی بیت اللہ چونکہ سبب متکرر نہیں اس لئے حج متکرر نہیں ہونا چاہئے اسی اشکال کی بنیاد پر سوال کیا ہے نہ اس بنا پر کہ امر موجب تکرار ہے لہذا آپ کا استدلال نا تمام ہے ر عند الشافعي يحتمله یعنی امام شافعی کے نزدیک امر موجب عموم و تکرار تو نہیں ہے البتہ احتمال تکرار و عموم رکھتا ہے۔ لما قلنا یعنی ان کی دلیل وہی ہے کہ لفظ اضرب مختصر ہے اطلب منك ضربا ان کے نزدیک مصدر نکرہ ہے اور نکرہ مقام اثبات میں خاص ہوتا ہے البتہ اس کے اندر احتمال عموم ہوتا ہے ۔ وعند بعض علمائنا الى الحنفیہ ہمارے بعض علماء کے نزدیک محتمل تکرار نہیں الدان يكون مگر یہ کہ معلق بالشرط ہو تو تکرار شرط کے ساتھ مکرر ہوگا جیسے ان کنتم جنبا فا طہرو تو تکرار جنابت سے فاطہر وا کا حکم مکرر ہوگا۔ او مخصوصا بوصف یعنی امر مخصوص اور مقید ہو ثبوت وصف کے ساتھ تو تکرار و صفت تکرار امر ہو گا جیسے اقم الصلوۃ لدلوك الشمس یہاں امر بالصلوۃ مقید ہے دلوک شمس کی چیف کے ساتھ یعنی دلوک الشمس کے ثبوت کے ساتھ تو دلوگ شمس والی صنف کے تکرار کے ساتھ اقم کا تکرار ہوگا۔ وعند عامة علمائنا لا يحتملها اصلا یعنی اکثر علماء احناف کے نزدیک امر یہ محتمل عموم ہے نہ محتمل تکرار اس مسئلہ میں کل مذاہب اربعہ ہوئے اول یہ امر موجب عموم و تکرار ہے ۔ ثانی مذہب امام شافعی رو کا کہ امر محتمل عموم و تکرا ر ہے ثالث بعض علماء احناف کا کہ جب معلق بالشرط ہو یا مقید بالوصف ہو تو پھر محتمل تکرا رہ ہے رابع اکثر علماء احناف کا کہ امر یہ محتمل عموم ہے نہ محتمل تکرار . لان المصدر فرد به مذهب رابع کی دلیل ہے خلاصہ کہ امر بالفعل دال علی المصدر ہوتا ہے اور مصدر فرد ہے یعنی مفرد ہے۔ انما یقع اور مفرد واقع ہوتا ہے واحد حقیقی پر کیونکہ یہ متعین فی المفرد ہے ۔ اولمجموع الافراد یا اس مفرد کا اطلاق مجموع افراد پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ مجموع من حیث المجموع واحد اعتباری ہوتا ہے وذا محتمل اور مجموع من حیث المجموع کا مراد ہونا محتمل ہے متیقن نہیں ہے۔ لا یثبت الآبالنية چونکہ یہ محتمل ہے اس لئے اس کا اثبات بلانیت نہیں ہوگا البتہ نیت کے ساتھ ثابت ہوگا لا على العدد الحض یعنی عدد محض پر اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہو گا فی طلقی نفسك یہ تفریح ہے مذاہب مذکورہ کے لحاظ سے یوجب الثلاث على الاول مذہب اول کے لحاظ سے یہ امر موجب ثلث ہوگا کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک امر موجب عموم تھا اور جمیع افراد طلاق کے ثلثہ ہیں اس لئے یہ موجب ثلث ہوگا۔ ويحتمل الاثنين والثلث عند الشافعی امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ محتمل تکرار تھا اس لئے اس کے اندر احتمال اثنین ہے اور چونکہ محتمل عموم تھا اس لئے یہ امر محتمل ثلاث ہے۔ دعندنا ای عند عامتہ علماء الاحناف كما هو المذهب الرابع يقع على الواحد واحد پر واقع ہوگی کیونکہ یہ فرد واحد ہے جو اقل اور متیقن ہے دی نية الثلث کیونکہ ثلث مجموع افراد طلاق ہے اور مجموع من حیث المجموع واحد اعتباری ہے جو کہ محتمل تھا لہذا نیت کے ساتھ اس کا مراد لینا صحیح ہوگا ولا تصلح نية الاثنين لانه عدد محض کیونکہ طلقات حرہ میں اثنین عدد محض ہے نہ واحد حقیقی واحد اعتباری لہذا اس کی نیت صحیح نہیں لا دلالة لاسم الفرد اى المفرد على العدد اب اس مسئلہ کے ساتھ شمرہ اختلاف تو واضح ہو گیا البتہ مذہب ثالث کے لحاظ سے اس مسئلہ میں شمرہ اختلاف ظاہر نہیں ۔ مذہب ثالث یہ تھا کہ امر محتمل تکرار نہیں ہے البتہ جب معلق بالشرط ہو تو محتمل تكرار ہوتا ہے فاوردت هذه المسئلة تو یہ مسئلہ پیش کیا گیا تا کہ شمرہ اختلاف ظاہر ہو جائے مثلاً ایک شخص اپنی بیوی سے کہتا ہے ان دخلت الدار نطلقى نفسك مذہب ثالث کے لحاظ سے لائق ہے کہ یہاں تکرار شرط سے تکرار طلاق ثابت ہو سکے ینبغی اس لئے کہا کہ ان حضرات سے اس مسئلہ میں کوئی روایت واقع نہیں ہے البتہ ان کے اصل وضابطہ کی بنیاد پر یہ موجب تکرار ہو گا فقال وفی ان دخلت الدار فطلقی نفسک فینبغی ان ثبت التكرار على المذهب الثالث لا عندنا .
They cannot be separated, and sometimes they can be separated. For example, in 'you divorce yourself [with the imperative]' — if generality is intended, then three divorces at once with one word is the option; in that case, he must say 'I divorce you thrice'. And if repetition is intended, then he must give them one after another. So according to some scholars, the absolute imperative — i.e., free from indications of repetition and generality — necessitates generality and repetition. Because 'idrib' is an abbreviation of 'atlub minka al-darb', meaning the verb is from a verbal noun defined by 'al', and 'idrib' is a generic noun that conveys generality, i.e., inclusion of all individuals. This is the proof for generality. And presenting the proof for repetition, he said: 'And from the question of the questioner in Hajj...' It is narrated from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'O people, Hajj has been prescribed for you.' Al-Aqra' ibn Habis said: 'Every year, O Messenger of Allah?' The author presented this tradition with these words: 'Is it for this year or forever?' Actually, Suraqa asked this question during the Farewell Pilgrimage with these exact words: 'Is it for this year or forever?' In any case, this questioner, who is a native speaker, understood repetition from the imperative, so it is known that the imperative necessitates repetition. We said: 'Consider the rest of the acts of worship.' This is the response to the proof of repetition. The conclusion is that this questioner analogized Hajj to the other acts of worship — prayer, fasting, zakat — that since repetition occurs in them, perhaps it also occurs in Hajj. And it was also problematic for the questioner that Hajj is connected to a specific time, and the time is repetitive, so repetition should accompany the time; but the cause of obligation is one, i.e., the House of Allah; since the cause is not repetitive, Hajj should not be repetitive. The question was based on this problem, not on the basis that the imperative necessitates repetition. Therefore, your argument is invalid. And according to al-Shafi'i, it is probable: meaning, for Imam al-Shafi'i, the imperative does not necessitate generality and repetition, but it bears the probability of repetition and generality. 'Because we said' — meaning their proof is also that the word 'idrib' is an abbreviation of 'atlubu minka darban'; according to them, the verbal noun is indefinite, and an indefinite in a positive context indicates specificity, but it bears the probability of generality. And according to some of our Hanafi scholars, it is not probable for repetition unless it is conditional, so it will be repeated with the repetition of the condition, like 'if you are in a state of janaba, then purify yourselves' — the command 'fatahharu' is repeated with the repetition of janaba. Or if it is qualified by a description, i.e., the command is specific and restricted by the existence of a description, then repetition occurs with the repetition of that description, like 'establish prayer at the decline of the sun' — here the command for prayer is restricted by the existence of the decline of the sun, so with the repetition of the description 'decline of the sun', 'aqim' is repeated. And according to the majority of our scholars, it does not bear that at all: meaning, most Hanafi scholars hold that the imperative bears generality but not repetition. In this issue, there are four total schools: First, this imperative necessitates generality and repetition. Second school: Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the imperative is probable for generality and repetition. Third: Some Hanafi scholars say that when it is conditional or qualified by a description, then it is probable for repetition. Fourth: The majority of Hanafi scholars say that the imperative is probable for generality, not for repetition. 'Because the verbal noun is a single instance' — this is the proof of the fourth school: summary: 'amr bi al-fi'l' indicates the verbal noun, and the verbal noun is an individual, i.e., singular. It only occurs as a single real instance. Or upon the totality of individuals, because the totality as a whole is an artificial unit, and that is probable. And intending the totality as a whole is probable, not certain. It is not established except by intention. Since it is probable, its affirmation without intention is not valid; however, it is established with intention. Not upon a mere number. 'In: you divorce yourself' — this is a subdivision according to the mentioned schools: 'It necessitates three' according to the first school, because according to them the imperative necessitates generality, and all individuals of divorce are three, so it necessitates three. 'And it is probable for two and three according to al-Shafi'i' — because according to Imam al-Shafi'i, since it is probable for repetition, it bears the probability of two, and since it is probable for generality, it is probable for three. 'And according to us, i.e., the majority of Hanafi scholars as per the fourth school, it occurs upon one' — because it is a single individual, which is the least and certain. 'And with the intention of three' — because three is the totality of the individuals of divorce, and the totality as a whole is an artificial unit which is probable, so intending it with intention is valid. 'And the intention of two is not valid because it is a mere number' — because in the divorces of a free woman, two is a mere number, not a real unit nor an artificial unit. 'There is no indication from the name of the individual, i.e., the singular, upon a number.' Now with this issue, the area of difference has become clear. However, according to the third school, the area of difference in this issue is not apparent. The third school was that the imperative is not probable for repetition, but when it is conditional, it is probable for repetition. Then this issue was presented so that the area of difference would become apparent. For example, a man says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced.' According to the third school, it is fitting that here repetition of divorce is established by the repetition of the condition. He said 'it is fitting' because there is no transmission from these scholars on this issue; however, based on their principle and rule, it would necessitate repetition. So he said: 'And in: if you enter the house, you are divorced, then it is fitting that repetition is established according to the third school, not according to us.'
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the Hanafi position on whether the imperative (amr) indicates repetition (takrar) and generality (umoom). The author presents four schools of thought (madhaahib) on this issue: (1) some scholars hold that the absolute imperative necessitates both generality and repetition; (2) Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is only probable for both, meaning it may but does not necessarily indicate them; (3) some Hanafis hold that it does not indicate repetition unless it is conditional or qualified by a description; and (4) the majority of Hanafis hold that it indicates generality but not repetition. The passage then provides the linguistic reasoning for the fourth school: the imperative refers to a verbal noun (masdar), which is a single instance (fard); it indicates a single real occurrence. However, it can also refer to the totality of individuals (majmoo' al-afraad) as an artificial unit (wahid i'tibari), which is probable. Therefore, without intention (niyyah), it only applies to one; with intention, it can apply to the whole (e.g., three divorces). It cannot indicate a mere number like two. The passage also addresses the proof from the hadith of Hajj, where a companion asked whether the command for Hajj is for every year or once, showing that the imperative may be understood as indicating repetition. However, the Hanafi response is that the question was based on the repetitive nature of time and the analogy to other acts of worship, not on the imperative itself. This is a pure usul discussion; the key takeaway is that in the Hanafi school, the imperative by default indicates a single occurrence (not repetition) and generality (shumul) of all individuals of the commanded action, but not number beyond one.

Key Terms
أمر (amr): The imperative form of a verb, used to command an action.
تكرار (takrar): Repetition of the commanded action multiple times if the imperative is repeated or if it is conditional/qualified.
عموم (umoom): The imperative encompasses all individuals or types of the commanded action (e.g., every instance of striking or divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if a man says to his wife 'طلقی نفسك' without any intention, how many divorces occur?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) Depends on the condition

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the imperative (amr) indicates generality (umoom) of the act but not repetition (takrar); a single instance is the default, and intention can extend it to the totality as an artificial unit (e.g., three divorces), but not to a mere number (e.g., two).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Rule of Acts Without Rational Equivalent in Worship
Usul rule with proof and applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that acts of worship without rational equivalent cannot be compensated except by explicit text, and apply it to examples such as straightening postures in prayer and quality of property in zakat.

Core Idea
Acts of worship without rational equivalent require explicit text for compensation; otherwise, qada is impossible.

In Hanafi usul, acts of worship are tawqifiyya—their rulings come from revelation, not rational analogy. This lesson introduces a key rule: if an act of worship has no rational equivalent (mithl) that the mind can recognize, it cannot be compensated (qada) unless the Sharia explicitly commands compensation. We will explore the textual basis from the Quran, examples like the takbirs of tashriq and standing at Arafah, and practical applications such as straightening postures in prayer and the quality of zakat payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
Read the opening sentence: 'كل ما لا يعقل له مثل قربة لا يقضى إلا بنص'. This is the core rule. Understand that 'لا يعقل له مثل' means no rational equivalent exists, so compensation (qada) is not performed unless a specific nass (text) commands it.
The rule applies to acts of proximity (qurbat) to Allah.
2
Examine the Quranic Proof
The author cites verses on dhikr: 'واذكر ربك في نفسك تضرعا وخيفة دون الجهر من القول' and 'ادعوا ربكم تضرعا وخفية'. These establish that the default in remembrance is concealment, not loudness. From this, the loud takbirs of tashriq are an exception limited to a specific time, showing that the rule relies on textual specification.
The proof demonstrates that a practice (loud takbir) that might seem rational is actually restricted by text.
3
Apply to the Given Examples
The passage lists standing at Arafah, throwing pebbles, sacrifice, and takbirs of tashriq. For each, note that the compensation is only done because text (Quran or hadith) commands it. Without text, no qada. Reflect on why these acts cannot be analogized.
These are specific to time or place; their 'like' is not rationally deducible.
4
Analyze the Straightening Postures Case
The author discusses compensation for straightening postures (tadeel al-arkan) in prayer. The attribute (sifat) alone cannot be compensated because it does not stand alone. Compensating the entire prayer with the attribute would nullify the original valid prayer. The conclusion: only sin remains, no qada.
This illustrates the principle that attributes of acts are not independently compensable.
5
Apply to the Quality in Zakat Case
Similarly, if someone pays deficient dirhams instead of good quality in zakat, the attribute of quality cannot be made up alone. Compensating the dirhams themselves would invalidate the original payment. Thus, no qada for the attribute; sin remains unless the deficiency is made up through other means (e.g., giving additional dirhams).
The rule works the same across different areas of fiqh.

کل ما لا يعقل له مثل قربة یہ ایک ضابطہ پیش کر دیا کہ ہر وہ مامور میں کی مثل بطور قربت و عبادہ کے عقلاً نہیں ہے اور یہ عقل اس کی مثل فی القربت سمجھ سکتا ہے لا یقضی ایسے ماموں کی قضا نہیں ہوتی ۔ الا بنص مگر یہ کہ اس کی قضاء کے ساتھ نص دارد ہو جائے تو پھر قضا کرنا لازم ہو جائیگا کالوقوف بعرفة جیسے وقوف فی العرفات اور رمی الجمار نی منی اور اضحیہ فی ایام النحر وتكبيرات التشريق كیونکہ تکبیرات تشریق بطور جہر کے یہ قربت معروفہ فی الشرع نہیں ہے الانی الوقت المخصوص ورنہ تو بالعموم معروف عند الشرح اخفا ہے اور اصل بھی یہی اخفا ہے قال اللہ تعالیٰ واذکر ربك في نفسك تضرعا وخيفة دون الجهر من القول وقال تعالى ادعوا ربكم تضرعا وخفية یہ ہے اصل فی ذکر اللہ تعالیٰ فان كونها قربة تھی قربت ہوتا مخصوص بالزمان ہے ولا یقضای تعدیل الاركان نماز بغیر تعدیل ارکان کے ادا کی گئی ہے تو تعدیل ارکان کی قضا نہیں ہوئی کیونکہ صرف تعدیل ارکان کی نہ کوئی مثل ہے اور نہ اس میں نص واقع ہے لہذا تعدیل ارکان وحدہ کی قضا نہیں ہو سکتی اگر یہ حکم دیا جائے کہ خود نماز مع تعدیل ارکان قضا کی جائے تو صلوۃ اصل تھی اور تعدیل ارکان وصف و تابع تھی تو یہ ابطال الاصل للصلوة بالوصف اى ببطلان الوصف هو التعديل باطلاق یہ تو باطل ہے لان ابطال الاصل بواسطة بطلان الوصف نقض الاصول وقلب المعقول والوصف وحده لا يقوم بنفسه اور صرف وصف تعدیل وحدہ کی قضا نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ وحدہ یہ صرف صیف ہے جو قائم بنفسہ نہیں ہے لہذا صرف اس کی قضا بدون الموصوف ممکن نہیں ہے اور قضا الوصف مع الاصل یہ نقض اصول ہے کما مر فلم يبق الا الاثم والگناہ باقی رہیگا۔ و صفة الجودة اسی طرح صفہ جوہ کی بھی قضا نہیں ہوگی مسئلہ یوں ہے کہ کسی شخص نے ادائیگی زکوۃ کے سلسلہ میں بجائے دراہم جید کے دراهم زيوف ادا کر دئیے تو اس صفتہ جودة کی قضا نہیں کیونکہ یہ ایک وصف ہے جو قائم بنفہ نہیں لہذا اس صفت کی وحدھا قضاء نہیں ہو سکتی اگر اس کی قضا مع الدراهم ہو یعنی بصورت قضاء دراہم خود ادا کرے تو ابطال اصل لازم آئیگا بطلان وصف کی وجہ سے یہ خلاف اصول ہے
Everything for which there is no rational equivalent in acts of worship: this is a rule presented: every commanded act whose like in terms of proximity and worship is not rational, and the intellect cannot understand its equivalent in proximity, its compensation is not performed, except by text, i.e., unless a text exists with its compensation, then compensation becomes necessary, like standing at Arafah, like standing at Arafah, and throwing pebbles at Mina, and sacrifice during the days of sacrifice, and the takbirs of tashriq, because the takbirs of tashriq in the manner of loudness: this proximity is not well-known in the Sharia except in the specified time; otherwise, in general, it is well-known in the commentary that concealment is the origin, and the origin is concealment; Allah said: 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and fear and without loudness of speech' and He said: 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately'; this is the origin in the remembrance of Allah. So they are a proximity specific to time, and its compensation is not performed. Compensation of straightening the postures: a prayer was performed without straightening postures, then the compensation of straightening postures is not done, because there is no equivalent for the mere straightening of postures nor is there a text established for it; hence compensation of straightening postures alone cannot be performed. If it is ordered that the prayer itself with straightening postures be compensated, then the prayer was the original and straightening postures were a description and subordinate, then this is nullifying the origin for the prayer by the description, i.e., by invalidation of the description; that invalidation is invalid, because nullifying the origin by means of invalidation of the description is violation of principles and reversal of what is rational. And the description alone does not stand by itself. And the compensation of just the description of straightening alone cannot be performed because it is a description that does not stand by itself; therefore, its compensation without the described is not possible, and compensation of the description with the original is violation of principles as mentioned. So nothing remains except sin and guilt. And similarly, the attribute of quality: likewise, quality attribute will not be compensated. The issue is: a person gave deficient dirhams instead of good dirhams in the payment of zakat, then the compensation of this quality attribute is not made, because it is a description that does not stand by itself; therefore, compensation of this attribute alone cannot be performed. If its compensation is performed with the dirhams, i.e., by giving the dirhams themselves in compensation, then nullification of the original becomes necessary due to invalidation of the description; this is contrary to principles.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental usul rule in Hanafi fiqh: acts of worship that cannot be rationally analogized (i.e., no known rational equivalent) cannot be compensated (qada) unless there is explicit textual evidence (nass) requiring compensation. The author illustrates this with several examples: standing at Arafah, throwing pebbles, sacrifice during specified days, and the takbirs of tashriq (which are to be said loudly only at specific times, while the general principle in dhikr is concealment as per Quranic verses). The rule is then applied to two cases: compensation of the 'straightening of postures' (tadeel al-arkan) in prayer and compensation of the quality attribute (sifat al-jooda) in zakat. In both, merely compensating the attribute alone is impossible because an attribute cannot exist independently. Compensating the attribute along with the original (e.g., repeating the entire prayer with proper postures) would nullify the original act and violate principles. Hence, no qada is possible; only sin remains. The discussion emphasizes the Hanafi principle that acts of worship are tawqifiyya (restricted to revelation), and analogy (qiyas) or rational reasoning cannot establish obligations in worship without textual basis.

Key Terms
قربت (qurbat): An act of worship that draws one closer to Allah, often with specific rulings on compensation.
مثل (mithl): A rational equivalent that the mind can recognize as similar in terms of worship value.
قضاء (qada'): Making up an obligatory act that was missed or performed incorrectly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on compensating the attribute of quality (sifat al-jooda) in zakat when deficient dirhams were given?
A) It is wajib to make up the quality separately
B) It is not possible to compensate the quality alone because it is an attribute that cannot stand alone
C) The entire zakat must be paid again with good dirhams
D) There is no sin if the deficient dirhams were given intentionally

Key Takeaway
Acts of worship without rational equivalent cannot be compensated (qada) without explicit textual command; attributes of such acts also cannot be compensated alone, as this would violate principles of usul.
